wheels), filled them with gunpowder, put a huge stone on top, and
touched it off with a flame. If the stone was thrown against the walls of a
castle, it had such force that it shattered the wall.

不久之後士兵們就意識到這種混合物有多大用處。他們製造了大型臼炮（看起來很像裝在輪子上的長金屬鍋），裡面裝滿火藥，上面放一塊巨石，然後用火點燃。如果石頭被投向城堡的城牆，它的力量足以粉碎城牆。

These were the first cannons, and they brought about the end of
walled castles as walls were no longer a protection. Soon people made
thin tubes to shoot from, guns and rifles, and that caused the end of
shields and helmets and armour, and when shields and armour went the
knights went too. Once gunpowder came, the days of knights in armour
were over.

這些就是最早的大炮，它們終結了有城牆的城堡時代，因為城牆不再是一種保護。不久人們製造了用來射擊的細管——槍和步槍，這導致了盾牌、頭盔和盔甲的終結，而當盾牌和盔甲消失時，騎士也隨之消失了。火藥一出現，身穿盔甲的騎士時代就結束了。

In time, rifles, revolvers and machine guns appeared and made wars

隨著時間推移，步槍、左輪手槍和機關槍出現了，使戰爭

# 10. The Age of Discovery
# 10. 大發現時代

A new spirit was abroad in Europe, a spirit of curiosity; there was an
eagerness to find out things, to discover the unknown. The next great
step in discovering the unknown was made in the Iberian Peninsula, the
lands south of the Pyrenees, in Portugal and Spain. It happened while
England and France were still locked in the Hundred Years' War.

一種新的精神在歐洲蔓延——一種好奇的精神；人們渴望發現事物、探索未知。發現未知的下一個偉大步伐是在伊比利半島——Pyrenees 山脈以南的土地——Portugal 和 Spain 邁出的。這發生在英格蘭和法蘭西仍深陷百年戰爭之際。

Arabs had ruled large parts of Spain and Portugal for hundreds of
years, since the early 700s. When Arab power was at its height, it was like
a crescent moon stretching from the Pyrenees across North Africa to the
Holy Land. But by the year 1400, the Arabs had lost much ground in the
Iberian peninsula, only the south was still held by the Arabs, while in the
north there was a Christian kingdom, the Kingdom of Spain. In the west
there was another Christian kingdom, Portugal, and it was here that a
period of history began which is often known in history books as the Age
of Discovery.

阿拉伯人統治了 Spain 和 Portugal 的大部分地區數百年，從七世紀初開始。當阿拉伯勢力達到鼎盛時，它像一輪新月，從 Pyrenees 山脈橫跨北非直到聖地。但到了 1400 年，阿拉伯人在伊比利半島已經失去了大片土地，只有南部仍由阿拉伯人控制，而北部有一個基督教王國——Spain 王國。在西部還有另一個基督教王國 Portugal，正是在這裡，歷史上一段常被稱為「大發現時代」的時期開始了。

It was one man who started the Age of Discovery. He was Prince
Henry, the third son of the king of Portugal. His mother was an English
princess, and perhaps he inherited his life-long love for the sea from her.
Prince Henry was also a Knight Templar. The Knights Templar, who had
been crusader knights, possessed great wealth, which they used to start
new enterprises, for example mines for metal-ore. The greed of King
Philip IV of France and of Pope Clement V destroyed the Knights Templar
almost everywhere. However, in Portugal the Knights Templar survived
and changed their name to the Order of Christ. Prince Henry was the
Grand Master, the leader, of this Order of Christ, and as Grand Master he
continued the task of the Knights Templar. This task was to strengthen
Christianity, to weaken the power of the Arabs and the Ottoman Turks,
and even more important, to open people's minds to the wisdom of the
world.

開啟大發現時代的是一個人。他是 Portugal 國王的第三個兒子 Henry 王子。他的母親是一位英格蘭公主，也許他對大海的終生熱愛就是從她那裡繼承的。Henry 王子也是一名聖殿騎士。聖殿騎士團曾是十字軍騎士，擁有巨大的財富，他們用這些財富開創新事業，例如金屬礦場。法蘭西國王 Philip 四世和教宗 Clement 五世的貪婪幾乎在所有地方摧毀了聖殿騎士團。然而在 Portugal，聖殿騎士團倖存下來，並改名為基督騎士團（Order of Christ）。Henry 王子是這個基督騎士團的大團長——領袖，作為大團長，他繼續執行聖殿騎士團的使命。這個使命是加強基督教、削弱阿拉伯人和鄂圖曼突厥人的力量，更重要的是，打開人們的心靈去接受世界的智慧。

Already as a young man, Prince Henry became famous for his part in a
great land and sea battle in which the Portuguese took the port of
Ceuta, opposite Gibraltar, from the Arabs.

Henry 王子年輕時就因參加一場偉大的海陸戰役而聞名，在那場戰役中，葡萄牙人從阿拉伯人手中奪取了 Gibraltar 對面的 Ceuta 港。

But Prince Henry was not only a man of action, he was also a man of
thought and of new ideas. The trade in spices had the merchants of
Venice buying the spices from the Ottoman Turks. But the spices came
from much further east, from islands in the Far East. The Turks brought
the spices from India and became rich selling them to Venice. But if ships
from Portugal could reach India, they could bypass the Turks and make
Portugal rich.

但 Henry 王子不僅是一個行動派的人，他也是一個有思想、有新點子的人。在香料貿易中，Venice 的商人從鄂圖曼突厥人那裡購買香料。但香料來自更遠的東方——遠東的島嶼。突厥人從印度帶來香料，通過賣給 Venice 而致富。但如果 Portugal 的船隻能到達印度，他們就可以繞過突厥人，使 Portugal 富裕起來。

But how could ships from Portugal get to faraway India? Today it is
easy to say, 'Sail around Africa! But at the time of Prince Henry nobody
from Europe had ever sailed around Africa, no one even knew whether
one could sail around it, no one knew how big or how small Africa was.*
There was no knowledge, but there were strange tales.

但 Portugal 的船隻怎麼才能到達遙遠的印度呢？今天要說「繞非洲航行」很容易！但在 Henry 王子的時代，歐洲從來沒有人繞非洲航行過，甚至沒有人知道能不能繞過去，沒有人知道非洲到底有多大或多小。*沒有知識，但有奇怪的傳說。

If you look at the map you see a great bulge on the west coast of
Africa. Such a bulge is called a cape. This cape was only known from
hearsay, no European had seen it, but it was called Cape No because it
was said that no one could sail beyond it. The sun, they said, is so hot
there that all the water of the ocean boils away and ships get stuck in the
salt. Even the bravest sailors were scared at the mere thought of sailing
in this direction.

如果你看地圖，會看到非洲西海岸有一個大凸起。這樣的凸起叫做海角（cape）。這個海角只是道聽途說，沒有歐洲人親眼見過，但它被稱為「否定角」（Cape No），因為據說沒有人能航行越過它。他們說那裡的太陽如此炎熱，海水都被蒸乾了，船隻會卡在鹽裡。即使是最勇敢的水手，光想到要朝這個方向航行就嚇壞了。

Prince Henry wanted the Portuguese ships to sail along the African
coast and to find a way to India, but there was no map and nothing was
known of the way. Even if one ship by sheer luck found a way, what use
was that unless the captain of the ship could make a good, reliable map
for others to follow.

Henry 王子想讓葡萄牙的船隻沿著非洲海岸航行，找到一條通往印度的路，但沒有地圖，對航路一無所知。即使一艘船純靠運氣找到了路，除非船長能繪製一張可靠的地圖供他人跟隨，否則有什麼用呢。

So Prince Henry set up a school of navigation, the first of its kind in
the world. In this school experienced captains from many nations, mapmakers, even Arab sailors and scientists, instructed the Portuguese seamen how to use the instruments that show the latitude of a place, how
to use a compass and how to observe the sun and stars with instruments, astrolabes, and how to make maps.

於是 Henry 王子建立了一所航海學校，這是世界上第一所這樣的學校。在這所學校裡，來自許多國家的經驗豐富的船長、地圖繪製師，甚至阿拉伯水手和科學家，教導葡萄牙海員如何使用顯示地點緯度的儀器、如何使用指南針、如何用儀器和星盤觀測太陽和星星，以及如何繪製地圖。

Only when they had learned all of this did the Portuguese ships set
out. But they did not go straightaway around Africa. The first ships went
only a short distance, then they came back and reported what they had
seen. The next ships went a bit further and again came back with reports. And from these reports, maps were made to guide other ships.

只有當他們學會了所有這些之後，葡萄牙的船隻才出發。但他們並沒有直接繞行非洲。第一批船隻只走了一小段距離，然後就回來報告他們看到了什麼。下一批船走得更遠一些，同樣帶著報告回來。根據這些報告，繪製出地圖來引導其他船隻。

Prince Henry received all these reports and saw to it that proper maps
were made, but he stayed behind and supervised all this work. The Portuguese people laughed about him, calling him, 'Prince Henry, the Navigator who never goes to sea'. But later on they very respectfully called
him only 'Prince Henry the Navigator'.

Henry 王子接收所有這些報告，並確保繪製出適當的地圖，但他本人留在後方監督所有這些工作。葡萄牙人嘲笑他，稱他為「從不出海的航海家 Henry 王子」。但後來他們非常尊敬地只稱他為「航海家 Henry 王子」（Prince Henry the Navigator）。

One of the earliest ships Prince Henry sent out ran into a storm and
was blown westwards. They lost sight of all land and thought they would
die of hunger and thirst, but then they saw an island, which they named
Porto Santo. It was one of the islands now called the Canary Islands.
There were no people on it, but the climate was very pleasant.

Henry 王子派出的最早一批船中，有一艘遭遇暴風被吹向西方。他們失去了所有陸地的蹤影，以為會餓死渴死，但後來他們看見了一座島嶼，命名為 Porto Santo。它是現在稱為加那利群島的島嶼之一。島上沒有人，但氣候非常宜人。

The ships came safely back to Portugal and Prince Henry sent Portuguese peasants to settle on these beautiful islands. They took seeds
with them and soon their crop flourished. Unfortunately, the colonists
also took rabbits with them. As there were no wild animals on the islands
the rabbits multiplied and ate all the crops. The colonists had to leave.
Soon another island further west was discovered, a large island that was
called Madeira, which means 'wooded island'.

船隻安全返回 Portugal，Henry 王子派葡萄牙農民前往這些美麗的島嶼定居。他們帶了種子，很快莊稼就繁茂起來。不幸的是，殖民者還帶了兔子。由於島上沒有野生動物，兔子大量繁殖，把所有莊稼都吃光了。殖民者不得不離開。不久，更西邊發現了另一座島嶼，一座叫做 Madeira 的大島，意思是「多林之島」。

But these discoveries in the west were not Prince Henry's goal. He
wanted to find a way south. His ships went further and further south,
and from these longer and longer journeys along the coast of West
Africa, they began to bring back things of wonder. They brought back
ivory, which they had bought from the indigenous people for a few glass
beads, and, even more exciting, was gold dust. Soon people not only in
Portugal but all over Europe talked about strange faraway lands where
the rivers ran with gold

但這些西方的發現並非 Henry 王子的目標。他想找到一條向南的路。他的船隻越走越南，從沿著西非海岸越來越長的航程中，他們開始帶回令人驚歎的東西。他們帶回了象牙——用幾顆玻璃珠從當地人那裡買來的——更令人興奮的是金沙。很快不僅 Portugal 人，全歐洲的人都在談論那些河流裡流淌著黃金的遙遠奇異土地。

If it was not gold and not ivory, it was something else. The Portuguese
sailors, seeing the African people, assumed that these black people were
enemies of the Christian faith. They attacked peaceful tribes on the
coast, took prisoners and brought them home to be used as slaves. So
began one of the most shameful chapters in the history of white people:
the African slave trade.

如果不是黃金，不是象牙，那就是別的東西。葡萄牙水手看到非洲人時，假定這些黑人是基督教信仰的敵人。他們攻擊沿海的和平部落，抓走俘虜帶回國當奴隸使用。白人歷史上最恥辱的篇章之一就此開始：非洲奴隸貿易。

The ships went still further south, and some went up rivers into the
interior of Africa. Every month brought new knowledge, new discoveries.
But in 1460 Prince Henry suddenly fell ill and died; he did not live to see
his dreams come true.

船隻繼續向更南方航行，有些沿著河流深入非洲內陸。每個月都帶來新的知識、新的發現。但在 1460 年，Henry 王子突然生病去世；他未能活著看到自己的夢想成真。

The enthusiasm, the spirit of discovery that he had roused in the Portuguese sailors lived on, however. They reached the southernmost tip of
Africa, the Cape of Good Hope. They sailed around the Cape and, thirtyeight years after Prince Henry's death, the Portuguese captain Vasco da
Gama reached India.

然而，他在葡萄牙水手中激發的熱情和探索精神延續了下來。他們到達了非洲最南端——好望角（Cape of Good Hope）。他們繞過好望角，在 Henry 王子去世三十八年後，葡萄牙船長 Vasco da Gama 抵達了印度。

Within a few years the people of Europe began to buy their spices

短短幾年之內，歐洲人開始購買他們的香料

# 11. Columbus
# 11. Columbus

The news of the Portuguese discoveries, the news that ships had sailed
to unknown shores, spread all over Europe. People's minds were stirred
by these stories. In the old days people had some hazy idea that there
was, far away, a place called Africa or a place called India, but no one had
given much thought to what these faraway places looked like. Now it
was different. Now there came tales of great riches, of gold, precious
stones and ivory in these faraway lands, and everybody wanted to know
more about these strange places.

葡萄牙人發現新土地的消息——船隻已航行到未知海岸的消息——傳遍了整個歐洲。人們的思想被這些故事所激盪。在以前，人們對遙遠的地方有一些模糊的概念，知道某處有個叫非洲或叫印度的地方，但沒有人認真想過這些遙遠的地方是什麼樣子的。現在不同了。現在傳來了關於這些遙遠土地上巨大財富、黃金、寶石和象牙的故事，每個人都想更多地了解這些奇異的地方。

Yet people still had very odd ideas about Africa and Asia. One can still
see maps of that time that show Java inhabited by men and women with
tails. Another map shows how cotton grows in India, depicting a tree
that has little sheep hanging from the branches like fruit.

然而人們對非洲和亞洲仍然有非常奇怪的想法。至今仍可以看到那個時代的地圖，上面顯示 Java 島住著有尾巴的男女。另一幅地圖展示棉花在印度如何生長，描繪了一棵樹，樹枝上像果實一樣掛著小羊。

But these maps were very popular and people all over Europe wanted
maps to see what the world was like. Map-making became a new profession. All this interest in faraway lands and in maps had been sparked by
Prince Henry the Navigator and by the discoveries made by his ships.

但這些地圖非常受歡迎，全歐洲的人都想要地圖來看看世界是什麼樣子。製圖成為一種新的職業。對遙遠土地和地圖的所有這些興趣，都是航海家 Henry 王子和他的船隻所做的發現所點燃的。

Portugal's rivals, Venice and Genoa, were still engaged in the spice
trade. Genoa also engaged in another profitable trade. There was very
fine cloth made in Italy and the ships of Genoa carried this fine Italian
cloth through the Strait of Gibraltar and then to England. The English
paid good money for the cloth, and so Genoese ships frequently sailed
through the Strait of Gibraltar and past the coast of Portugal on their
way to England. It was not always a safe journey, because French ships
made a habit of attacking the ships of Genoa and robbing them of their
valuable cargo. There were regular sea-battles between French and Genoese ships.

Portugal 的競爭對手 Venice 和 Genoa 仍然從事香料貿易。Genoa 還從事另一項有利可圖的貿易。義大利生產非常精美的布料，Genoa 的船隻載著這些精美的義大利布料穿過 Gibraltar 海峽，然後運往英格蘭。英格蘭人為這些布料付出高價，因此 Genoa 的船隻經常穿過 Gibraltar 海峽、路過 Portugal 海岸前往英格蘭。這並不總是安全的旅程，因為法蘭西的船隻習慣性地攻擊 Genoa 的船隻，搶劫他們珍貴的貨物。法蘭西和 Genoa 船隻之間經常發生海戰。

In the year 1476, about fifty years after the death of Joan of Arc and
sixteen years after the death of Prince Henry, there was one such battle
between French and Genoese ships only a few miles from the coast of
Portugal. The ships from Genoa were sunk and many of the sailors
drowned. One young Genoese sailor, although badly wounded, caught
hold of a wooden plank in the water and managed to stay afloat. For
hours he drifted helplessly, but luck was with him and the waves flung
him ashore on the coast of Portugal. The name of this young Genoese
sailor was Christopher Columbus.

1476 年——Joan of Arc 去世大約五十年後、Henry 王子去世十六年後——在離 Portugal 海岸只有幾哩的地方，法蘭西和 Genoa 船隻之間發生了這樣一場戰鬥。Genoa 的船被擊沉，許多水手溺亡。一位年輕的 Genoa 水手雖然身受重傷，但在水中抓住了一塊木板，設法漂浮著。他無助地漂流了好幾個小時，但幸運眷顧了他，海浪把他沖上了 Portugal 的海岸。這位年輕的 Genoa 水手的名字叫 Christopher Columbus。

The Portuguese who found the shipwrecked sailor were kind
and
helpful. They looked after him and when Columbus had recovered he
made his way to Lisbon, the capital of Portugal. Lisbon was very different
from his home town of Genoa. Genoa's port was slowly dying, there was
less and less trade every year, but Lisbon was a flourishing port teeming
with vessels bringing spices from the East, gold dust, ivory and slaves
from Africa. Sailors from many nations thronged in the streets. Columbus
decided he would not go back to his own land, to Italy, he would stay in
this prosperous, lively port of Lisbon. He was good at drawing maps, and
so he settled down as a mapmaker. He did well in this trade and married
a Portuguese girl, the daughter of one of the captains who had discovered Madeira for Prince Henry.

發現這位遇難水手的葡萄牙人善良又樂於助人。他們照顧了他，當 Columbus 康復後，他來到了 Portugal 的首都 Lisbon。Lisbon 與他的家鄉 Genoa 非常不同。Genoa 的港口正在慢慢衰亡，每年的貿易越來越少，但 Lisbon 是一個繁榮的港口，擠滿了從東方帶來香料、從非洲帶來金沙、象牙和奴隸的船隻。來自許多國家的水手在街上熙來攘往。Columbus 決定不回義大利老家了，他要留在這個繁榮熱鬧的 Lisbon 港。他擅長繪製地圖，於是安頓下來當了一名製圖師。他在這一行做得很好，娶了一位葡萄牙女孩——她是曾為 Henry 王子發現 Madeira 島的一位船長的女兒。

As a mapmaker, Columbus studied every map he could get hold of
and one day he bought a map made by a fellow Italian, Paolo dal Pozzo
Toscanelli. Now this Toscanelli had read the books of a famous Italian
traveller, Marco Polo, who two hundred years earlier had travelled to
Cathay - what the Europeans called northern China - visiting the lands of
Kublai Khan. Marco Polo had travelled east to reach China and India. But
this Italian mapmaker, Toscanelli, two hundred years later, had a new
idea. If the earth was round, it should be possible to get to Asia, to China,
to India by sailing west: if you went on and on west, you were bound to
come to Asia in the end.

作為一名製圖師，Columbus 研究了他能找到的每一張地圖，有一天他買了一張同為義大利人的 Paolo dal Pozzo Toscanelli 繪製的地圖。這位 Toscanelli 讀過一位著名義大利旅行家 Marco Polo 的書，Marco Polo 在兩百年前曾旅行到 Cathay——歐洲人對中國北方的稱呼——訪問了 Kublai Khan 的領地。Marco Polo 是向東旅行到達中國和印度的。但這位義大利製圖師 Toscanelli 在兩百年後有了一個新想法。如果地球是圓的，應該可以通過向西航行到達亞洲、中國、印度：如果你一直向西走，最終必然會到達亞洲。

Now this is quite true. But this mapmaker, Toscanelli, made one great
mistake. He had no idea of the real size of the earth, he imagined it to be
much smaller than it really is. And so on his map the coast of China was
only three thousand miles west of Portugal. The real distance is about
ten thousand miles. But no one knew anything about the real distance at
that time.

這的確是對的。但這位製圖師 Toscanelli 犯了一個重大錯誤。他不知道地球的真實大小，他想像它比實際小得多。因此在他的地圖上，中國海岸只在 Portugal 以西三千哩處。真正的距離大約是一萬哩。但在那個時代，沒有人知道真實距離是多少。

When Columbus pored over that map of his fellow Italian mapmaker
he had a great idea. The Portuguese ships were trying to sail eastwards
round Africa to India for the spices. But this eastward journey was more
than ten thousand miles long, as they had to sail all around Africa. But if
the ships were to sail west across the Atlantic Ocean, it would be a journey of only three thousand miles - or so he thought. And he, Columbus,
would be the first to open a new way to Cathay, a way that went west,
across the Atlantic. Of course, Columbus himself was not rich enough to
buy a ship, to pay sailors and to buy food for the journey. His dream
could only come true if a king gave him ships and sailors to explore the
great ocean west of Europe.

當 Columbus 仔細研究那位義大利同鄉製圖師的地圖時，他有了一個偉大的想法。葡萄牙的船隻正試圖向東繞非洲航行到印度去取香料。但這條東行路線超過一萬哩，因為他們必須繞行整個非洲。但如果船隻向西橫渡大西洋，旅程只有三千哩——至少他是這麼認為的。而他 Columbus 將成為第一個開闢通往 Cathay 新航路的人——一條向西、橫渡大西洋的路。當然，Columbus 本人並不夠富有來購買船隻、支付水手薪資和購買旅途所需的食物。他的夢想只有在國王給予他船隻和水手去探索歐洲以西的大洋時才能實現。

This ocean, which we now call the Atlantic, was in those days called the
Sea of Darkness, for people believed that beyond the Canary Islands and
Madeira, there was an endless dark fog in which no ship could find its
way. When Columbus put his idea before the king of Portugal, he found
that the days of the adventurous Prince Henry were over. The king had
no wish to waste money or ships by sending them into the terrible Sea of
Darkness.

這片我們現在稱為大西洋的海洋，在那個年代被稱為黑暗之海，因為人們相信在加那利群島和 Madeira 之外，是一片無盡的黑暗濃霧，沒有船隻能在其中找到方向。當 Columbus 向 Portugal 國王提出他的想法時，他發現冒險的 Henry 王子的時代已經過去了。國王不想把錢或船隻浪費在送入可怕的黑暗之海上。

At this time Columbus' Portuguese wife died. There was nothing to
keep him in Portugal, and he decided to try his luck in the neighbouring
country of Spain. So Columbus and his young son left Portugal for Spain.
But Columbus' hopes that the Royal Court of Spain would be interested
in his idea were dashed. He came at the worst possible time.

此時 Columbus 的葡萄牙妻子去世了。沒有什麼能讓他留在 Portugal，他決定到鄰國 Spain 去碰碰運氣。於是 Columbus 帶著年幼的兒子離開 Portugal 前往 Spain。但 Columbus 希望 Spain 王室會對他的想法感興趣的期望落空了。他來的時機再糟糕不過。

At the time Spain was ruled by King Ferdinand and Queen Isabella,
and it was the Queen who made all the important decisions. Queen Isabella was the real ruler and she had set her heart on one great
ambition. The southern half of Spain was still ruled by Muslim Arabs, and
Queen Isabella, who was extremely religious, was determined to conquer the south of Spain and make it Christian. When Columbus came,
this war against the Muslims was still going on. Queen Isabella told
Columbus she would only consider his idea to sail westwards to Cathay
when Granada, the last Muslim stronghold, had fallen.

當時 Spain 由 Ferdinand 國王和 Isabella 女王統治，而女王才是做所有重大決策的人。Isabella 女王是真正的統治者，她一心一意追求一個偉大的目標。Spain 南半部仍由穆斯林阿拉伯人統治，極度虔誠的 Isabella 女王決心征服 Spain 南部並使之基督教化。Columbus 來的時候，這場對穆斯林的戰爭仍在進行中。Isabella 女王告訴 Columbus，她只有在最後一個穆斯林堡壘 Granada 陷落之後，才會考慮他向西航行到 Cathay 的想法。

So Columbus had to wait, and the waiting was not made easy for him.
The Spanish noblemen of the Court despised him as a commoner, and
the monks and priests who were the advisors of Queen Isabella were
against his new-fangled ideas. They said to him, 'If you sail your ships
around the edge of the world they will fall, you can never sail back again!
You must be a fool even to think of it!' It was a very trying time for
Columbus.

所以 Columbus 不得不等待，而等待對他來說並不容易。宮廷裡的 Spain 貴族鄙視他是一個平民，而擔任 Isabella 女王顧問的修士和神父則反對他的新奇想法。他們對他說：「如果你把船開到世界邊緣，它們會掉下去，你永遠無法再航行回來！你連想都想了就是個傻瓜！」對 Columbus 來說，這是一段非常艱難的時光。

At long last Granada was taken by Queen Isabella's troops; the last
Muslim stronghold in Europe had fallen and the whole of Spain was
under Isabella's rule. But the war had cost a great deal of money and Isabella could not afford to spend money on a wild adventure. The ships
sailing into the Sea of Darkness might never come back and the money

終於，Granada 被 Isabella 女王的軍隊攻下了；歐洲最後一個穆斯林堡壘陷落，整個 Spain 都在 Isabella 的統治之下。但這場戰爭花費了大量金錢，Isabella 無力在一場瘋狂的冒險上花錢。駛入黑暗之海的船隻可能永遠不會回來，而那些錢

# 12. The Year 1492
# 12. 一四九二年

It was not only Toscanelli's map, showing the coast of Asia only three
thousand miles west from Portugal (which is, of course, quite wrong)
that made Columbus think of sailing out into the Sea of Darkness. There
is a story that, as a young sailor, Columbus had once been to Iceland and
heard tales of a land in the west that the Vikings had found and which
they called Vinland. Columbus may have thought that Vinland was a part
of Asia but, in any case, it was a story about a land not too far away beyond the Sea of Darkness.

讓 Columbus 想到航入黑暗之海的，不僅是 Toscanelli 的地圖——那張顯示亞洲海岸只在 Portugal 以西三千哩處的地圖（當然這完全是錯的）。有一個故事說，Columbus 年輕當水手時曾去過 Iceland，聽到過維京人發現西方一塊土地的傳說，他們稱之為 Vinland。Columbus 可能認為 Vinland 是亞洲的一部分，但無論如何，這是一個關於黑暗之海彼端不太遙遠處有一塊陸地的故事。

Something else happened when he was still a mapmaker in Lisbon.
One day a boat with two dead bodies was washed ashore on the coast of
Portugal. These bodies were brown skinned. Columbus could only think
that they were Indian people, which was a mistake, but he was quite
right in thinking that this boat could not have drifted ten thousand miles,
it would have sunk long before reaching land. It could only have come a
much shorter distance.

還有一件事發生在他還在 Lisbon 當製圖師的時候。有一天，一艘載著兩具屍體的小船被沖上了 Portugal 的海岸。這些屍體有著棕色的皮膚。Columbus 只能想到他們是印度人——這是一個錯誤——但他認為這艘船不可能漂流了一萬哩，它早在到達陸地之前就會沉沒，這一點他是完全正確的。它只可能來自一個短得多的距離。

So Columbus was right in one thing: there was a coast only a few thousand miles away across the Sea of Darkness. His mistake - and it was the
mistake
of Toscanelli, really - was to think that the coast beyond the
ocean was Asia.

所以 Columbus 有一件事是對的：在黑暗之海對面只有幾千哩遠的地方確實有一片海岸。他的錯誤——其實真正是 Toscanelli 的錯誤——是認為大洋彼岸的海岸是亞洲。

But even making this mistake, Columbus was still wiser than the
'learned' monks of Queen Isabella who said if he sailed 'down the globe'
he could never sail 'up' it again. One day, Columbus got so impatient with
their silly arguments that he said to them, 'You tell me my voyage is not
possible. How do you know what is possible or not? Tell me, is it possible
to make an egg stand on this table?'

但即使犯了這個錯誤，Columbus 仍然比 Isabella 女王那些「博學的」修士們更有智慧——那些修士說如果他把船開到地球「下面」，就再也不可能開「上來」了。有一天，Columbus 對他們愚蠢的論點失去了耐心，對他們說：「你們告訴我，我的航行是不可能的。你們怎麼知道什麼是可能的、什麼是不可能的？告訴我，有沒有可能讓一顆雞蛋立在這張桌子上？」

'Of course not,' said the learned monks.

「當然不可能，」博學的修士們說。

Then Columbus had an egg brought in and he set it so hard on the
table that the shell broke and was flattened and the egg stood.

然後 Columbus 讓人拿來一顆雞蛋，他用力把它放在桌子上，蛋殼破裂壓平，雞蛋就立住了。

'It is possible, and so is my voyage, said Columbus.

「這是可能的，我的航行也是可能的。」Columbus 說。

In the end, his wish was fulfilled. He was given three ships to sail out
into the Sea of Darkness to find China and India and to bring back gold
and spices.

最終，他的願望實現了。他獲得了三艘船，駛入黑暗之海去尋找中國和印度，並帶回黃金和香料。

The Santa Maria and her companion vessels, the Pinta and the Niña,
were the best ships of that time. These kind of ships were called caravels.
They had three masts and three sets of sails (fore, main and mizzen) and
could sail close to the wind. So to set sail against the wind they could
tack, which means to go in a zig-zag course against the wind

Santa Maria 號和她的姊妹船 Pinta 號和 Niña 號是當時最好的船。這種船被稱為卡拉維爾帆船（caravels）。它們有三根桅桿和三組帆（前帆、主帆和後桅帆），可以逆風航行。為了逆風前進，它們可以走之字形航線來搶風行駛。

The caravels were a great improvement compared to earlier ships,
such as Viking dragon-ships. But compared with modern ships they were
very small. The Santa Maria, the largest, had room for only forty sailors,
and the other two vessels carried only twenty-five men each.

與早期的船隻（如維京龍船）相比，卡拉維爾帆船是一大進步。但與現代船隻相比，它們非常小。最大的 Santa Maria 號只能容納四十名水手，另外兩艘船各只載二十五人。

They were also very uncomfortable boats. The bodies of the caravels
were much rounder than modern ships and, being so small, they pitched
and tossed like washtubs on the waves. None of these wooden ships was
really watertight, and so the bottom was always filled with bilge-water,
which had a terrible stench and was a breeding ground for cockroaches.
Only the captain had a cabin and bunk (or bed) for himself; the crew had
to lie down below deck in the stench and among rats and cockroaches.
There was only one meal a day, consisting without change of tough, salted meat, dried peas and rock-hard ship's biscuits. Water was carried in
wooden kegs and after a few days at sea had a brackish taste.

它們也是非常不舒適的船。卡拉維爾帆船的船身比現代船隻圓得多，而且因為太小，在波浪上像洗衣盆一樣前後顛簸。這些木船沒有一艘是真正防水的，因此船底總是積滿了惡臭的艙底水，成為蟑螂的溫床。只有船長有自己的艙房和床鋪；船員不得不在甲板下的惡臭中、在老鼠和蟑螂之間躺下。每天只有一頓飯，內容千篇一律：又硬又鹹的醃肉、乾豌豆和硬得像石頭的船餅。水裝在木桶裡，在海上幾天後就帶有鹹味。

This was the kind of ship that set out on the most famous voyage in
the history of the West in August 1492. They were not fast ships. It took
them three weeks to reach the last known island in the Atlantic, Madeira,
which had been discovered by Prince Henry's sailors. They only stayed a
short while to take in fresh water, and then the real journey into the unknown began.

這就是 1492 年 8 月出發進行西方歷史上最著名航行的那種船。它們不是快船。它們花了三週才到達大西洋中最後一個已知的島嶼 Madeira——那是 Henry 王子的水手們發現的。他們只短暫停留補充淡水，然後進入未知的真正旅程就開始了。

The first days were perfect. A gentle wind swelled the sails and Columbus kept a steady course due west. But after a week, by the middle of
September, the ships
encountered
something that astonished and
frightened the sailors. For miles and miles as far as the eye could see the
water was covered with floating seaweed. The sailors, who had never
seen such an endless area of seaweed, feared the ships would get stuck
and would be unable to move backwards or forwards. They would remain there forever and die of hunger and thirst. The sailors fell to their
knees and prayed to God, but their fears were unfounded. The ships
sailed easily through the seaweed of the Sargasso Sea, as it is called.

最初幾天完美無比。微風鼓起了帆，Columbus 保持著正西方的穩定航向。但一週後，到了九月中旬，船隻遇到了令水手們驚訝和恐懼的東西。一望無際的水面上覆蓋著漂浮的海藻。水手們從未見過如此無邊無際的海藻區域，擔心船隻會卡住，既無法前進也無法後退。他們會永遠留在那裡，渴死餓死。水手們跪下向上帝祈禱，但他們的恐懼是沒有根據的。船隻輕鬆地穿過了這片所謂的 Sargasso 海的海藻。

After they had passed through the seaweed, there came other things
to worry the sailors. A strong wind blew the ships with great speed westwards, and every mile further and further west they went, the further
and further away they went from their homeland. Now the sailors feared
they would be blown to the rim of the world. But Columbus quietened
their fears and the sailors took new heart.

穿過海藻之後，又有其他事情讓水手們擔憂。一陣強風以極快的速度把船吹向西方，每向西多走一哩，他們就離家鄉更遠一哩。現在水手們害怕會被吹到世界的邊緣。但 Columbus 安撫了他們的恐懼，水手們重新鼓起了勇氣。

Three weeks passed. It was a whole month since they had last seen
land. Never before had they been so far away from land. Columbus himself was now uncertain: according to his reckoning they should have
reached Japan already, but on October 8 there was still no sight of land,
only the endless ocean.

三週過去了。他們已經整整一個月沒有見到陸地了。他們從未離陸地如此遙遠。Columbus 本人現在也不確定了：根據他的計算，他們應該已經到達日本了，但到了 10 月 8 日仍然看不到陸地，只有無盡的海洋。

Columbus may have been uncertain, but his sailors were desperate.
The captains of the Pinta and the Niña came on board the Santa Maria
and demanded the ships turn back. There was no sense in sailing into
the blue emptiness that stretched out before them on all sides. The
sailors were wild with fear and excitement. They cursed Columbus, calling him a murderer who led them to their deaths. Columbus pleaded
with the captains and with the crews. He asked them to sail westwards
for another three days, and if they should still see no land then they
would turn back and sail home to Spain. Grumbling and cursing the
sailors agreed.

Columbus 或許還不確定，但他的水手們已經絕望了。Pinta 號和 Niña 號的船長登上 Santa Maria 號，要求船隻掉頭。繼續駛入四面八方無盡的藍色虛空毫無意義。水手們又恐懼又激動。他們咒罵 Columbus，稱他為帶領他們走向死亡的兇手。Columbus 懇求船長們和船員們。他請求他們再向西航行三天，如果仍然看不到陸地，就掉頭返航回 Spain。水手們嘟嘟囔囔地咒罵著同意了。

Now it seemed
as if the winds wanted to help Columbus. A near
gale-force wind rose and drove the ships with great speed westwards.
Columbus hardly slept at all; day and night he stood on the deck waiting
for a glimpse of land. The first and second of the three days he had
agreed on passed. Then the third day came... and went. There was still
no land. Then in the middle of the night, on October 11, Columbus saw
the flicker of a flame far across the water and the news spread among
the sailors. At 2 am the moon rose and a great cry went out: 'Land ahoy,
land ahoy!'

現在似乎連風都想要幫助 Columbus。一陣接近強風等級的大風刮起，以極快的速度把船推向西方。Columbus 幾乎完全不睡覺；日日夜夜他站在甲板上等待看到陸地的一瞥。他同意的三天中，第一天和第二天過去了。然後第三天來了......又過去了。仍然沒有陸地。然後在 10 月 11 日的半夜，Columbus 看到遠處水面上有火光閃爍，消息在水手們之間傳開了。凌晨兩點月亮升起，一聲巨大的呼喊傳出：「看到陸地了，看到陸地了！」

In the light of the moon they saw a shimmering, white sand dune with
hills rising behind it. The sailors cried and laughed and prayed and sang.
No one slept that night.

在月光下，他們看到了一片閃爍的白色沙丘，背後是起伏的山丘。水手們又哭又笑，又祈禱又唱歌。那一夜無人入眠。

When daylight came, the sailors saw a crowd of people gathering on
the shore, shouting and talking excitedly among themselves.

天亮時，水手們看到一群人聚集在岸邊，興奮地彼此喊叫和交談。

Columbus was rowed ashore in a boat and his two captains followed
him. He was dressed in dark velvet, with purple silk stockings, carrying in
one hand a sword and in the other the royal banner of Spain. He was the
first European to set foot on the new land. The crowd of people who had
gathered stood and stared in wonder as these strange, white-skinned

Columbus 乘小船被划上岸，他的兩位船長跟在後面。他穿著深色天鵝絨，紫色絲襪，一手持劍，一手持 Spain 王室旗幟。他是第一個踏上這塊新土地的歐洲人。聚集的人群站著驚奇地注視著這些奇異的白膚

# 13. America
# 13. 美洲

The inhabitants of the island they had found were peaceful and gentle. It
did not even occur to them to fight the newcomers - quite the contrary,
they looked at them with awe and reverence. Having no clothes themselves, they touched the sailors' clothes again and again, wondering why
these
strangers wore extra skins over their own white skin. They
brought fruit as gifts, and smiled happily if they were given some glass
beads in return.

他們發現的這座島嶼上的居民和平而溫和。他們甚至想都沒想過要和新來者戰鬥——恰恰相反，他們以敬畏和崇敬的眼光看著他們。由於自己不穿衣服，他們一次又一次地觸摸水手們的衣服，好奇為什麼這些陌生人在自己的白色皮膚外面還穿著額外的「皮」。他們帶來水果作為禮物，如果得到一些玻璃珠作為回報，就會高興地微笑。

As Columbus and his sailors believed this island was off the coast of
India, they called the inhabitants 'Indians'. The name was, of course,
quite wrong as these people have nothing to do with the Indians of
India. Today they are referred to as Indigenous Americans, meaning they
are descended from the people who originally inhabited America before
Europeans arrived.

由於 Columbus 和他的水手們相信這座島嶼位於印度海岸附近，他們稱當地居民為「印地安人」（Indians）。這個名稱當然是完全錯誤的，因為這些人與印度的印度人毫無關係。今天他們被稱為美洲原住民（Indigenous Americans），意思是他們是歐洲人到達之前原本居住在美洲的人的後裔。

But Columbus and his men
were looking for spices, for precious
stones or for gold. As there was nothing of any value on the first island,
they soon left and discovered other islands not far away. They did find
one island where the inhabitants brought them some gold-like pebbles,
called 'nuggets'. The inhabitants
showed them a river where such
nuggets could be found amongst the pebbles. It was not much gold, but
at least Columbus had something to prove that his voyage had been
worthwhile.

但 Columbus 和他的人在尋找香料、寶石或黃金。由於第一座島嶼上沒有任何有價值的東西，他們很快就離開了，發現了附近的其他島嶼。他們確實發現了一座島嶼，那裡的居民帶給他們一些像黃金的鵝卵石，叫做「金塊」（nuggets）。居民們帶他們去看一條河，在那裡的鵝卵石之間可以找到這樣的金塊。黃金不多，但至少 Columbus 有了一些東西來證明他的航行是值得的。

He started on the return journey with the two smaller caravels; the
Santa Maria had run aground on an island and was not fit for a long journey. In March 1493, seven months after they had set out, Columbus arrived back in Spain. The reception that the king and queen of Spain gave
him was a triumph. Columbus walked at the front of a great procession,
and behind him marched Indigenous Americans carrying gold ornaments and parrots. When Columbus knelt down to kiss the queen's hand
he was invited to sit down beside her. He was appointed governor of the
new lands and any others he might still discover.

他帶著兩艘較小的卡拉維爾帆船踏上返程；Santa Maria 號在一座島嶼上擱淺了，不適合長途航行。1493 年 3 月，出發七個月後，Columbus 回到了 Spain。Spain 國王和女王給予他的接待是一場凱旋。Columbus 走在盛大遊行隊伍的最前面，他身後走著攜帶黃金飾品和鸚鵡的美洲原住民。當 Columbus 跪下親吻女王的手時，他被邀請坐在她身旁。他被任命為新領地以及他可能繼續發現的任何其他土地的總督。

Columbus soon sailed again, but this time with a large fleet of ships.
Many Spaniards came with him, not as sailors but as passengers - they
wanted to settle in the new lands as colonists.

Columbus 很快再次啟航，但這次帶著一支龐大的船隊。許多 Spain 人跟著他去，不是作為水手而是作為乘客——他們想作為殖民者到新土地定居。

Columbus put the colonists ashore on an island he had discovered on
his first journey, the island of Haiti. Then he sailed on in search of further

Columbus 讓殖民者在他第一次航行中發現的一座島嶼——Haiti 島——上岸。然後他繼續航行尋找更多

But from now on ill-luck followed him. The sailors and soldiers who
came with him started fights with the inhabitants of wherever they landed. There was bloodshed on every island. Ill and exhausted, Columbus
returned again to Spain only to find that Queen Isabella had died.

但從此以後，厄運便如影隨形。跟他來的水手和士兵在每一個登陸的地方都與當地居民發生衝突。每座島上都有流血事件。Columbus 病弱疲憊地再次返回 Spain，卻發現 Isabella 女王已經去世了。

King Ferdinand had
never cared for Columbus, and now that he no
longer had any use for him, he refused to pay him for his
services.
Columbus, who was too ill to work and earn money, was not even allowed to see the king. He could only write letters begging the king for
some money. In the end he was given a pittance, and Columbus died in
miserable poverty. But within a few years his discoveries made Spain the
richest country in the world.

Ferdinand 國王從來不關心 Columbus，現在他不再需要 Columbus 了，就拒絕支付他的報酬。Columbus 病得太重，無法工作賺錢，甚至不被允許面見國王。他只能寫信乞求國王給他一些錢。最終他得到了一筆微薄的錢，Columbus 在悲慘的貧困中死去。但幾年之內，他的發現使 Spain 成為世界上最富有的國家。

When Columbus died he did not know that he had come across a new
continent. But ten years after the death of Columbus, another Italian,
Amerigo Vespucci, visited the new land and wrote a book about what he
had seen. People were curious about faraway lands and the book was
widely read. Amerigo Vespucci was the first one to say that this land was
neither India nor China, it was a 'new world'. This new continent was
named after him: America.

Columbus 去世時並不知道自己發現了一個新大陸。但在 Columbus 去世十年後，另一位義大利人 Amerigo Vespucci 訪問了新大陸並寫了一本關於他所見所聞的書。人們對遙遠的土地充滿好奇，這本書被廣泛閱讀。Amerigo Vespucci 是第一個說這塊土地既不是印度也不是中國，而是一個「新世界」的人。這個新大陸以他的名字命名：America（美洲）。

It is interesting how many Italians come into this story. Marco Polo
told the world of Cathay; Toscanelli thought Cathay could be reached by
sailing west instead of east; Columbus did sail across the Sea of Darkness
and came upon a new continent, and Amerigo Vespucci recognised it
was a new continent. They were all Italians.

有趣的是這個故事中出現了多少義大利人。Marco Polo 告訴世界關於 Cathay 的事；Toscanelli 認為可以向西而非向東航行到達 Cathay；Columbus 確實橫渡了黑暗之海，發現了一個新大陸；而 Amerigo Vespucci 認識到它是一個新大陸。他們全都是義大利人。

However, it was not Italy but Spain that profited from discovering
America. More and more Spaniards went across, driven by their desire
for gold. Wherever they went they fought and enslaved the indigenous
population, who were worked hard and given little food. They were beaten and whipped by cruel masters and they died in their thousands. A
Spanish monk, Las Casas, was so upset by seeing them treated like this
that he wanted to help them. He went to the king of Spain and suggested that Africans would be much stronger and work better.

然而，從發現美洲中獲利的不是義大利而是 Spain。越來越多的 Spain 人在對黃金的渴望驅使下渡海而去。無論走到哪裡，他們都與原住民戰鬥並奴役他們，強迫他們做苦工卻只給很少的食物。他們被殘忍的主人毆打和鞭打，成千上萬的人死去。一位名叫 Las Casas 的 Spain 修士看到他們被如此對待而非常痛心，想要幫助他們。他去見 Spain 國王，建議說非洲人會更強壯、工作更有效率。

And so the shameful trade in slaves, which had begun in the time of
Prince Henry the Navigator, increased. Every year about a hundred thousand African people were captured on the west coast of Africa and
shipped to America to be sold as slaves.

於是，從航海家 Henry 王子時代開始的可恥奴隸貿易加劇了。每年大約有十萬非洲人在西非海岸被捕獲，運往美洲作為奴隸出售。

Las Casas, a monk, had helped the Indigenous Americans at the price
of bringing untold suffering to millions of African slaves whose descendants, African-Americans, live in America today.

修士 Las Casas 幫助了美洲原住民，代價卻是給數百萬非洲奴隸帶來了難以言喻的苦難——他們的後代，非裔美國人，今天仍生活在美洲。

When Columbus set out proudly in the Santa Maria on that Friday in
August 1492, he could not foresee what his voyage would bring to himself, to Spain, to Europe, to Africa and to the whole world.

當 Columbus 在 1492 年 8 月的那個星期五驕傲地乘坐 Santa Maria 號出發時，他無法預見這次航行會給他自己、給 Spain、給歐洲、給非洲以及全世界帶來什麼。

# 14. Francisco Pizarro
# 14. Francisco Pizarro

Columbus travelled to America in 1492, which is not so very long ago in
history. It was a time that already had many things in common with our
time. The Vikings, who were the first Europeans to reach America (they
called it Vinland), stopped going there when they found that it was already inhabited by people who resisted invasion.

Columbus 於 1492 年航行到美洲，在歷史上並不是很久以前的事。那個時代與我們的時代已經有許多共同之處。維京人是第一批到達美洲的歐洲人（他們稱之為 Vinland），當他們發現那裡已經有人居住且抵抗入侵時，便不再前往。

At the time of Marco Polo, two hundred years earlier, only he and his
family were keen to make long journeys into unknown regions. The
Polos were an exception; other people of their time never went further
than the Mediterranean Sea.

在 Marco Polo 的時代——兩百年前——只有他和他的家人熱衷於踏上前往未知地區的長途旅程。Polo 家族是個例外；那個時代的其他人從未走出過地中海以外。

But at the time of Columbus people had changed. It was such a great
change that from that time onwards life became quite different. Once it
became known that Columbus had not landed in Asia but in a new continent, America, thousands and thousands of people were curious about
this 'new world'. They were ready to set out and to try and seek their fortune in these distant lands.

但到了 Columbus 的時代，人們已經改變了。這是一個如此巨大的變化，從那時起生活變得截然不同。一旦人們知道 Columbus 登陸的不是亞洲而是一個新大陸——America，成千上萬的人對這個「新世界」充滿了好奇。他們準備好出發，試著在這些遙遠的土地上尋找自己的命運。

How different from the people of Marco Polo's time, who had laughed
about his stories but did not dream of travelling to Cathay themselves.
After Columbus, people were ready to cross the sea and penetrate deeper into the new continent. There was something that made these adventurers very keen to explore the new continent. When the Spaniards landed on the east coast of America they found some peaceful tribes and
some fearsome warriors, all of whom were hunters and nomads; they
had no cities, no treasures. But from these people the Spaniards heard
about great cities, far away in the west, where there were temples with
walls lined with gold.

與 Marco Polo 時代的人們多麼不同啊——那些人嘲笑他的故事，但自己做夢也沒想到要去 Cathay 旅行。Columbus 之後，人們準備好渡海深入新大陸。有一些東西讓這些冒險者非常渴望探索新大陸。當 Spain 人登陸美洲東海岸時，他們發現了一些和平的部落和一些令人畏懼的戰士，所有人都是獵人和游牧民族；他們沒有城市，沒有寶藏。但從這些人那裡，Spain 人聽說了遙遠西方的偉大城市——那裡的神廟牆壁鑲滿了黃金。

Men started to band together under a leader and journey through
jungles, across mountains and rivers, enduring hunger and thirst, wild
animals, indigenous tribes defending their territory from these new invaders, burning sun and mountain glaciers - all in the search for gold.
These men were called Conquistadors, which of course means conquerors. Hundreds of these Conquistadors perished on the way without
ever seeing a glimmer of gold, hundreds came back, half-starved, in rags
without having found anything. But some of them did succeed
and
found gold and treasures beyond their wildest dreams.

人們在一位領袖的帶領下聚集起來，穿越叢林、翻越山嶺和河流，忍受飢渴、野獸、保衛領土抵抗新入侵者的原住民部落、灼熱的太陽和高山冰川——一切都是為了尋找黃金。這些人被稱為征服者（Conquistadors），當然就是征服者的意思。數百名征服者在途中喪命，連一絲黃金的光芒都沒見到；數百人半飢半餓、衣衫襤褸地回來，什麼也沒找到。但其中一些人確實成功了，找到了超乎最狂野夢想的黃金和寶藏。

The most famous of these Conquistadors was a man called Francisco
Pizarro. He had all the best and the worst qualities of the Conquistadors.
He was courageous and utterly fearless, but he was also cruel and ruthless. Bloodshed meant nothing to him.

這些征服者中最著名的是一個叫 Francisco Pizarro 的人。他兼具征服者最好和最壞的品質。他勇敢無畏，但他也殘忍無情。流血對他來說毫無意義。

Pizarro began his career as a swineherd in Spain. There, on the dry,
high plateau of Spain he looked after other peoples' herds of pigs. He
never went to school, he never even learned to write his own name. But
he was strong, and he thought he could do better for himself as a soldier
in the Spanish army. So Pizarro became a soldier. After years of fighting
in Europe he was sent to America and there he took part in expeditions
against the indigenous tribes.

Pizarro 的職業生涯始於 Spain 的一個豬倌。在 Spain 乾燥的高原上，他替別人看豬。他從未上過學，甚至不會寫自己的名字。但他很強壯，他認為自己在 Spain 軍隊當兵能過得更好。於是 Pizarro 成了一名士兵。在歐洲打了多年仗後，他被派往美洲，在那裡參加了對原住民部落的遠征。

Being an uneducated man, Pizarro did not rise to a high rank in the
army, he did not make a great fortune. But when he was fifty years old
and had given up hope of further advancement and making a great fortune, he and his soldiers captured members of a local tribe who told
Pizarro of a great kingdom in a land called Peru: the kingdom of the
Incas. In this kingdom, so the tribesmen said, there were wonderful
cities and gold was as plentiful there as leaves in the forest.

作為一個沒受過教育的人，Pizarro 在軍隊中沒有升到高位，也沒有賺到大筆財富。但當他五十歲、已經放棄了進一步晉升和發大財的希望時，他和他的士兵俘獲了一個當地部落的成員，他們告訴 Pizarro 在一個叫 Peru 的地方有一個偉大的王國：印加帝國。據部落民們說，在這個王國裡有奇妙的城市，黃金像森林裡的樹葉一樣豐富。

Other Spaniards had heard these stories before but were daunted by
the hundreds of miles of dense,
trackless jungle and the enormous,
snow-covered mountain ranges that had to be crossed to get to Peru.
But Pizarro was not daunted or deterred; he was fired with the idea of
getting the gold of the Incas. He needed a band of men to come with
him, but
they needed
equipment, horses, arms, and Pizarro had no
money. So he persuaded another soldier, Almagro, who had money, to
go into partnership with him. Moreover, Pizarro managed to obtain a
promise from the king of Spain that he would become governor of any
land he conquered.

其他 Spain 人以前也聽過這些故事，但被通往 Peru 必須穿越的數百哩密不透風的無路叢林和巨大的雪山山脈嚇住了。但 Pizarro 沒有被嚇倒或勸退；他滿腦子都是要得到印加帝國的黃金。他需要一群人跟他一起去，但他們需要裝備、馬匹、武器，而 Pizarro 沒有錢。所以他說服了另一個有錢的士兵 Almagro 和他合夥。此外，Pizarro 還設法從 Spain 國王那裡獲得承諾，他將成為所征服的任何土地的總督。

And so, in the year 1529, 37 years after the discovery of America,
Pizarro set out with 180 men. They had two small cannons and three of
these men were armed with muskets, the first kind of rifle.

於是在 1529 年——美洲被發現三十七年後——Pizarro 帶著 180 人出發了。他們有兩門小型大炮，其中三人配備了火繩槍——最早的步槍。

Between this tiny force and their goal, the Kingdom of the Incas, there
stood the enormous mountain range of the Andes, with towering, icy
peaks and yawning precipices. On many parts of this journey the
Spaniards had to dismount and climb up the steep slopes leading their
horses.
Had they been attacked during that part of their journey, they
probably would have been wiped out in a few minutes, but they met no
enemies. Finally, they reached the crest of the mountains and made a
slow, dangerous descent. As they came down the slopes in the light of
the setting sun, they saw below them the flourishing fields and gardens,
the mighty palaces and glittering temple-towers of a great city. And,
right in their path, outside the city they saw thousands and thousands of
tents, the tents of a great army of thirty thousand Incas - nearly two
hundred Incas to every Spaniard.

在這支小部隊和他們的目標——印加帝國——之間，橫亙著巨大的 Andes 山脈，聳立的冰峰和深不見底的懸崖。在旅途的許多路段，Spain 人不得不下馬，牽著馬攀爬陡峭的山坡。如果他們在旅途的那段路程中遭到攻擊，可能幾分鐘內就會被全殲，但他們沒有遇到敵人。最後，他們到達了山脊頂部，緩慢而危險地下山。當他們在夕陽的光芒中沿山坡而下時，看到了下方繁盛的田野和花園、雄偉的宮殿和閃閃發光的神廟塔樓——一座偉大的城市。而就在他們的必經之路上，城市外面有成千上萬的帳篷——三萬印加大軍的帳篷——幾乎是每個 Spain 人對應近兩百名印加人。

Yet this great army of Incas showed no hostile intent. When the
Spaniards came riding down, their helmets glittering in the setting sun,
their banners streaming in the wind, the Incas made no move. Instead,
they looked at them with utter amazement. They had never seen white
men before, or men clad in armour or mounted on monsters - for they
had not seen horses either.

然而這支龐大的印加軍隊並未表現出敵意。當 Spain 人騎馬而下、頭盔在夕陽中閃閃發光、旗幟在風中飄揚時，印加人沒有任何動作。相反，他們以完全的驚訝注視著他們。他們從未見過白人、從未見過穿著盔甲的人、從未見過騎在怪物上的人——因為他們也從未見過馬。

The vast army of the Incas watched with awe and wonder while
Pizarro and his men found a little village outside the city that for some
reason had been deserted. In that little village, the Conquistadors made
their camp, and no one interfered.

印加大軍以敬畏和驚奇的眼神注視著，而 Pizarro 和他的人在城外找到了一個不知為何已被遺棄的小村莊。在那個小村莊裡，征服者們紮了營，沒有人干涉。

The next morning Pizarro sent two officers with an interpreter to the
king of the Incas in order to invite the king for a friendly visit. The two
officers were just as astonished by what they saw in the great city as the
Incas had been at the sight of the Spaniards. The Inca civilisation in Peru
is something that amazes even today. They built towers and palaces from
enormous blocks of stones, weighing sixteen to twenty tons, which had
been brought over great distances, and which had been cut so accurately that when they were put together, they fitted so exactly that you
could not push a piece of paper between them - no cement was needed.

第二天早上，Pizarro 派兩名軍官帶著翻譯去見印加國王，邀請國王進行一次友好的拜訪。這兩名軍官看到大城市中的景象同樣驚訝，就像印加人看到 Spain 人時一樣驚訝。Peru 的印加文明即使在今天也令人讚嘆。他們用重達十六到二十噸的巨大石塊建造塔樓和宮殿，這些石塊從很遠的地方運來，被切割得如此精確，當它們拼合在一起時，嚴絲合縫，連一張紙都塞不進去——完全不需要水泥。

Yet the Incas had neither rollers nor wheels for transport. They had
not discovered the wheel, neither had they horses nor oxen. They had
no iron to cut the stones either. The tools and weapons they had were
made from obsidian, a glassy volcanic stone.

然而印加人既沒有滾筒也沒有輪子來運輸。他們沒有發明車輪，也沒有馬匹和牛。他們也沒有鐵來切割石頭。他們擁有的工具和武器是用黑曜石——一種玻璃狀的火山岩——製成的。

Their cities were bigger than any in Europe at that time. The wide,
paved streets were so clean that the Spaniards' feet remained as clean as
their hands. These cities had things no European city had at that time:
pipes that brought fresh water from the mountains, underground sewers that took the dirt away. They had public hospitals and public baths
with hot-water systems. And the people of the cities never locked their
doors, for thieves or robbers did not exist among them.

他們的城市比當時歐洲的任何城市都大。寬闊的鋪砌街道如此乾淨，Spain 人走過後腳和手一樣乾淨。這些城市有當時歐洲城市所沒有的東西：從山上引來淡水的管道、排走污物的地下水道。他們有公立醫院和帶有熱水系統的公共浴場。城市裡的人從不鎖門，因為他們之中不存在小偷或強盜。

All the land and all the food grown on the land belonged to the king,
and the king's officers went around and distributed the food according
to the needs of every family. There was no buying or selling and no one
ever went hungry.

所有的土地和土地上種植的所有食物都屬於國王，國王的官員們四處巡視，根據每個家庭的需要分配食物。沒有買賣，也沒有人挨餓。

The king was regarded as a kind of god on earth - he was called the
son of the sun-god. The sun was the highest god of the Incas, and the
walls of the great temple of the sun were lined with gold an inch thick.
The temple of the moon was lined with silver.

國王被視為地上的一種神——他被稱為太陽神之子。太陽是印加人最高的神，太陽大神廟的牆壁鑲著一英寸厚的黃金。月亮神廟的牆壁則鑲著白銀。

It was a high civilisation, but it also had its dark side. At great festivals
the priests made human sacrifices - men and women were killed on the
altars in honour of their gods. But the men and women chosen to be
sacrificed never resisted: their life belonged to the king, the god on
earth, and if his priests wanted that life they could take it.

這是一個高度文明，但它也有陰暗面。在盛大的節慶中，祭司會進行人祭——男人和女人在祭壇上被殺死以尊崇他們的神靈。但被選中獻祭的男女從不反抗：他們的生命屬於國王——地上的神——如果他的祭司要他們的生命，他們可以取走。

And now this great and powerful king was invited by Francisco Pizarro,
the former swineherd, for a friendly visit. This visit was to be the end of
the mighty kingdom of the Incas.

而現在，這位偉大而強大的國王被 Francisco Pizarro——那個從前的豬倌——邀請進行一次友好的拜訪。這次拜訪將是強大的印加帝國的終結。
# 15. The Fall of the Incas
# 15. 印加帝國的覆滅

Pizarro had less than two hundred men while the king of the Incas had
an army of thirty thousand. Moreover, the king of the Incas had a personal bodyguard of two thousand. So it did not even occur to him that
this handful of white men would dare do anything against him.

Pizarro 的兵力不到兩百人，而印加國王擁有三萬大軍。不僅如此，印加國王還有兩千人的貼身護衛。因此他壓根不覺得這一小撮白人膽敢對他做出任何不軌之事。

The name of the Inca king was Atahualpa. He was curious to meet
these strange, white men with beards (the Incas did not grow beards)
and who dressed in hard metal and rode on monstrous animals. He was
curious and did not fear any harm from this little band. Atahualpa came
the next day, carried in a litter by the highest noblemen, covered with
plumes, golden ornaments and jewels. Behind the litter of the king came
thousands of his warriors with their obsidian spears.

印加國王名叫 Atahualpa。他很好奇想見見這些長著鬍子的奇怪白人（印加人不長鬍子），這些人穿著堅硬的金屬衣服，騎著巨大的怪獸。他充滿好奇，絲毫不覺得這一小群人能造成什麼威脅。Atahualpa 在第二天前來，由最高貴的貴族們抬著轎子，身上裝飾著羽毛、黃金飾品和寶石。國王的轎子後面跟著數千名手持黑曜石長矛的戰士。

Pizarro sent an interpreter and a monk to meet King Atahualpa. The
monk approached the king and made a long speech in which he explained the Christian religion, and he ended by telling the king he should
become a Christian.

Pizarro 派了一名翻譯和一名修士去見 Atahualpa 國王。修士走到國王面前，發表了一段長篇大論，解釋基督教的教義，最後告訴國王他應當皈依基督教。

King Atahualpa listened politely, but he could not make head nor tail
of what he heard about the Old Testament and the New Testament. He
could not make out what this man wanted of him, and so he shook his
head. This made the monk very angry. He held up a book, the Bible, and
shouted, 'It's all written in this book!'

Atahualpa 國王禮貌地聽著，但他完全聽不懂什麼舊約、什麼新約。他搞不清楚這個人到底想要他怎樣，於是搖了搖頭。這讓修士勃然大怒。他舉起一本書——聖經——大喊：「全都寫在這本書裡了！」

King Atahualpa had never before seen a book for the Incas had no
writing. He took the book in his hand and looked at it.

Atahualpa 國王從未見過書本，因為印加人沒有文字。他接過書，端詳了一番。

It tells you all,' yelled the monk.

「它會告訴你一切！」修士吼道。

Atahualpa put the book to his ear, then said: 'No, it does not tell me
anything, and he dropped it to the ground.

Atahualpa 把書湊到耳邊，然後說：「不，它什麼也沒告訴我。」說完便把書丟到了地上。

'Cursed heathen, shouted the monk. 'Is that how you treat the holy
word of God?'

「該死的異教徒！」修士大喊，「你就是這樣對待神聖的上帝之言的嗎？」

At that moment Pizarro, who had remained in the background, gave a
sign and with a crack of thunder his men fired their cannons into the
mass of Inca warriors, killing hundreds of them. At the same time, the
Conquistadors rode with their swords drawn into the Incas and cut them
down.

就在那一刻，一直待在後方的 Pizarro 發出了信號，他的手下在雷鳴般的巨響中向印加戰士們開砲，瞬間殺死了數百人。與此同時，征服者們拔出劍衝入印加人群中，一路砍殺。

The Incas were taken completely by surprise. King Atahualpa was torn
from his litter and taken prisoner. In half an hour his noblemen and four
thousand of his warriors were killed. Their obsidian weapons were
useless against iron swords, and
all the thousands of warriors were in
such terror that they fled. They had seen thunder and lightning; they
had seen their king, their god, roughly handled; it was like the end of the
world for them.

印加人完全措手不及。Atahualpa 國王被從轎子上拖下來，淪為階下囚。短短半小時內，他的貴族和四千名戰士被殺。他們的黑曜石武器在鐵劍面前毫無用處，數以千計的戰士驚恐萬分，四散奔逃。他們見到了雷電，他們見到自己的國王、自己的神被粗暴對待——對他們來說，這簡直是世界末日。

King Atahualpa was in a daze. Who were these
people who commanded thunder and lightning and who had
put his whole army to
flight? Now he feared for his life. He was willing to do anything the
strangers wanted if they would only let him go.

Atahualpa 國王陷入了恍惚。這些能操控雷電、讓他的整支大軍潰逃的人究竟是誰？他現在開始擔心自己的性命。只要這些陌生人放了他，他願意做任何事。

To his surprise, he was told that what they wanted was gold. For the
Incas, gold was not very valuable. They used it for decorating and ornaments; it was a beautiful metal, but not anything special. When Atahualpa saw the strangers were greedy for gold, he said to Pizarro, 'If you
spare my life and set me free, I will fill this room where I am kept prisoner with gold as high as my arms reach.'

讓他吃驚的是，他被告知這些人想要的是黃金。對印加人而言，黃金並不是什麼特別珍貴的東西。他們用黃金來裝飾，做成飾品；它是一種美麗的金屬，但並不稀罕。當 Atahualpa 看到這些陌生人對黃金如此貪婪時，他對 Pizarro 說：「如果你饒我一命、放我自由，我會用黃金填滿這間囚禁我的房間，堆到我雙手舉起所及的高度。」

Pizarro could hardly believe his ears. He promised to let Atahualpa go
as soon as the gold had been delivered. A messenger was sent to the
Incas telling them what their king wanted, and for days they came laden
with golden ornaments, cups, plates and statues, which they took off the
temple walls and from their wives.

Pizarro 簡直不敢相信自己的耳朵。他承諾一旦黃金送到，就放了 Atahualpa。使者被派去告知印加人他們國王的要求，接連好幾天，印加人帶著滿載的黃金飾品、杯盤、器皿和雕像前來，這些全是從神廟牆上和妻子們身上取下的。

The Spaniards thought they were in a dream when they saw the room
filling with the precious metal. As it would have been difficult to divide
the thousands of different golden objects fairly between them, the Incas
had to melt all the things down and mould them into gold bars of the
same size. So many beautiful works of art were destroyed.

西班牙人看著房間漸漸被貴重金屬填滿，覺得自己彷彿身在夢中。由於要公平分配數以千計各式各樣的黃金器物實在太困難，印加人不得不把所有東西熔化，鑄成大小一致的金條。無數精美的藝術品就這樣被毀掉了。

At long last the gold was all there, the room stacked to arms' height
with gold bars. When it was done, Pizarro gave orders to kill Atahualpa.
The king of the Incas was strangled in the marketplace before the eyes
of his people.

終於，黃金全部到齊，整間房間堆滿了金條，高至手臂所及。任務完成後，Pizarro 下令處死 Atahualpa。印加國王在市集廣場上，在他的子民面前被絞死了。

The Incas without their king were like a beehive without a queen: they
were completely lost and did not know what to do. The people who had
killed their god-like king must themselves be gods. They looked at them
with fear and awe and obeyed them blindly.

失去國王的印加人就像失去蜂后的蜂巢：他們徹底迷失，不知所措。殺死他們神一般國王的人，本身一定也是神。他們懷著恐懼和敬畏看著這些人，盲目地服從。

And so the former swineherd had become rich beyond his dreams. By
treachery and surprise he had destroyed a great kingdom and become
governor of the richest American colony, for that had been the promise
of the king of Spain. But the time came when Pizarro had to pay for his
deeds.

就這樣，這個曾經的養豬人變得富可敵國，超乎他最狂野的夢想。他靠著背叛和突襲摧毀了一個偉大的王國，成為最富庶的美洲殖民地的總督——這是西班牙國王給他的承諾。但報應終究到來了。

First there was trouble between Pizarro and his partner, Almagro.
Almagro was not satisfied with his share of the plunder and some Conquistadors sided with him. It came to a terrible battle between the
Spaniards, which Almagro lost. Pizarro, as governor, condemned him to
death and Almagro was hanged.

首先，Pizarro 和他的夥伴 Almagro 之間出現了糾紛。Almagro 對自己分到的掠奪品不滿，一些征服者站到了他那邊。西班牙人之間爆發了一場可怕的戰鬥，Almagro 落敗。身為總督的 Pizarro 判處他死刑，Almagro 被絞死了。

But Almagro had a son, Diego, who escaped and was kept hidden
from Pizarro's spies by some friends. Soon, more and more of the
Spaniards came to Diego to plot against Governor Pizarro because he
was as cruel to the Conquistadors who had fought for him as he was to
the Incas.

但 Almagro 有一個兒子 Diego，他逃了出去，在朋友們的幫助下躲過了 Pizarro 的密探。很快，越來越多的西班牙人來到 Diego 身邊密謀反對總督 Pizarro，因為他對曾為他征戰的征服者們同樣殘忍，一如他對待印加人。

One day, eighteen men, all sworn enemies of Pizarro, stormed into his
house shouting, 'Death to the tyrant!'

有一天，十八個人——全都是 Pizarro 的死敵——衝進他的宅邸，高喊：「暴君去死！」

Pizarro had some of his officers with him. They drew their swords and
fought back, but one by one they fell. Pizarro held out longer than the
others, but eventually, breathless and exhausted, he was killed when a
sword pierced his chest.

Pizarro 身邊有幾名軍官。他們拔劍應戰，但一個接一個倒下。Pizarro 比其他人堅持得更久，但最終，他氣喘吁吁、精疲力竭，一把劍刺穿了他的胸膛，結束了他的一生。

Another Conquistador, Hernán Cortés, also with a handful of men,
conquered the Kingdom of the Aztecs in Mexico. It, too, was a story of
murder and treachery, and of a vast treasure of gold. The gold of the
Conquistadors - of Pizarro, Cortés and others - went by the shipload to
Spain and made Spain the richest nation in Europe.

另一位征服者 Hernán Cortés 也率領一小隊人馬征服了 Mexico 的 Aztec 王國。那同樣是一段充滿謀殺與背叛的故事，還有大量的黃金寶藏。征服者們——Pizarro、Cortés 和其他人——掠奪的黃金一船一船地運往 Spain，使 Spain 成為歐洲最富有的國家。

Columbus had died in utter poverty, but his discovery made Spain
richer and more powerful than any other country.

Columbus 在赤貧中離世，但他的發現使 Spain 比任何其他國家都更富有、更強大。

# 16. Magellan
# 16. Magellan

The story of Conquistadors like Pizarro is certainly not one in which Europeans can take any pride. The Incas were in many ways more civilised
than the Conquistadors, and all that the Spaniards did was to destroy
this marvellous civilisation and turn the Incas into miserable and halfstarved slaves. But how was it possible that such a great nation as the
Incas, with an army of thirty thousand, could be shattered and enslaved
by a mere handful of two hundred?

像 Pizarro 這樣的征服者的故事，絕不是歐洲人能引以為傲的。在許多方面，印加人比征服者更加文明，而西班牙人所做的一切不過是摧毀這個了不起的文明，把印加人變成悲慘的、半飢半飽的奴隸。然而，擁有三萬大軍的印加帝國這樣一個偉大的民族，怎麼可能被區區兩百人擊潰、奴役呢？

It was not the weapons that gave the Spaniards victory; the two clumsy cannons took hours to be loaded. It was not the swords, for one man
with the best sword could not really win against hundreds of enemies
even if they had no arms at all. Instead there were certain cultural differences that governed how the individuals of the two societies behaved.

並不是武器讓西班牙人取勝——那兩門笨重的大砲裝填一次要好幾個小時。也不是劍——一個人即使拿著最好的劍，也不可能真正打贏數百個手無寸鐵的敵人。真正的原因在於文化差異，這些差異決定了兩個社會中個體的行為方式。

The Incas lived in a highly regulated society where their leaders told
them what to do and when to do it. The leaders distributed the food and
all necessities of life for everyone, and all decisions were made for the
people by a handful of priests and the king. Once the king was taken
prisoner the Incas fell into disarray. The warriors would not fight without
orders from the king, and once the king had been killed, there was in
their mind nothing to fight for. They accepted the murderers of the king
as their new masters.

印加人生活在一個高度管制的社會裡，他們的領袖告訴他們該做什麼、什麼時候做。領袖為所有人分配食物和一切生活必需品，所有的決定都由少數祭司和國王替人民做出。一旦國王被俘，印加人便陷入混亂。戰士們不會在沒有國王命令的情況下作戰，而國王一旦被殺，在他們心中就沒有什麼值得為之戰鬥的了。他們接受了殺害國王的人作為新的主人。

The Spaniards were different. They were hard men, selfish, greedy,
cruel, but every one of them was used to fending for himself, to fighting
for himself and to making his own decisions. It was this which helped
make two hundred adventurers masters of a kingdom of many millions
of Incas.

西班牙人則不同。他們是硬漢——自私、貪婪、殘忍，但每一個人都習慣自力更生，為自己而戰，自己做決定。正是這一點使得兩百名冒險者成為擁有數百萬人口的印加王國的主人。

Of course, this independence also has another side. It makes people
selfish and quarrelsome, and it did not take long before the Spaniards
fought each other. For us today the challenge is to learn to be self-reliant
and independent, but use our independence for each other and not
against each other.

當然，這種獨立性也有另一面。它使人自私好鬥，沒過多久，西班牙人就開始互相廝殺。對今天的我們來說，挑戰在於學會自立和獨立，但把我們的獨立用來彼此合作，而非彼此對抗。

Along with their plundered gold, the Spanish Conquistadors also
brought back reports of what they had seen on their journeys. As a result, Europeans learned more and more about the continent that they
had named America.

除了掠奪來的黃金，西班牙征服者們還帶回了他們在旅途中所見所聞的報告。因此，歐洲人對這片他們命名為 America 的大陸瞭解得越來越多。

One band of Conquistadors, starting on the east coast of America,
marched further and further west. After incredible hardships they came
upon another ocean. They were the first Europeans to see the great
ocean that lies on the other side of America, the Pacific Ocean. The leader of this band of Conquistadors, Balboa, had little reward for his discovery. On his return he quarrelled with a Spanish governor and was
hanged for rebellion. But his discovery of a great ocean west of America
inspired one of the greatest navigators and sailors in history.

一支征服者隊伍從 America 東岸出發，一路向西挺進。在經歷了難以想像的艱辛之後，他們發現了另一片大洋。他們是第一批看到 America 另一側那片遼闊大洋——太平洋——的歐洲人。這支隊伍的領袖 Balboa 卻沒有因為他的發現得到什麼好的回報。在回程途中，他與一位西班牙總督發生爭執，以叛亂罪被絞死。但他發現 America 以西有一片大洋，這激勵了歷史上最偉大的航海家之一。

This great sea captain, Ferdinand Magellan, was Portuguese, from the
country of Prince Henry the Navigator. For many years Magellan had
sailed on Portuguese ships around Africa to India for spices. The trade in
spices was still very profitable for Portugal.

這位偉大的船長 Ferdinand Magellan 是 Portugal 人，來自航海家 Prince Henry 的國度。多年來，Magellan 一直乘坐 Portugal 的船隻繞過 Africa 前往 India 運送香料。香料貿易仍然為 Portugal 帶來豐厚的利潤。

When Magellan heard that there was a great ocean west of America
he thought, 'We Portuguese are still sailing east around Africa to get to
India. But why should it not be possible to sail west, around America and
over the newly discovered ocean, and so get to India that way?'

當 Magellan 聽說 America 以西有一片大洋時，他心想：「我們 Portugal 人仍然是向東繞過 Africa 才到 India。但為什麼不能向西航行，繞過 America，穿越這片新發現的海洋，從那條路到達 India 呢？」

Columbus had thought he could reach India by sailing west, but he
had come upon America. Magellan wanted to reach India by sailing west
and going around America. The only difficulty was that so far no one
knew where America ended, where there was a cape around which you
could sail. But Magellan, who had sailed around the cape of Africa,
thought that America must have a similar cape.

Columbus 曾以為向西航行就能到達 India，但他卻碰上了 America。Magellan 想要向西航行繞過 America 來到達 India。唯一的困難是，至今無人知道 America 在哪裡結束，哪裡有一個可以繞行的海角。但曾經繞過 Africa 海角的 Magellan 認為，America 一定也有一個類似的海角。

Magellan first went with his idea to the king of Portugal, but what had
happened to Columbus also happened to him. His plans were met with a
cold refusal. And so Magellan did what Columbus had done and left Portugal and offered his plans to the king of Spain.

Magellan 首先帶著他的構想去找 Portugal 國王，但 Columbus 的遭遇再次重演——他的計畫遭到了冷冰冰的拒絕。於是 Magellan 做了和 Columbus 一樣的事：離開 Portugal，將他的計畫獻給 Spain 國王。

The Spanish king, Charles V, was shown a globe of the world that Magellan had had made and then painted. He showed King Charles on the
globe where, he thought, there was a cape in the south of America
around which one could sail (of course he only assumed there was such
a cape). Magellan explained to King Charles the advantage Spain would
have, with not only the gold of America but the profitable spice trade
with India as well.

西班牙國王 Charles V 看到了 Magellan 命人製作並繪製的一個地球儀。他在地球儀上向 Charles 國王指出他認為在 America 南端有一個可以繞行的海角（當然，他只是假設有這樣一個海角）。Magellan 向 Charles 國王解釋 Spain 將獲得的好處——不僅有 America 的黃金，還有與 India 之間利潤豐厚的香料貿易。

In the end, the Spanish king agreed to give him ships for exploring a
new sea route to India. But, as it turned out, they were not very good
ships because the king had no wish to risk much money on such an
uncertain venture. Magellan was given five ships, which were so old that
another sea captain said, 'I would not dare to sail on them to the Canary
Islands.' Yet it was these leaky tubs that made the first European voyage
around the world.

最終，西班牙國王同意給他船隻去探索一條通往 India 的新航路。但結果證明，這些船並不怎麼樣，因為國王不想在這麼不確定的冒險上投入太多錢。Magellan 得到了五艘船，這些船老舊到另一位船長說：「讓我坐這些船去 Canary Islands 我都不敢。」然而，就是這些漏水的破船完成了歐洲人的第一次環球航行。

Magellan set out on August 10, 1519, leaving behind a young wife and
a baby son. The most precious possession he carried with him was his
self-made globe. In the difficult days that lay ahead, Magellan would look
at his globe and draw strength and courage from the sight.

Magellan 於 1519 年 8 月 10 日啟航，留下年輕的妻子和年幼的兒子。他隨身攜帶最珍貴的物品就是他親手製作的地球儀。在前方艱困的日子裡，Magellan 會凝視他的地球儀，從中汲取力量和勇氣。

The first part of the journey, the crossing of the Atlantic to America,
was as bad as it could possibly be. The five caravels ran into heavy weather, there were thunderstorms and pouring rain, gale followed gale, and
the ships were tossed about like nutshells. Something that nearly frightened the sailors out of their wits was that little flames of light appeared
at night on the masts and ropes, running up and down and then disappearing. These lights, called St Elmo's Fire, are caused by electricity in the
air and are harmless, but the sailors of those times were in great fear of
them.

旅程的第一段——橫渡大西洋前往 America——糟糕到了極點。五艘帆船遭遇了惡劣的天氣，雷暴和傾盆大雨不斷，狂風一陣接著一陣，船隻像胡桃殼一樣被拋來拋去。還有一件幾乎把水手們嚇破膽的事：夜晚的桅杆和繩索上出現了小小的火焰，上下竄動，然後消失。這種光被稱為「St Elmo 之火」，是由空氣中的電造成的，其實無害，但那個時代的水手們對此十分恐懼。

After two months of storm-tossed seas, the five caravels reached the
coast of Brazil, where they had a short rest. Then they sailed further and
further south, following the coast in search of a cape where they could
turn west into the great ocean on the other side of America.

經過兩個月的風暴顛簸，五艘帆船抵達了 Brazil 海岸，在那裡短暫休息。然後他們繼續向南航行，沿著海岸尋找一個可以向西轉入 America 另一側大洋的海角。

Only one ship had tried to sail south before, but when a few sailors
had landed ashore to get fresh water, they had been captured by a warlike tribe who had killed them, roasted them and ate them. Terrified, the
remaining sailors had turned round and sailed back.

此前只有一艘船嘗試過南下，但當幾名水手上岸取淡水時，他們被一個好戰的部落俘虜，被殺死、烤熟並吃掉了。其餘的水手嚇壞了，掉頭原路返回。

Magellan and his caravels were now coming to a part of America,
Patagonia, of which little was known except tales of horror. It was also
drawing closer to winter in that part of the world and Magellan realised
he could not sail on into snowstorms and howling winter gales. They
would have to go ashore, spend the winter months on land and continue
the voyage in spring.

Magellan 和他的帆船隊現在來到了 America 的一個地區——Patagonia——人們對這裡幾乎一無所知，只有一些恐怖的傳說。而且那個地區的冬天正在逼近，Magellan 意識到他不可能在暴雪和呼嘯的冬季狂風中繼續航行。他們必須上岸，在陸地上度過冬季，等到春天再繼續航程。

# 17. Crossing the Pacific Ocean
# 17. 橫渡太平洋

The king of Spain had not been very generous with the ships he had
given Magellan, and as the money he had given to Magellan to pay his
sailors was also not very much, the crew Magellan found for his ships
were unruly and unreliable. They were a mixture of Spanish, Portuguese,
Italian and French sailors. There was even an Englishman.

西班牙國王給 Magellan 的船算不上大方，而他給 Magellan 用來支付水手薪資的經費也不多，因此 Magellan 找來的船員都是些桀驁不馴、不太可靠的人。他們是由西班牙、Portugal、Italy 和 France 水手混合組成的隊伍，其中甚至有一個英國人。

When the winter storms came, Magellan found a safe harbour on the
coast to anchor the ships. It was a bleak coast consisting of grey rocks
with little patches of grass here and there, and nothing that could be
used for food. Magellan knew they would have to stay in the harbour for
four to five months and, as the only food was what they had on the ships,
all men had to get by on short rations to make their store last.

當冬季風暴來臨時，Magellan 在海岸找到了一個安全的港灣停泊船隻。那是一片荒涼的海岸，灰色的岩石上零星長著幾簇草，沒有任何可以充作食物的東西。Magellan 知道他們必須在港灣待上四到五個月，而唯一的食物就是船上的存糧，所有人都必須靠減量配給來撐過這段時間。

But the sailors had no wish to spend months in this desolate spot with
gnawing hunger. The captain and the crew of a Spanish ship mutinied,
capturing another ship and breaking open the stores to feast on the
ship's biscuits and wine.

但水手們可不想在這個荒涼的地方忍飢挨餓好幾個月。一艘西班牙船的船長和船員發動了叛變，奪取了另一艘船，還撬開了儲藏室，大吃船上的餅乾和葡萄酒。

Magellan sent messengers to the mutinous captain with the order to
report to him. The messengers had swords hidden under their cloaks
and when the captain refused, they drew their swords and killed him.
After this the other mutineers surrendered. Magellan had shown that he
was master of his fleet.

Magellan 派使者去見叛變的船長，命令他來報到。使者們的斗篷下藏著劍，當船長拒絕服從時，他們拔劍將他殺了。此後，其他叛變者紛紛投降。Magellan 證明了他才是艦隊的主人。

The crews had already been two months on this desolate shore where
no sign of life could be seen, when someone appeared. In the accounts
they gave when they returned, the sailors said that this man was so tall
that even the tallest of the Europeans reached only to his waist. According to them, the giant was quite friendly, as were the other men of his
tribe who soon joined him. The tall men showed by signs their great surprise that people as small as these sailors could build such big ships. The
sailors, too, were surprised when they invited tall men to a meal. Each of
the men ate a whole large basketful of ship's biscuits after which each
drank a whole bucketful of water. Magellan gave one giant a little mirror
as a present. He was so frightened at seeing his own face in the glass
that he fell over backwards and knocked down four sailors who happened to be standing behind him.

船員們已經在這片荒涼的海岸上待了兩個月，周圍看不到任何生命跡象，這時有人出現了。水手們回國後的敘述中說，這個人高大到即使最高的歐洲人也只到他的腰部。據他們說，這位巨人相當友善，他部落裡的其他人很快也來了，同樣友好。這些高大的人用手勢表達了極大的驚訝——像水手們這麼小的人竟然能造出這麼大的船。水手們也感到驚訝：他們邀請這些高大的人一起用餐，每個人吃了整整一大籃船上餅乾，然後每人喝了整整一桶水。Magellan 送了一面小鏡子給其中一個巨人。當他在鏡中看到自己的臉時，嚇得整個人往後倒，撞倒了身後站著的四名水手。

Other European explorers who came after Magellan also reported encounters with very tall people, but it is thought that the original
description of those Spanish sailors of giants twice the size of an average
person was an exaggeration told for dramatic effect.

Magellan 之後來到這裡的其他歐洲探險家也報告遇到了非常高大的人，但一般認為，最初那些西班牙水手描述的身高兩倍於常人的巨人是誇大其詞，為了增添戲劇效果。

Unfortunately many of these indigenous people later died of diseases
brought by the Europeans.

不幸的是，這些原住民中有許多人後來死於歐洲人帶來的疾病。

At last, after six months, the weather improved and Magellan's fleet
went on its way further south. After a week's sailing they saw the coast
broken by channels running westwards. Perhaps by sailing through
these channels and picking their way between the rocks, they might
come out on the other side of America.

終於，六個月之後，天氣好轉，Magellan 的艦隊繼續向南航行。航行一週後，他們看到海岸被幾條向西延伸的水道所切割。也許穿過這些水道，在岩石之間小心行進，他們就能到達 America 的另一邊。

Rain was pouring down, there was dense fog, and so Magellan sent
one of his ships, with a Spanish captain, ahead of the others to see if
there was a safe passage between the rocks and islands. But the treacherous captain used the dense fog to turn round and sail back to Spain.
When the ship did not return Magellan thought it had run against a rock,
and he spent days looking for survivors. He did not know that this ship
had deserted him.

大雨傾盆，濃霧瀰漫，Magellan 派了一艘船——由一位西班牙船長率領——先行探路，看看岩石和島嶼之間是否有安全的航道。但這個背信棄義的船長利用濃霧掉轉船頭，逃回了 Spain。當那艘船遲遲不歸時，Magellan 以為它撞上了礁石，花了好幾天尋找倖存者。他不知道這艘船已經拋棄了他。

No trace was found and now the remaining ships wound their way
cautiously between rocks and reefs and steep cliffs. Once they saw at
night the flame of a campfire in the distance, so they called the land Tierra del Fuego, meaning Land of Fire, which is what it is still called today.

什麼蹤跡也沒找到，剩下的船隻現在小心翼翼地在岩石、暗礁和陡峭的懸崖之間蜿蜒前行。有一次，他們在夜晚看到遠處有營火的光芒，於是將這片土地命名為 Tierra del Fuego，意思是「火之地」，至今仍沿用這個名字。

What made navigation between rocks and cliffs even more difficult
were the storms that constantly buffeted the ships. But after five weeks
they came out of the channels and onto
a wide, calm, open sea. The
sailors were overjoyed and they called this calm sea the Pacific Ocean,
meaning the peaceful ocean. The strait through which they had come is
called the Strait of Magellan after the navigator who was the first European to sail through it.

讓岩石和懸崖之間的航行更加困難的，是不斷侵襲船隻的暴風雨。但五個星期後，他們終於駛出水道，進入了一片寬闊、平靜、開闊的海面。水手們欣喜若狂，他們把這片平靜的大海稱為太平洋（Pacific Ocean），意思是「和平的海洋」。他們穿越的那條海峽以這位第一個通過它的歐洲航海家命名，叫做 Magellan 海峽。

But Magellan was soon to find out that the calm waters of the Pacific
would bring worse suffering than the stormy seas from which they had
come. He set a course north-west, in the hope that they would soon
reach an island where they could replenish their food, which was getting
dangerously low. He could not guess how big the Pacific Ocean really is.

但 Magellan 很快就會發現，太平洋平靜的水面帶來的苦難比他們來時經歷的暴風雨海域更加嚴酷。他設定了向西北方的航線，希望很快就能抵達一座島嶼，補充已經危險地接近耗盡的食物。他無法想像太平洋究竟有多大。

After they had left the strait, the ships sailed for fourteen weeks without
seeing any sign of land at all. The lack of food became desperate. What
remained of the ship's biscuits was only dust mixed with worms, and the
only water they had left was yellow and foul. Things became so bad that
the sailors cut leather from the mast covering. The sun had dried it as
hard as wood, so the sailors had to hang these strips of leather in the sea
for five days before they became a little softer. Then they roasted and
ate them. For a rat, men were willing to pay a gold coin, but there were
not enough rats on the boats.

離開海峽之後，船隻航行了整整十四個星期，連一絲陸地的影子都看不到。食物匱乏到了絕望的地步。剩下的船上餅乾只有混著蟲子的粉末，僅存的水又黃又臭。情況糟糕到水手們不得不從桅杆的皮革包覆上割下皮來吃。太陽已經把皮革曬得像木頭一樣硬，水手們只好把這些皮革條浸在海裡五天，讓它們稍微軟一點，然後烤來吃。一隻老鼠可以賣到一枚金幣的價錢，但船上的老鼠根本不夠。

Diseases broke out and nineteen men died. Meanwhile, Magellan sat
in his cabin and looked at his precious globe: it was the only thing that
still gave him hope.

疫病爆發，十九人死亡。在此期間，Magellan 坐在他的船艙裡凝視著他那珍貴的地球儀——那是唯一還能給他希望的東西。

At last, after three and a half months, they came to an island. But
there was an unpleasant surprise in store for them: a boatful of people
appeared who climbed aboard the caravels and immediately began to
steal everything they could lay their hands on. The sailors charged at
them with their swords and drove them off. The people jumped overboard and swam ashore, leaving their boat behind. In the boat, Magellan's men found coconuts, fresh fruit, sugarcane and fresh water. This
boat saved their lives.

終於，三個半月後，他們來到了一座島嶼。但一個不愉快的驚喜等著他們：一船人出現了，爬上帆船，立刻開始偷拿所有他們能拿到的東西。水手們拔劍衝向他們，將他們趕走。那些人跳入海中游上岸去，留下了他們的船。在那艘船裡，Magellan 的人發現了椰子、新鮮水果、甘蔗和淡水。這艘船救了他們的命。

But the hardest blow for the expedition came when they reached the
next group of islands, which Magellan called the Philippines, in honour
of the son of the king of Spain. The chief of one of these islands received
Magellan very well. He made a trade agreement with him and even became a Christian. But this friendly chief was at war with the chief of another island, and Magellan offered to help his friend.

但遠征隊最沉重的打擊來自他們抵達下一組島嶼的時候。Magellan 將這些島嶼命名為 Philippines，以紀念西班牙國王的兒子。其中一座島嶼的酋長熱情地接待了 Magellan，與他簽訂了貿易協定，甚至皈依了基督教。但這位友善的酋長正與另一座島嶼的酋長交戰，Magellan 主動提出幫助他的朋友。

He went with a party of his sailors in three rowing boats to the enemy
island. The sailors were armed with muskets and Magellan expected
these weapons would drive their enemies to flight. They waded ashore,
firing their guns, but the island's inhabitants were not afraid. They came
in their hundreds and Magellan gave orders to retreat to the boats. Magellan was halfway to the boat when one of the warriors struck him with a
spear. Magellan turned round and fought back, but a second man struck
at Magellan's legs and wounded him. Magellan fell down into the shallow
water where the warriors fell upon him and killed him. The great navigator died before he could complete the task he had set himself. It was
now up to his captains to complete the voyage.

他帶著一隊水手乘三艘划船前往敵對的島嶼。水手們配備了火槍，Magellan 預期這些武器會讓敵人望風而逃。他們涉水上岸，開槍射擊，但島上的居民絲毫不懼。他們成群結隊地湧來，Magellan 下令撤退回船。Magellan 走到半路，一名戰士用長矛刺中了他。Magellan 轉身反擊，但另一個人砍中了 Magellan 的腿，傷了他。Magellan 倒在了淺水中，戰士們蜂擁而上，將他殺死。這位偉大的航海家在完成他為自己設定的任務之前便已殞命。現在，要靠他的船長們來完成這趟航行了。

But their troubles were not over. The friendly king now came to the
conclusion that the Christian god was not very powerful. He turned
against the sailors who had thought he was their friend. In the end, one

但他們的麻煩並沒有結束。那位友善的國王此時得出結論：基督教的神似乎沒那麼厲害。他轉而對付那些以為他是朋友的水手們。最終，只有一

# 18. The Renaissance
# 18. 文藝復興

The expeditions
of the Conquistadors and Magellan's great voyage
around the world were both signs that a new age was coming. But while
the people of Europe began to explore the world to the west, the Ottoman Turks rose up in the east.

征服者的遠征和 Magellan 偉大的環球航行，都是一個新時代即將來臨的標誌。但就在歐洲人開始探索西方世界的同時，Ottoman Turk 在東方崛起了。

During the time of the Crusaders, the Turks had never invaded Europe. There was one thing that kept them out of Europe and that was
Constantinople.

在十字軍時代，Turk 人從未入侵過歐洲。有一樣東西把他們擋在歐洲門外，那就是 Constantinople。

The city, named after the Roman Emperor Constantine the Great, was
situated on the narrow strait between the Mediterranean and the Black
Sea, and was like a strong gate stopping the Turks from advancing into
Europe. Ever since the Crusades, they had tried repeatedly to take Constantinople, but had failed.

這座以羅馬皇帝 Constantine 大帝命名的城市，坐落在地中海與黑海之間的狹窄海峽上，猶如一道堅固的大門，阻擋著 Turk 人向歐洲推進。自十字軍東征以來，他們多次嘗試攻占 Constantinople，但都失敗了。

Although Constantinople was a Christian city, its people did not belong to the same church as those of Western Europe, who belonged to
the Church of Rome with the Pope as the highest authority. The people
of Constantinople did not recognise the Pope as an authority at all; the
Emperor of Constantinople was at the same time head of the Eastern
Church. Because of this there was no great friendship between Western
Europe and Constantinople.

雖然 Constantinople 是一座基督教城市，但它的人民並不屬於與西歐相同的教會。西歐人屬於以教宗為最高權威的羅馬教會，而 Constantinople 的人民根本不承認教宗的權威；Constantinople 的皇帝同時也是東方教會的領袖。因此，西歐與 Constantinople 之間並沒有深厚的友誼。

Around the time Columbus was born, about 1451, the Sultan of the
Ottoman Empire, Mehmed II, swore that he would not rest until the crescent moon of Islam flew over Constantinople. He led a vast army of three
hundred thousand Turks against the city and at the same time a Turkish
fleet attacked from the sea. The emperor of Constantinople, who was
called Constantine like the first emperor, had only fifty thousand men to
defend the city.

大約在 Columbus 出生的時候，也就是 1451 年左右，Ottoman 帝國的蘇丹 Mehmed II 發誓不攻下 Constantinople、不讓伊斯蘭的新月旗飄揚在城上，他絕不罷休。他率領三十萬大軍進攻這座城市，同時 Turk 艦隊從海上發動攻擊。Constantinople 的皇帝——與第一位皇帝同名 Constantine——只有五萬人可以守城。

In despair he asked for help from the Christians in Europe, sending
messengers to the Pope in Rome begging for help: perhaps a new crusade could save Constantinople. But the Pope was not interested in people who called themselves Christians without accepting him as head of
their church. People who did not look up to the Pope were called
'heretics' and to be a heretic was considered worse than not being a
Christian at all. So the Pope and the Christians of Europe simply ignored
the desperate pleas for help that came from Constantinople.

他在絕望中向歐洲的基督徒求助，派使者到羅馬向教宗求救：也許一場新的十字軍東征可以拯救 Constantinople。但教宗對那些自稱基督徒卻不承認他為教會領袖的人沒什麼興趣。不尊奉教宗的人被稱為「異端」，而身為異端被認為比根本不是基督徒還要糟糕。於是教宗和歐洲的基督徒們對 Constantinople 傳來的絕望求援置之不理。

When Constantine realised that he could not expect any help from the
Pope, he called his people together and said: 'It is the duty of every man
to give his life in the defence of his family, his country and his religion.
You are now called upon to fight and give your life for all three Then he
added: 'If I have ever hurt or offended any one of you, I am asking your
forgiveness so that we shall fight and die as friends!

當 Constantine 意識到不可能從教宗那裡得到任何援助時，他召集了他的人民，說道：「每個人都有義務為保衛自己的家庭、國家和信仰獻出生命。你們現在被召喚為這三者而戰、而獻身。」然後他補充道：「如果我曾經傷害或冒犯過你們任何人，我請求你們的原諒，好讓我們以朋友的身份戰鬥和赴死！」

Constantine could have saved his life and the life of his family, for the
Ottoman Turks offered to let him and his family go if he surrendered the
city without a fight. But he refused to save himself and leave his people,
who he believed should at least have the chance to fight. And so for
three weeks the Turks threw their whole might against Constantinople:
their cannons smashed walls, houses and whole streets. But the people
of Constantinople, the merchants, shopkeepers - men who had never
carried arms - now fought with the courage of veteran soldiers. But they
were too heavily outnumbered, and after three weeks the Turks broke
through and poured into the city. They plundered and burnt houses,
they killed Emperor Constantine and sold his family as slaves. The crescent moon of Islam rose over the churches of Constantinople and they
were turned into mosques that remain to this day.

Constantine 本可以保全自己和家人的性命，因為 Ottoman Turk 提出只要他不戰而降，就放他和家人離去。但他拒絕獨自逃生、拋棄他的人民，他認為他的子民至少應該有機會戰鬥。於是，三個星期裡，Turk 人傾全力猛攻 Constantinople：他們的大砲轟塌了城牆、房屋和整條街道。但 Constantinople 的人民——商人、店主——這些從未拿過武器的人，此刻以老兵的勇氣奮勇作戰。但他們的人數劣勢太大，三個星期後，Turk 人突破了防線，湧入城中。他們燒殺搶掠，殺死了 Constantine 皇帝，把他的家人賣為奴隸。伊斯蘭的新月升起在 Constantinople 的教堂上空，教堂被改建為清真寺，至今依然如此。

Now that the gate to Europe had been broken, the Turks crossed the
strait and could reach the Balkan Peninsula. Soon Greece was conquered, and it became part of the Ottoman Empire for four hundred
years. The Turkish armies swept onwards, through the Balkans and into
Hungary.

如今通往歐洲的大門已被打破，Turk 人渡過海峽，兵臨 Balkan 半島。Greece 很快被征服，成為 Ottoman 帝國的一部分長達四百年。Turk 大軍繼續橫掃，穿過 Balkan 半島，直入 Hungary。

Only when the Turks came to Vienna, the capital of Austria, were they
stopped. Vienna held out against the Turkish advance and so saved the
other countries of Europe from being invaded.

直到 Turk 人來到 Austria 的首都 Vienna，他們才被擋住。Vienna 頂住了 Turk 人的進攻，從而使歐洲其他國家免於被入侵。

The danger of Ottoman invasion remained, however. As Europe had
once been threatened by the Huns and later by the Mongols of Genghis
Khan, so it was now under the threat of the Turks. Europe paid a terrible
price for having left Constantinople to its fate. Yet some good came from
the Ottoman invasion.

然而，Ottoman 入侵的威脅依然存在。正如歐洲曾經受到匈奴人的威脅，後來又受到 Genghis Khan 蒙古人的威脅一樣，現在歐洲面臨的是 Turk 人的威脅。歐洲為拋棄 Constantinople、任其自生自滅付出了慘痛的代價。然而，Ottoman 入侵也帶來了一些好處。

Before Constantinople was taken by the Turks, a great number of people fled westwards, mainly to Italy. These refugees from Constantinople
spoke the Greek language and they brought with them books that contained the knowledge of ancient Greece and Rome, a knowledge that
Western Europe had forgotten.

在 Constantinople 被 Turk 人攻陷之前，大量的人逃往西方，主要是去 Italy。這些來自 Constantinople 的難民說的是希臘語，他們帶來了包含古 Greece 和古 Rome 知識的書籍——這些知識西歐早已遺忘。

If this had happened three hundred years earlier, no one would have
paid much attention to these Greeks from Constantinople and the
knowledge they brought. But in this new age, when people's minds were
eager and curious, the knowledge that came from Constantinople, the
knowledge of ancient Greece, excited and stirred the Italians.

如果這件事發生在三百年前，沒有人會在意這些來自 Constantinople 的希臘人和他們帶來的知識。但在這個新時代，人們的心靈充滿渴望與好奇，來自 Constantinople 的知識——古 Greece 的知識——激起了 Italy 人的熱情。

Everywhere in Italy there were
still ruins from the time of ancient
Rome: temples, statues and buildings. In earlier days no one had taken
much notice of these ruins. If an Italian peasant unearthed a Roman statue with his plough, he broke it up and used the marble to fill a hole in a
wall. But now all this changed. People realised that these things from the
