past were treasures. Bishops, princes and rich merchants began to collect anything that could still be found. An old manuscript from Greek or
Roman times, or a statue (even if it had no head) became valuable and
sought-after.

Italy 各地仍然到處可見古 Rome 時代的遺跡：神廟、雕像和建築。在過去，沒有人太注意這些廢墟。如果一個 Italy 農民在犁地時挖出一尊羅馬雕像，他會把它打碎，用大理石去補牆上的洞。但現在一切都變了。人們意識到這些來自過去的東西是珍寶。主教、王公和富商開始收集一切還能找到的古物。一份來自希臘或羅馬時代的古手稿，或一尊雕像（即使沒有頭）都變得珍貴而搶手。

People also studied the Greek myths - the stories of Hercules, of the
Trojan War, of Odysseus. They enjoyed and loved these stories so much
that there were bishops who knew more about the Greek gods than
about the Bible. And at the same time the Italian nation, from princes to
peasants,
became
passionately interested in art,
in painting, sculpture
and architecture. In our time, thousands of people get excited about a
pop singer or film star, but in Italy at that time the population of a city
would come to look at an artist's new painting or statue.

人們也開始研究希臘神話——Hercules 的故事、Troy 戰爭的故事、Odysseus 的故事。他們如此喜愛和熱愛這些故事，以至於有些主教對希臘諸神的瞭解超過了對聖經的瞭解。與此同時，整個 Italy 民族，從王公到農民，都對藝術——繪畫、雕塑和建築——產生了狂熱的興趣。在我們的時代，成千上萬的人會為一個流行歌手或電影明星瘋狂，但在當時的 Italy，整座城市的居民都會跑來觀看一位藝術家新完成的畫作或雕像。

This period when love for art and beauty was reborn, first in Italy and
then spreading to all the countries of Europe, is called the Renaissance,
which means rebirth. The Renaissance came at the same time as the
great voyages of exploration, and it brought wonderful artists such as
Leonardo da Vinci, Raphael and Michelangelo.

這個對藝術和美的熱愛重新誕生的時期，先在 Italy 發端，然後傳遍歐洲各國，被稱為文藝復興（Renaissance），意思是「重生」。文藝復興與偉大的航海探險同時發生，它孕育了 Leonardo da Vinci、Raphael 和 Michelangelo 等傑出的藝術家。

# 19. Leonardo: Childhood and Youth
# 19. Leonardo：童年與青年時期

The sixteenth century brought forth a blossoming of great genius. If a
person had been born in 1500 and if they had lived to be a hundred, during their lifetime they could have met the astronomers Copernicus,
Tycho de Brahe, Kepler and Galileo Galilei. The same person could have
met Columbus, Magellan and the Conquistador Pizarro. They could even
have met William Shakespeare and Queen Elizabeth I.

十六世紀是偉大天才百花齊放的時代。如果一個人生於 1500 年並且活到一百歲，在他一生中就有可能遇到天文學家 Copernicus、Tycho de Brahe、Kepler 和 Galileo Galilei。同一個人也有可能遇到 Columbus、Magellan 和征服者 Pizarro。他甚至可能遇到 William Shakespeare 和 Elizabeth I 女王。

Of course this fortunate individual would have had to travel around a
lot, and they would only have encountered some of these people when
they were in their old age, while others would have been only in their
youth. But such a person would have been able to meet people of genius, perhaps more than in any other century. And perhaps the greatest
were the Italian artists of the Renaissance.

當然，這個幸運的人必須四處旅行，而且他遇到其中一些人時，這些人可能已經年邁，另一些人則可能尚在年少。但這樣一個人將能見到許多天才人物，也許比其他任何一個世紀都多。而其中最偉大的，或許正是文藝復興時期的 Italy 藝術家們。

They were not just painters of pictures - they could do that superbly -
but they also made marble and bronze statues, they were architects who
could design churches and palaces, they could compose music and write
poetry, and they had a thorough knowledge of geometry and mathematics. They even made new discoveries in art such as perspective.

他們不僅僅是畫家——畫畫他們當然畫得出色——但他們還製作大理石和青銅雕像，他們是能設計教堂和宮殿的建築師，他們能作曲和寫詩，而且他們對幾何和數學有透徹的理解。他們甚至在藝術中做出了新的發現，例如透視法。

In earlier times,
the background behind the figures of a painting was
very often gold. Before the Renaissance, a painting of Mary and the Jesus
Child had no landscape or houses or anything in the background. These
earlier painters used gold behind the figures to show that Mary and
Jesus are holy, they belong to a higher world, the world of the spirit.

在更早的時代，畫作中人物背後的背景往往是金色的。在文藝復興之前，一幅描繪聖母 Mary 和聖嬰 Jesus 的畫作背景中沒有風景、沒有房屋、什麼都沒有。這些早期的畫家在人物背後使用金色，以表明 Mary 和 Jesus 是神聖的，他們屬於一個更高的世界——靈性的世界。

If any of these early painters did paint a house or a landscape it was
without perspective. But the painters of the new age - the painters of
the Renaissance - painted Mary and Jesus in the world we all see with
our eyes, and in perspective. They discovered that, for our eyes, parallel
lines come together in a vanishing point. The rules of perspective were
only discovered about five hundred years ago by the great artists of the
Renaissance.

如果這些早期畫家確實畫了房屋或風景，那也是沒有透視的。但新時代的畫家——文藝復興的畫家——將 Mary 和 Jesus 畫在我們用眼睛看到的真實世界中，並且運用了透視法。他們發現，在我們的視覺中，平行線會匯聚到一個消失點。透視法的規則是大約五百年前由文藝復興的偉大藝術家們發現的。

It was a wonderful period in history, and one of the most incredible
individuals was the artist Leonardo da Vinci. He was so called because he
was born in the little village of Vinci, near the famous Italian city of Florence, and his name means Leonardo from Vinci. Leonardo's father,
Piero da Vinci, was a rich lawyer and he wanted his son to also become a
lawyer. But young Leonardo did not care to learn Latin, which was
necessary for a lawyer. He preferred to spend his time in the hills around
Vinci with a little book and a pencil, for he loved to make drawings of
everything he saw: the waves and whirls of a brook, the fish darting in
the water, the frogs in the reeds, a lizard sunning itself on a stone. All
these he watched quietly for hours on end and made drawings of them
in his book. It was in these early days when he was only thirteen or fourteen years old that Leonardo trained his eyes to observe accurately, and
he trained his hand in the skill of drawing what he saw.

這是歷史上一個精彩的時期，而其中最令人難以置信的人物之一就是藝術家 Leonardo da Vinci。他之所以被這樣稱呼，是因為他出生在 Florence 附近一個叫 Vinci 的小村莊，他的名字意思是「來自 Vinci 的 Leonardo」。Leonardo 的父親 Piero da Vinci 是一位富有的律師，他希望兒子也能成為律師。但年輕的 Leonardo 對學習拉丁文——當律師的必備條件——毫無興趣。他寧可帶著一本小冊子和一支鉛筆，在 Vinci 周圍的山丘上消磨時光，因為他熱愛把看到的一切畫下來：小溪的波紋和漩渦、水中穿梭的魚、蘆葦叢中的青蛙、在石頭上曬太陽的蜥蜴。這一切他都靜靜地觀察好幾個小時，然後畫在他的本子上。正是在這些早年時光裡，年僅十三、十四歲的 Leonardo 訓練了他精確觀察的眼力，也訓練了他把所見之物畫下來的手藝。

But his father was not very pleased with the boy who spent his time
drawing pictures of frogs and lizards instead of learning Latin grammar.

但他的父親對這個整天畫青蛙和蜥蜴、不學拉丁文法的男孩可不太滿意。

Now one day a man from the village came to Leonardo's father and
said: 'Look, Sir Piero, I have a nice round, flat and smooth piece of wood
- a perfect circle - which would look well if I hung it up in front my house
as a sort of shield with a nice picture on it. You, Sir Piero, often go to the
city of Florence and know some good painters there. Would you be kind
enough to take the piece of wood with you next time you go and ask
one of the painters to paint a picture on it, something I shall really enjoy
when I look at it. I don't mind if it costs a bit of money!

有一天，村裡的一個人來找 Leonardo 的父親說：「Piero 先生您看，我有一塊漂亮的圓形木板，又扁又光滑——完美的圓形——如果上面畫上一幅好看的圖，掛在我家門前當作盾牌裝飾，一定很好看。Piero 先生，您常去 Florence，認識那裡的好畫家。下次您去的時候，能不能幫我帶上這塊木板，請一位畫家在上面畫些什麼，讓我每次看到都會開心的東西。花點錢我不在乎！」

Piero da Vinci was quite willing to oblige the man, and when he left,
Leonardo's father put the round piece of wood in a corner to take with
him the next time he went to Florence.

Piero da Vinci 很樂意幫這個忙。那人走後，Leonardo 的父親把那塊圓木板放在一個角落裡，準備下次去 Florence 時帶上。

Well, young Leonardo with his sharp eyes soon discovered this shieldlike piece of wood with its smooth surface, and he thought: 'This is just
made to paint on.'

嗯，眼睛銳利的年輕 Leonardo 很快就發現了這塊盾牌狀的光滑木板，心想：「這簡直就是為了畫畫而生的。」

He took the piece of wood up into his room and he spent a few hours
making it even smoother until it became as smooth as glass. Now it was
ready to paint on it. Now what should he paint? Leonardo took out his
sketch book. There were drawings of fish and frogs and lizards and
snakes. Which should it be? Then Leonardo had a bright idea: he was
going to paint something that was a mixture of a frog, a lizard and a
snake - he was going to paint a dragon!

他把木板帶上自己的房間，花了幾個小時把它打磨得更加光滑，直到像玻璃一樣。現在可以在上面作畫了。但該畫什麼呢？Leonardo 拿出他的素描本。裡面有魚、青蛙、蜥蜴和蛇的畫。該選哪個呢？然後 Leonardo 有了一個好主意：他要畫一個混合了青蛙、蜥蜴和蛇的東西——他要畫一條龍！

Fired by this great idea, he set to work. For many hours he painted
and painted. He copied the bulging eyes of the frog, the head of the
lizard, the scales of the fish and the long curving and twisting body of a
snake. When, at last, he put his brush down, a perfectly frightful monster
glared at him from the shield.

被這個好點子激發，他動手工作了。好幾個小時他不停地畫啊畫。他模仿了青蛙鼓凸的眼睛、蜥蜴的頭、魚的鱗片，以及蛇那長長的彎曲扭動的身體。當他終於放下畫筆時，一頭完全嚇人的怪物正從盾牌上瞪著他。

Now this was going to be a surprise for his father. Leonardo drew the
heavy curtains on the windows so that the room was in pitch-darkness.
Only a slit between the curtains was left so that light fell on the painted
monster; everything else was in darkness. When he had arranged every.
thing to his satisfaction, he cried out with a piercing voice: 'Father, father,
come up quickly!'

現在這要給他父親一個驚喜了。Leonardo 拉上窗戶的厚重窗簾，讓房間陷入一片漆黑。只留下窗簾之間的一條縫隙，讓光線恰好照在畫好的怪物上，其他一切都隱沒在黑暗中。等一切安排妥當之後，他尖聲大喊：「父親，父親，快上來！」

Piero da Vinci came rushing upstairs, wondering if his son had hurt
himself. He burst into the room and had the shock of his life when he
saw, in the gloom, a hideous dragon staring balefully at him.

Piero da Vinci 衝上樓，擔心兒子是不是受傷了。他闖進房間，在昏暗中看到一條醜陋的惡龍正凶狠地盯著他，嚇得魂飛魄散。

For a moment he gasped, but then he heard his son chuckling in the
dark room and realised what young Leonardo had been up to. He said:
'It will cost me money to pay the man for his wood that you have wasted.
He isn't going to hang this in front of his house. But if you, my boy, can
do this sort of thing, then you will probably make a better painter than a
lawyer.'

他倒吸一口氣，但隨即聽到兒子在黑暗中偷笑，才明白小 Leonardo 搞了什麼鬼。他說：「我得花錢賠那個人被你糟蹋的木板了。他可不會把這東西掛在家門口。不過，我的孩子，如果你能畫出這樣的東西，那你當畫家恐怕比當律師更合適。」

The next day the father went to Florence and showed his son's picture
to a famous painter called Verrocchio, who said immediately: 'If your boy
could do such a painting, he is, indeed, a born painter and I shall be glad
to have him as a pupil.'

第二天，父親前往 Florence，把兒子的畫給一位名叫 Verrocchio 的著名畫家看。Verrocchio 立刻說：「如果你的孩子能畫出這樣的作品，他確實是天生的畫家，我很樂意收他為徒。」

And so
Leonardo came to Florence as apprentice to this famous
painter. But he did not start immediately with lessons in drawing or
painting. Because you could not buy paint in those days, every painter
had to make their own paint, and it was the job of their pupils to do this.
The apprentices had to make charcoal that was needed for drawing outlines, they had to prepare the canvas for oil paintings. For two years
Leonardo did only these jobs. Then he had to learn geometry and perspective, and when he had learned these things thoroughly he was still
not allowed to do his own paintings. He was only allowed to paint a little
part of one of his master's paintings - he might paint part of the blue sky
in a picture, or a cloud, or the grass. It was a long period of study and
learning for Leonardo.

就這樣，Leonardo 來到 Florence，成為這位著名畫家的學徒。但他並沒有立刻開始學習素描或繪畫。因為在那個年代你買不到現成的顏料，每位畫家都必須自己調製顏料，而這正是學徒的工作。學徒們必須製作畫輪廓用的炭筆，必須為油畫準備畫布。Leonardo 整整兩年只做這些事。然後他必須學習幾何和透視法，即使徹底學會了這些，他仍然不被允許畫自己的畫。他只能畫師傅畫作中一個小小的部分——他可能畫一幅畫中的一片藍天，或一朵雲，或一片草地。對 Leonardo 來說，這是一段漫長的學習時期。

# 20. Leonardo in Florence and Milan
# 20. Leonardo 在 Florence 和 Milan

It took years before Leonardo, as an apprentice painter, was allowed to
paint a small, unimportant part of one of his master's paintings. But one
day Verrocchio, the master, said: 'We shall now make a start with figure
painting. I have finished this picture of saints and angels, except for one
angel here, which you can paint, Leonardo!

Leonardo 當了好幾年學徒，才被允許在師傅的畫作中畫一個小小的、不重要的部分。但有一天，師傅 Verrocchio 說：「我們現在開始學畫人物吧。這幅聖徒和天使的畫我已經完成了，只剩這裡的一個天使沒畫，Leonardo，你來畫吧！」

So, for several days, Leonardo worked on that one angel in the picture. When he had finished, Verrocchio looked at Leonardo's work for a
long time. Then he turned to the young man and said: 'Your work is better than mine, Leonardo. There is nothing I can teach you any longer.
You are a master! And so Leonardo left Verrocchio and set up as a master painter on his own.

於是，Leonardo 花了好幾天畫那幅畫中的一個天使。畫完之後，Verrocchio 端詳了 Leonardo 的作品很久。然後他轉向這位年輕人說：「Leonardo，你的作品比我的還好。我已經沒有什麼可以教你的了。你是一位大師！」就這樣，Leonardo 離開了 Verrocchio，自立門戶成為獨當一面的畫家。

A painter could only make a living if people ordered a painting from
them, if they gave them a commission. The people of Florence loved art,
and a good painter could always be certain of getting commissions in
Florence. Because Leonardo was a great painter, a number of people
gave him commissions, but people soon stopped coming to him for pictures. Leonardo would
start a picture, but then he would
become
interested in something else and would stop. As a result, the picture was
never finished.

一位畫家只有在有人訂畫——也就是委託他創作時——才能維持生計。Florence 的人民熱愛藝術，一位好畫家在 Florence 總是能確定會有委託上門。因為 Leonardo 是一位偉大的畫家，不少人向他委託作品，但人們很快就不再找他畫畫了。Leonardo 會開始畫一幅畫，但隨後就對別的事情產生了興趣，然後停下來。結果，那幅畫永遠也沒有完成。

Don't think that the people of Florence did not like Leonardo, they
loved him. Many people said that he was the most beautiful human
being they had ever seen. He was excellent company, told amusing stories for hours on end, and on occasions entertained his friends with his
great strength. He would take a horseshoe in his hands and bend it
apart until it was a straight length of iron. Or he would tell his friends to
drive a riderless horse through the street in full gallop, then he would
step in the horse's path and stop it with one tug on the reins. He played
a dozen musical instruments to perfection, and he invented some new
instruments as well. One was a wooden box shaped like a horse's head
with strings drawn across.

別以為 Florence 的人不喜歡 Leonardo——他們愛他。很多人說他是他們見過最俊美的人。他是極好的伴侶，能講幾個小時的趣事，有時還會用他驚人的力量來娛樂朋友。他能用雙手把一個馬蹄鐵掰開，掰成一根直鐵條。或者他會讓朋友們趕一匹無人騎乘的馬在街上全速奔馳，然後他站到馬的路線上，只拉一下韁繩就把馬停住。他能完美地演奏十幾種樂器，還發明了一些新樂器。其中一個是一個形狀像馬頭的木箱，上面繃著弦。

The people of Florence were proud to have such a gifted man in their
city, but they did not give him any work because it was quite pointless -
he never finished it.

Florence 的人民為城裡有這樣一位天才而自豪，但他們不再給他任何工作，因為那完全沒有意義——他永遠也不會完成。

Why was this? It was not because he was lazy - far from it. He could be
seen working in his house deep into the night. He even invented a
special light for himself to work at night, for there was as yet no electricity or gas. People had to work by the light of candles with flickering
flames. To prevent the flickering, he put a candle in a glass cylinder and
the glass cylinder in a bowl filled with water. The cylinder kept the flame
steady and the water in the bowl magnified the flame and made the light
brighter, as bright as dozens of candles. So Leonardo at times worked all
night by the light of his invention.

為什麼會這樣呢？絕不是因為他懶——恰恰相反。人們可以看到他在家裡工作到深夜。他甚至發明了一種特殊的燈光方便自己夜間工作，因為那時還沒有電也沒有煤氣。人們只能靠搖曳的燭光工作。為了防止燭火搖曳，他把蠟燭放進一個玻璃圓筒裡，再把玻璃圓筒放進一個裝滿水的碗中。圓筒讓火焰穩定，碗裡的水放大了火焰，使光線更加明亮，亮得如同數十支蠟燭。就這樣，Leonardo 有時靠著他發明的燈光通宵工作。

Leonardo was so keen on inventing new things that, at times, he lost
interest in painting. Although he could paint better than anybody else,
he was, in his heart, a scientist and an inventor rather than a painter.

Leonardo 如此熱衷於發明新事物，以至於有時他對繪畫失去了興趣。雖然他畫得比任何人都好，但在他心底，他是一個科學家和發明家，而不是一個畫家。

For example, when he had climbed the hills around Vinci as a young
boy, he had noted seashells embedded in the rocks. Even as a boy he
had wondered how seashells came to be in a place hundreds of miles
from the sea. Now, as a man he thought of it again and he came to the
conclusion that, once upon a time, the hills of Vinci must have been covered by the sea. At that time no one gave a thought to such questions. It
took three hundred years until modern scientists came to the answer
Leonardo had found for himself.

舉個例子，當他還是小男孩在 Vinci 周圍的山丘上攀爬時，他注意到岩石中嵌著貝殼。即使是小時候，他就好奇貝殼怎麼會出現在離大海幾百英里的地方。現在成年後，他再次思考這個問題，得出了一個結論：在很久以前，Vinci 的山丘一定曾被大海覆蓋。在那個時代，沒有人思考過這樣的問題。三百年後，現代科學家才得出了 Leonardo 自己早已找到的答案。

Leonardo
also became very interested in human anatomy. He got
hold of some corpses, which was not difficult in those days as criminals
were often hanged. As there was no refrigeration the corpses must have
smelt horribly, but Leonardo spent days studying these corpses, cutting
them up and making drawings of the bones, muscles, hearts and blood
vessels. His drawings are so exact and accurate they could still be used
by a medical student today. Leonardo knew more about the human
body than most doctors of his time. Another time he became interested
in map-making and was, perhaps, the first person to make a contour
map, which shows the height of the land. At other times, he would fill his
notebooks with drawings of plants.

Leonardo 也對人體解剖學產生了濃厚的興趣。他弄到了一些屍體——在那個年代這並不困難，因為罪犯經常被絞刑處決。由於沒有冷藏設備，屍體的氣味一定極其可怕，但 Leonardo 花了好幾天研究這些屍體，把它們切開，畫下骨骼、肌肉、心臟和血管。他的畫作如此精確，今天的醫學生仍然可以使用。Leonardo 對人體的瞭解超過了他那個時代大多數的醫生。還有一次，他對製圖產生了興趣，他可能是第一個製作等高線地圖（顯示地面高度的地圖）的人。其他時候，他會在筆記本上畫滿植物的圖。

So Leonardo was very busy, working very hard. But with all these
things to study and to draw he had no time to get on with the paintings
he had promised to do, and that is why people in Florence no longer
gave him commissions.

所以 Leonardo 忙得不得了，工作非常勤奮。但要研究和繪製的東西太多了，他沒有時間去完成承諾過的畫作，這就是 Florence 的人們不再向他委託作品的原因。

Eventually, Leonardo found himself without money and with debts; he
owed people money and could not pay them
back. Fortunately,
Francesco Sforza, the ruler of Milan, engaged Leonardo not as a painter,
but as a director of music and to make decorations for festivals and theatre performances. Leonardo did this work very well, inventing all kinds
of complicated machinery so that actors seemed to fly over the stage.

最終，Leonardo 身無分文，債台高築；他欠人錢卻還不起。幸運的是，Milan 的統治者 Francesco Sforza 聘用了 Leonardo，不是當畫家，而是擔任音樂總監，並為節日慶典和戲劇演出製作佈景裝飾。Leonardo 把這份工作做得非常出色，他發明了各種複雜的機械裝置，讓演員看起來像是在舞台上飛翔。

Sforza was so pleased with Leonardo that he gave him a great and
important task: to make an enormous bronze
statue
of
a rider on
prancing horse, in honour of Sforza's father. (It was taken for granted
that a painter was also a sculptor.)

Sforza 對 Leonardo 十分滿意，交給他一項重大而重要的任務：製作一座巨大的青銅雕像——一個騎士騎在揚蹄駿馬上的雕像——以紀念 Sforza 的父親。（在當時，畫家同時也是雕塑家，這是理所當然的事。）

Leonardo threw himself heart and soul into this work. It was to be the
largest bronze statue in the world. He first made countless drawings of
horses, then he made a little clay model of a horse and rider, and then
he made a large clay model the size the statue should really be.

Leonardo 全心全意地投入了這項工作。這將是世界上最大的青銅雕像。他先畫了無數幅馬的素描，然後做了一個馬和騎手的小型泥塑模型，接著又做了一個與雕像實際尺寸等大的大型泥塑模型。

When that large clay model was finished, the prancing horse was
twenty feet high, and the whole population of Milan came to admire it.

當這座大型泥塑模型完成時，揚蹄的駿馬高達二十英尺，全 Milan 的居民都來讚賞它。

To make the whole thing in bronze, Leonardo wanted seventy tons of
bronze. That was a lot. Even the very wealthy ruler of Milan was shaken
by the cost, but in the end he agreed, and the foundries began to make
the bronze for Leonardo's enormous statue.

要把整座雕像鑄成青銅，Leonardo 需要七十噸青銅。這個數字驚人。即使是非常富有的 Milan 統治者也被這筆費用嚇了一跳，但最終他同意了，鑄造廠開始為 Leonardo 的巨型雕像準備青銅。

Just then the French invaded Italy and the bronze that had been
intended for Leonardo's statue was used to make cannons instead. But
worse was to happen. The French armies won and Sforza had to flee.
When the French entered Milan and their bowmen saw the great clay
model Leonardo had made, they used it for target practice. In a short
time the clay crumbled and the whole thing became just a heap of dust.
So this was another great work of Leonardo's that was never finished.

就在這時，France 人入侵了 Italy，原本為 Leonardo 的雕像準備的青銅被改鑄成了大砲。但更糟的事還在後頭。France 軍隊獲勝，Sforza 不得不逃亡。當 France 人進入 Milan，他們的弓箭手看到 Leonardo 製作的那座巨大泥塑模型時，把它當作射箭的靶子。不久，泥塑便碎裂了，整座作品化為一堆塵土。就這樣，Leonardo 又一件偉大的作品未能完成。
# 21. The Last Supper
# 21. 最後的晚餐

Some people are easily satisfied with their own work, they don't aim very high. They are quite happy if they can get away with poor work and little effort.

有些人很容易對自己的工作感到滿足，他們的目標不高。如果能用拙劣的作品和少少的努力矇混過關，他們就很開心了。

Leonardo looked upon such people with contempt; in all he did he set himself the highest standard. He would give endless time and unceasing effort to every task, whatever it was. But often people who did not have such high standards simply could not understand why Leonardo always took such an endlessly long time to finish his work. They could not understand that Leonardo was not easily satisfied and that only the very highest achievement was ever good enough for him, as can be seen from the story of the famous painting of the Last Supper.

Leonardo 對這樣的人嗤之以鼻；無論做什麼，他都為自己設定最高的標準。他會為每一項工作投入無盡的時間和不懈的努力，不管那是什麼。但那些標準不那麼高的人，往往無法理解為什麼 Leonardo 完成工作總是要花那麼長的時間。他們無法理解，Leonardo 不是容易滿足的人，只有最高的成就才夠得上他的要求——從那幅著名的《最後的晚餐》的故事中就可以看出來。

When Leonardo was still working on that great clay model of rider and horse, the monks of a monastery in Milan came to him and asked him to paint a very special picture for them.

當 Leonardo 還在製作那座巨大的騎士與馬匹黏土模型時，Milan 一座修道院的修士們來找他，請他為他們畫一幅非常特別的畫。

On a wall of their refectory (their communal dining room) the monks wanted a picture of the last meal Jesus had with his disciples, the last meal before he was betrayed and taken to be crucified. At this last supper with his disciples, Jesus said: 'One of you will betray me,' meaning Judas Iscariot, who was also present, although Jesus did not say who was to betray him.

修士們想在他們食堂（也就是共用餐廳）的一面牆上，畫一幅 Jesus 與門徒共進最後一餐的畫——那是他被出賣、被帶去釘十字架之前的最後一頓飯。在這場與門徒的最後晚餐上，Jesus 說：「你們當中有一個人要出賣我。」他指的是同樣在場的 Judas Iscariot，雖然 Jesus 並沒有說出是誰要出賣他。

This is the moment Leonardo painted. Jesus has just said these words and the disciples are shocked that one of them could betray their master. Every one of the disciples in the picture shows his horror or grief in a different way; only Judas sits grim and sullen and dark, knowing whom the Lord meant.

這就是 Leonardo 所描繪的那一刻。Jesus 剛說完這些話，門徒們震驚於他們之中竟有人會出賣自己的老師。畫中的每一位門徒都以不同的方式表現出他的驚恐或悲痛；唯獨 Judas 面色陰沉、凶狠而黯淡地坐著，因為他知道主指的是誰。

Even for a genius like Leonardo, painting this moment was an enormously difficult task. But he set about it with his usual thoroughness. First he wanted to find models for the faces of the disciples. For weeks and months he walked through the streets of Milan peering at people's faces. When, at long last, he saw a man whose face he thought could represent one of the disciples (although he is likely to have been Italian rather than Palestinian), Leonardo observed that man for hours until he could remember every feature of his face, then he rushed home to make a quick sketch of the face he had seen.

即使是像 Leonardo 這樣的天才，要描繪這一刻也是極其困難的任務。但他以一貫的嚴謹態度著手進行。首先，他想為門徒的面孔找到模特兒。一連數週數月，他在 Milan 的街頭行走，端詳人們的面孔。當他終於看到一個人，覺得那張臉可以代表某位門徒時（雖然那人很可能是 Italian 而不是 Palestinian），Leonardo 會觀察那個人數個小時，直到記住他臉上的每一個特徵，然後趕回家快速畫下他所看到的那張臉。

But sometimes months and months passed in which he could not see a face that was of any use to him.

但有時候好幾個月過去了，他都看不到一張對他有用的臉。

The face of Christ was, of course, a very great difficulty. Where could he find a face to use as a model for Jesus? But, after many months, he saw a young nobleman whose face he thought had just the right balance between kindness and sorrow.

Christ 的面孔當然是非常大的難題。他要到哪裡去找一張臉來作為 Jesus 的模特兒呢？但是，過了好幾個月後，他看到一位年輕的貴族，覺得他的面容恰好在慈悲與悲傷之間取得了完美的平衡。

It was not only the finding of models for the faces that took such a long time. Sometimes Leonardo would arrive in the morning and stand before the unfinished picture in the monastery for the whole day, deep in thought. Then, at the end of the day, he would leave without having done a single brushstroke.

不僅是尋找面孔的模特兒花了那麼長的時間。有時 Leonardo 早上來到修道院，在那幅未完成的畫前站上一整天，沉浸在思考中。然後到了傍晚，他一筆都沒畫就離開了。

You can imagine that the abbot of this monastery became frantic with impatience about the slow progress of this picture. He pleaded with Leonardo to work faster and to finish it. He became cross with Leonardo, but it made no difference - the great painter took no notice of him.

你可以想像，這座修道院的院長對這幅畫緩慢的進度急得抓狂。他懇求 Leonardo 加快速度完成畫作。他對 Leonardo 生起氣來，但毫無用處——這位偉大的畫家完全不理會他。

At long last the picture was nearly finished; only one face was still missing: the face of Judas, the miserable traitor. Once more Leonardo roamed the streets of Milan searching for just the right face. He went to places where thieves and rogues came together, and filled his notebooks with sketches of their features. But none of them seemed just the right model for Judas.

終於，這幅畫快要完成了；只剩一張臉還沒畫：那個可悲的叛徒 Judas 的臉。Leonardo 再次在 Milan 街頭遊蕩，尋找恰好合適的面孔。他去了盜賊和惡棍聚集的地方，在筆記本上畫滿了他們面孔的素描。但沒有一個人看起來是 Judas 恰好合適的模特兒。

By then the abbot of the monastery had lost patience. He screamed and shouted at Leonardo: 'I have put up with all this slow work as long as you had the excuse of taking great trouble over the faces of Jesus and the disciples, but I am not going to wait and wait for the face of that scoundrel Judas. Finish the picture immediately!'

到那時，修道院院長已經失去了耐性。他對 Leonardo 又叫又喊：「只要你還有藉口說你是在 Jesus 和門徒的面孔上費盡苦心，我就忍受了這一切緩慢的進度，但我不打算為了那個無賴 Judas 的臉一等再等。立刻把畫完成！」

'Well,' said Leonardo calmly, 'if you are really in such a hurry, I can finish the picture in a couple of hours. I shall simply use your face for Judas Iscariot!'

「好吧，」Leonardo 平靜地說，「如果你真的那麼急，我可以在幾個小時內完成這幅畫。我只要用你的臉來畫 Judas Iscariot 就行了！」

The answer shook the abbot. He was terrified at the idea that his monks and the whole of Milan would see him painted as Judas. And so he calmed down and let Leonardo finish the picture in his own time.

這個回答把院長嚇了一大跳。一想到他的修士們和整個 Milan 的人都會看到自己被畫成 Judas，他就嚇壞了。於是他冷靜下來，讓 Leonardo 按照自己的節奏完成畫作。

Leonardo's answer showed what he thought of people who did not take great trouble over their own work and therefore could not appreciate a person who did. They were no better than Judas Iscariot, for every kind of careless work is really a betrayal of the good work that is possible.

Leonardo 的回答顯示了他對那些不在自己的工作上費盡心力、因此也無法欣賞認真之人的看法。他們並不比 Judas Iscariot 好到哪裡去，因為每一種草率的工作，其實都是對可能做好的工作的一種背叛。

When, in the end, the picture was finished, people from all over Italy and other countries came to Milan to see it. They praised it as the most wonderful painting ever created.

當這幅畫最終完成時，來自 Italy 各地和其他國家的人們紛紛來到 Milan 觀賞。他們稱讚它是有史以來最美妙的畫作。

But here again misfortune struck Leonardo, and it was his own fault because he could not stop experimenting. Unlike painting on canvas where one can use oil paints, painters had always mixed their paint with milk when painting on walls. Leonardo wanted to try something new on the wall of this monastery. He used a special mixture of oil paint which did not work out well at all. Only a couple of years later, damp patches came out and spoiled the picture, then the brilliant colours became dull, and in more and more places the paint began to peel off. In the course of time the picture became only a shadow of what it had been.

但不幸再次降臨在 Leonardo 身上，而且是他自己的錯，因為他無法停止實驗。不像在畫布上作畫可以使用油彩，畫家們在牆上作畫時向來把顏料與牛奶混合。Leonardo 想在這座修道院的牆上嘗試新東西。他使用了一種特殊的油彩混合物，結果完全不理想。僅僅幾年之後，潮濕的斑點就出現了，破壞了畫面，然後燦爛的色彩變得暗淡，越來越多的地方顏料開始剝落。隨著時間推移，這幅畫變成了它曾經輝煌面貌的一道影子。

Later, other painters who were not as skilled as Leonardo were called in to 'improve' the poor masterpiece, but they only made things worse.

後來，其他技藝不如 Leonardo 的畫家被請來「修復」這幅可憐的傑作，但他們只讓情況更糟了。

In the Second World War a strange thing happened. A bomb fell near the monastery, and the whole building collapsed except for the one wall bearing Leonardo's Last Supper. Recently, modern methods have tried to wash away the overpainting of the other painters and to restore Leonardo's work.

在第二次世界大戰中，一件奇特的事發生了。一顆炸彈落在修道院附近，整棟建築都倒塌了，唯獨承載 Leonardo《最後的晚餐》的那面牆倖存。近年來，人們運用現代技術試圖洗去其他畫家覆蓋上去的顏料，恢復 Leonardo 原來的作品。

The Last Supper made Leonardo so famous that the city of Florence called him back to paint a picture of a great battle on the walls of the town hall. A battle scene with hundreds of men and horses - that was a wonderful task for Leonardo! You can imagine how he worked on every detail. This time he had invented a quite special kind of paint: when you painted the picture the colours looked quite dull, but when the colours were heated they became wonderfully brilliant. Leonardo had tried it out on cardboard and it had worked out very well. And so he painted this battle scene with tireless effort to show the Florentine people what he could do.

《最後的晚餐》讓 Leonardo 聲名大噪，以至於 Florence 城請他回來，在市政廳的牆上畫一幅大型戰役圖。一幅有著數百人和馬匹的戰爭場景——對 Leonardo 來說，這是一項美妙的任務！你可以想像他在每一個細節上如何精益求精。這一次他發明了一種相當特殊的顏料：畫的時候顏色看起來很暗淡，但加熱之後就會變得無比絢爛。Leonardo 先在紙板上試過了，效果非常好。於是他不知疲倦地畫下這幅戰役場景，想向 Florence 的人們展示他的能耐。

The galloping horses, the shining swords, the fighting men in this picture would be something that could never be surpassed. When the picture was finished the colours looked dull. Now charcoal-braziers were brought in and the glowing coals began to heat the painting. But a wall is not the same as cardboard, and as the heat rose the colours began to run down the picture; hastily the fire was extinguished, but it was too late.

畫中奔馳的駿馬、閃亮的刀劍、搏鬥的勇士，將是無人能超越的傑作。畫完成時，顏色看起來很暗淡。於是炭火爐被搬了進來，灼熱的炭火開始加熱畫面。但牆壁不同於紙板，隨著溫度升高，顏料開始沿著畫面流淌而下；人們匆忙把火撲滅，但已經太遲了。

# 22. Inventions and the Mona Lisa
# 22. 發明與蒙娜麗莎

You may wonder how such a great man as Leonardo could ruin his first great paintings by experiments. But he was one of the few people in his time who realised that we can only learn from experiments. There was no one else who shared his love and interest for experimenting. There were no scientists who knew enough about chemistry or physics who could have given him good advice. He had to find out everything for himself, and he loved knowledge so much that he was willing to risk his wonderful paintings for the sake of an experiment.

你也許會納悶，像 Leonardo 這樣偉大的人怎麼會用實驗毀掉自己最初的偉大畫作。但他是那個時代少數認識到我們只能從實驗中學習的人之一。沒有別人和他分享對實驗的熱愛與興趣。沒有任何科學家對化學或物理學有足夠的了解能給他好的建議。一切都得靠他自己去摸索，而他如此熱愛知識，甚至願意為了一場實驗而冒著毀掉精彩畫作的風險。

Many people loved and admired Leonardo, yet he had no real friend, a friend with whom he could share his burning interest for knowledge. He was really a lonely man because he was so far ahead of his time.

許多人喜愛並欽佩 Leonardo，但他沒有一個真正的朋友，一個能分享他對知識熾熱興趣的朋友。他真的是一個孤獨的人，因為他遠遠超越了他的時代。

When Milan was taken by the French and the great clay model of the rider and horse was destroyed, Leonardo first went to Venice. At that time Venice was at war with the Ottoman Turks. The Turks were storming into Europe after the fall of Constantinople and their ships attacked the Venetian ships in the Mediterranean, and so Leonardo turned his mind to inventing ways of defeating them.

當 Milan 被法國人占領、那座巨大的騎士與馬匹黏土模型被摧毀後，Leonardo 先去了 Venice。當時 Venice 正與 Ottoman Turks 交戰。Turks 在 Constantinople 陷落後大舉入侵 Europe，他們的船隻在 Mediterranean 攻擊 Venetian 的船隊，於是 Leonardo 開始把心思轉向發明擊敗他們的方法。

In his notebooks (which still exist today) we find ideas that were only put into practice five hundred years later. He designed a one-man submarine to attack the Ottoman ships underwater, and a diving-suit with a glass-fronted helmet and air-filled bladders from which tubes led to the helmet so that the diver could breathe underwater. He thought of using gloves with webbed fingers for swimming underwater. These were used hundreds of years later by divers in the Second World War.

在他的筆記本裡（至今仍然存世），我們發現了直到五百年後才被付諸實現的構想。他設計了一艘單人潛水艇來從水下攻擊 Ottoman 的船隻，還有一套潛水裝——配備玻璃面罩的頭盔和充氣囊，管子從氣囊通到頭盔，讓潛水者可以在水下呼吸。他想到了使用蹼狀手指手套在水下游泳。這些在數百年後的第二次世界大戰中被潛水員使用。

He had the idea that one could throw containers of arsenic sulphide at the enemy. Arsenic sulphide is a poisonous gas, and was used for the first time in the First World War. He also thought that one's own troops should be protected against the poisonous gas by a damp cloth bound over nose and mouth, which is the first idea of a kind of gas mask. He designed an armoured car driven by pedals (of course the petrol engine was unknown at that time).

他想到可以向敵人投擲裝有砷化硫的容器。砷化硫是一種有毒氣體，在第一次世界大戰中首次被使用。他還想到己方的軍隊應該用一塊濕布綁在鼻子和嘴巴上來防護毒氣，這是防毒面具的最初構想。他設計了一輛用踏板驅動的裝甲車（當然，那個時代還沒有汽油引擎）。

But having thought out all these modern weapons of war, Leonardo wrote in his notebook: 'I will not make these things known for men are evil and might use them for killing.'

但在想出了這一切現代戰爭武器之後，Leonardo 在筆記本中寫道：「我不會公開這些東西，因為人是邪惡的，可能會用它們來殺人。」

He did not tell the Venetians or anybody else of his ideas, but he kept them in his notebooks where he wrote everything in mirror-writing (so that it would be harder to read). Nobody bothered to look at these notebooks until the twentieth century when these kinds of weapons already existed.

他沒有把自己的想法告訴 Venetian 人或任何其他人，而是把它們保存在筆記本裡，用鏡像書寫記錄一切（這樣更難被閱讀）。直到二十世紀——當這些武器已經存在的時候——才有人費心去翻閱這些筆記本。

Leonardo left Venice and returned to Florence to paint the battle scene that ended so sadly. But the battle scene did not matter so much to Leonardo for, at that time, a new idea had got hold of him: the idea of building a flying machine.

Leonardo 離開了 Venice，回到 Florence 去畫那幅結局如此悲慘的戰役圖。但戰役圖對 Leonardo 來說已經不那麼重要了，因為那時一個新的想法已經占據了他的心：建造一台飛行器的想法。

He bought birds in the market and set them free to watch how they took off. He measured their wingspan compared with their body and made drawings of birds in flight. Then he began to build all kinds of wings only to destroy them and start others.

他在市場上買來鳥兒，放飛牠們，觀察牠們如何起飛。他測量了鳥的翼展與身體的比例，畫了飛行中的鳥的圖畫。然後他開始製造各種各樣的翅膀，只為了再把它們拆毀，重新開始。

He even thought of the possibility that the machine might fail in mid-air, and designed a parachute to save the pilot. His drawing clearly shows the same principle as a modern parachute. One of his drawings is of a machine that we now call a helicopter. The last of his drawings relating to flight is a glider similar to those used today.

他甚至考慮到飛行器可能在半空中失靈的可能性，因此設計了一個降落傘來拯救飛行員。他的圖紙清楚地展示了與現代降落傘相同的原理。他的一幅圖畫所描繪的機器，就是我們今天所說的直升機。他與飛行相關的最後一幅圖畫，是一架類似於今日使用的滑翔機。

It is fairly certain that Leonardo not only drew the glider but built it. He disappeared from Florence for a few weeks and when he returned he never mentioned to anybody what he had done, and his later notebooks never mentioned flying machines again. But in the countryside around Florence for centuries there was a legend that peasants had seen a strange enormous bird flying over the hills. So it seems Leonardo had tried out his glider. He was perhaps the first person to fly, but he kept the secret to himself.

幾乎可以確定，Leonardo 不僅畫了滑翔機的圖，而且把它造了出來。他從 Florence 消失了幾個星期，回來之後從未向任何人提起他做了什麼，他後來的筆記本也再沒提過飛行器。但在 Florence 周圍的鄉間，幾百年來一直流傳著一個傳說：農民們曾看到一隻巨大的奇鳥飛越山丘。所以看來 Leonardo 確實試飛了他的滑翔機。他也許是第一個飛上天的人，但他把這個秘密留給了自己。

We can see why Leonardo was a lonely man. There was so much he knew but could not and would not share with others. People had only begun to make machines like the printing press, they did not yet have reliable clocks or watches. Yet here was a man who thought of helicopters, gliders and submarines. People back then could not follow his ideas, he was just too far ahead of his time. They only appreciated Leonardo as a painter, but as a painter he upset and bewildered even his admirers.

我們可以理解為什麼 Leonardo 是個孤獨的人。他知道的太多了，卻無法也不願與他人分享。人們才剛開始製造像印刷機這樣的機器，還沒有可靠的時鐘或手錶。然而這裡有一個人，卻在構想直升機、滑翔機和潛水艇。當時的人們跟不上他的想法，他實在太超前於他的時代了。人們只欣賞作為畫家的 Leonardo，但即使是作為畫家，他也讓他的崇拜者們感到不安和困惑。

Kings and princes begged Leonardo to paint their portraits, but he simply refused. Instead of painting these great and powerful people, he chose to paint the portrait of the wife of an Italian merchant. She was not a person of any great importance, but because Leonardo painted her, her name is known today all over the world, while the noble princes and great ladies of that time are forgotten. Mona Lisa was the name of this lady, and her portrait is perhaps the most famous portrait in the world.

國王和王子們懇求 Leonardo 為他們畫肖像，但他就是拒絕了。他沒有為這些偉大而有權勢的人作畫，反而選擇畫一位 Italian 商人妻子的肖像。她不是什麼重要人物，但因為 Leonardo 畫了她，她的名字今天全世界都知道，而那個時代的高貴王子和偉大貴婦們反而被遺忘了。Mona Lisa 就是這位女士的名字，她的肖像也許是世界上最著名的肖像畫。

This portrait is not large at all, but it took Leonardo six years to paint it. It became a portrait that shows not only the face of Mona Lisa but her soul.

這幅肖像畫一點也不大，但 Leonardo 花了六年才畫完。它成為了一幅不僅展現 Mona Lisa 面容、更展現她靈魂的肖像畫。

By that time, the people of Florence had lost interest in Leonardo, who was about sixty years old. His battle picture had been a grandiose failure; if he painted a portrait it took him years and years, and he spent most of his time drawing machinery that no one understood. The Florentines turned their backs on him. Then Leonardo suffered another great misfortune. He had a stroke. His right arm was paralysed and he could no longer use it for painting or drawing. But this strange man had another rare gift: he was ambidextrous, meaning he could use his left hand just as well as his right, so from now on he worked with his left hand.

到那時，Florence 的人們已經對 Leonardo 失去了興趣，他大約六十歲了。他的戰役圖是一場壯觀的失敗；如果他畫一幅肖像，就要花上好幾年又好幾年；而他大部分時間都在畫那些沒人看得懂的機械圖。Florence 人背棄了他。接著 Leonardo 又遭受了一次重大的不幸。他中風了。他的右手癱瘓了，再也無法用來繪畫或素描。但這個奇特的人還有另一項罕見的天賦：他是雙手靈巧的，意思是他的左手和右手一樣好用，所以從此他改用左手工作。

Florence was no longer interested in him, but the king of France was a great admirer of Leonardo, and invited Leonardo to spend the last eight years of his life in France in peace and without worries.

Florence 已不再關心他了，但法國國王是 Leonardo 的忠實崇拜者，邀請 Leonardo 在 France 安詳無憂地度過他人生最後的八年。

When people in these last years of his life praised Leonardo for all the work he had done, for the beauty he had created, he only shook his head and said: 'I have achieved nothing!' He died in 1519, the year in which Magellan set out on the first journey around the world.

在他生命最後幾年裡，當人們讚揚 Leonardo 所做的一切工作、所創造的美時，他只是搖搖頭說：「我什麼也沒有成就！」他於 1519 年去世，那一年正是 Magellan 啟程進行第一次環球航行的一年。

Today we know that Leonardo da Vinci was one of the greatest people who ever lived: an artist, scientist, painter, sculptor, architect, engineer, and a seeker for knowledge and truth.

今天我們知道，Leonardo da Vinci 是有史以來最偉大的人物之一：藝術家、科學家、畫家、雕塑家、建築師、工程師，以及一位知識與真理的追尋者。

# 23. Raphael and Michelangelo
# 23. Raphael 與 Michelangelo

[Note: The beginning of this chapter is missing from the source text.]

[備註：本章開頭在原始文本中缺失。]

...the picture). This picture, showing Mary and her child in heaven above the clouds, and with the blue sky made up of countless blue angels, is perhaps the most famous picture in the world of Mary and the Jesus Child. Raphael was a painter who wanted to touch people's hearts, their feelings - not their minds.

……那幅畫）。這幅畫描繪了 Mary 和她的孩子在雲端之上的天堂，蔚藍的天空由無數藍色天使組成，它也許是世界上最著名的一幅 Mary 與聖嬰 Jesus 的畫作。Raphael 是一位想要觸動人們內心、觸動他們情感的畫家——而不是觸動他們的理智。

Raphael, who could paint the most lovely pictures with ease, died young at the age of thirty-seven. But he left behind hundreds of paintings, far more than Leonardo who was thirty years older when he died.

Raphael 能夠輕而易舉地畫出最美麗的圖畫，卻英年早逝，年僅三十七歲。但他留下了數百幅畫作，遠多於比他年長三十歲才去世的 Leonardo。

Raphael was, perhaps, one of the most fortunate artists who ever lived. He was handsome, charming and everybody loved him. He was kind and gentle, and he made friends easily. The Pope, kings, princes and rich merchants gave him commissions. They gave him more work than he could ever cope with and paid him generously so that he never had the worries Leonardo had. His paintings gave pleasure to millions, but this happy life was also a short one. He died at an age when other painters are just beginning to become famous.

Raphael 也許是有史以來最幸運的藝術家之一。他英俊、迷人，人人都喜歡他。他善良而溫柔，很容易交到朋友。教宗、國王、王子和富商們都給他委託。他們給了他多到做不完的工作，並慷慨地付他報酬，因此他從未有過 Leonardo 那樣的煩惱。他的畫作給數百萬人帶來了歡愉，但這幸福的人生也是短暫的。他去世時，其他畫家才剛開始嶄露頭角。

Quite different is the life of another great master, the painter and sculptor Michelangelo. He, too, loved beauty, but the beauty of strength.

另一位偉大大師的生涯卻截然不同，他就是畫家兼雕塑家 Michelangelo。他也熱愛美，但他熱愛的是力量之美。

Most of the figures he painted are not sweet and gentle like Raphael's, but figures of might and power.

他筆下的大多數人物不像 Raphael 的那樣甜美溫柔，而是充滿力量與威嚴的人物。

Raphael loved to paint Mary and the Jesus Child, but Michelangelo made statues of Mary holding the dead body of the adult Jesus in her lap. He depicted the sorrow, the tragedy of the mother who had to see her son crucified. Such pictures or statues of Mary and the body of Jesus are called Pieta.

Raphael 喜歡畫 Mary 和聖嬰 Jesus，但 Michelangelo 卻雕塑了 Mary 抱著成年 Jesus 遺體的雕像。他刻畫了那位必須看著兒子被釘十字架的母親的悲傷與悲劇。這類描繪 Mary 與 Jesus 遺體的畫作或雕像被稱為 Pieta（聖殤）。

Michelangelo painted enormous pictures of God creating the world and of God creating man. These pictures are painted on the ceiling of the Sistine Chapel in Rome. To paint these pictures on the ceiling, Michelangelo had to stand on scaffolding with his head turned upwards, and he had to do this for four years. He became so used to keeping his head this way that, when the work was finished, he still kept his head turned up, and had to read letters by holding them above his head. It took a year before he could hold his head normally again.

Michelangelo 繪製了巨幅畫作，描繪上帝創造世界和上帝創造人類。這些畫作畫在 Rome 的 Sistine Chapel 天花板上。為了在天花板上繪畫，Michelangelo 必須站在鷹架上，頭一直仰著向上，他持續這樣做了四年。他的頭已經習慣了這個姿勢，以至於工作完成後，他仍然保持著頭向上仰的姿態，讀信時得把信舉到頭頂上方才行。花了一整年他才能重新正常地低頭。

If you look at the works of Raphael it is like walking through a lovely garden. If you look at the works of Michelangelo it is like seeing mighty mountains reaching into the sky. In the work of Michelangelo everything is serious. But there was also little happiness in his own long life, even though he lived to well over eighty.

如果你看 Raphael 的作品，那就像漫步於一座可愛的花園。如果你看 Michelangelo 的作品，那就像看到巍峨的高山直插雲霄。在 Michelangelo 的作品裡，一切都是莊嚴的。但在他自己漫長的一生中也少有快樂，即使他活到了八十多歲。

Michelangelo was not handsome like Leonardo and Raphael, nor was he gentle or charming. He did not make friends easily, he was ill-tempered and had fits of rage. He could work for months on a statue, and then, if it was not as good as he wanted it to be, he would take a hammer and break it to pieces.

Michelangelo 不像 Leonardo 和 Raphael 那樣英俊，也不溫柔或迷人。他不容易交到朋友，脾氣暴躁，時常大發雷霆。他可以花好幾個月做一座雕像，然後如果它不如他所期望的那樣好，他就會拿起錘子把它砸得粉碎。

We see how different three of the great artists of the Renaissance were. Leonardo, the thinker and seeker after truth; Raphael, gentle, sweet-tempered, whose paintings touch the feelings; and the fiery, quick-tempered Michelangelo.

我們看到文藝復興三位偉大藝術家是多麼不同。Leonardo，思想家與真理的追尋者；Raphael，溫柔、脾氣甜美，他的畫作觸動人的情感；以及火熱、暴躁的 Michelangelo。

In Italy at the time of the Renaissance, there were not only these three great masters, there were hundreds of artists, painters, sculptors and architects who produced very beautiful work. How was it possible that so many artists could flourish at that time?

在文藝復興時期的 Italy，不僅有這三位偉大的大師，還有數百位藝術家、畫家、雕塑家和建築師創作了非常美麗的作品。當時怎麼可能有那麼多藝術家蓬勃發展呢？

A few centuries earlier, in the time of the feudal system, the noble knights could fight, but could not read or write and still less did they care for art. The villagers and serfs were worked far too hard and were too poor and ignorant to know anything about art. Only the monks in the churches and monasteries had some interest in art. The time of the feudal system did not give many opportunities to artists. If Leonardo or Raphael had been born three hundred years earlier, they could only have been monks painting little pictures on hand-written parchment books.

幾個世紀前，在封建制度的時代，貴族騎士能征善戰，卻不識字也不會寫字，更不用說關心藝術了。村民和農奴們勞動得太辛苦，又太窮太無知，對藝術一無所知。只有教堂和修道院裡的修士對藝術有些興趣。封建制度的時代沒有給藝術家太多機會。如果 Leonardo 或 Raphael 早生了三百年，他們只能做修士，在手抄的羊皮紙書上畫小小的圖畫。

But in the Renaissance in Italy there were hundreds of thousands of people who loved art, who could afford to buy paintings and could give work to all these artists of the Renaissance. Who were these people who could employ so many artists and who had the money and the time and the love to enjoy art?

但在 Italy 的文藝復興時代，有成千上萬的人熱愛藝術，有能力購買畫作，能夠給所有這些文藝復興的藝術家提供工作。這些能僱用那麼多藝術家、有金錢、有時間、有熱愛來欣賞藝術的人是誰呢？

They were the 'citizens', the city-people: merchants, people of business, bankers, lawyers, doctors. They were not knights, they were not serfs - they were free citizens, and a love of art was cultivated in the freedom of the cities that made all these great masterpieces possible.

他們就是「市民」，城市裡的人：商人、生意人、銀行家、律師、醫生。他們不是騎士，不是農奴——他們是自由的市民，而對藝術的熱愛就在城市的自由中被培養起來，正是這種自由使得所有這些偉大的傑作成為可能。

In the feudal age there had been only three classes of people: the peasantry or unfree serfs, the nobility, which included knights and priests, and the king. In the Renaissance there was a new class of free citizens. They encouraged art and artists. The great artists themselves - Leonardo, Raphael, Michelangelo - came from this middle class. They were not noblemen or serfs or priests, but free citizens.

在封建時代只有三個階級：農民或不自由的農奴、包括騎士和教士在內的貴族，以及國王。在文藝復興時代出現了一個新的自由市民階級。他們鼓勵藝術和藝術家。那些偉大的藝術家自己——Leonardo、Raphael、Michelangelo——也來自這個中產階級。他們不是貴族，不是農奴，也不是教士，而是自由的市民。

In Italy, the feudal system had slowly withered away. In place of the noblemen and lords the cities had grown rich and powerful. But this freedom of cities also had its problems. Italy was not one country, but was split up into dominions of great cities. Each city had its own government and its own army or, like Venice, its own navy. And the cities were quite often at war with each other. When the French attacked Milan, neither Florence nor Venice took much notice. The city people were business people: they regarded another city as competitors. That is why there was so much trouble between them. But the free cities were the cradle of Renaissance art.

在 Italy，封建制度已經慢慢消亡。取代貴族和領主的，是日益富裕強大的城市。但城市的自由也有它的問題。Italy 不是一個統一的國家，而是分裂為各大城市的領地。每座城市有自己的政府和自己的軍隊，或者像 Venice 那樣有自己的海軍。而城市之間經常互相開戰。當法國人進攻 Milan 時，Florence 和 Venice 都沒怎麼在意。城市裡的人是生意人：他們把別的城市視為競爭對手。這就是為什麼他們之間有那麼多紛爭。但自由的城市卻是文藝復興藝術的搖籃。

# 24. The Wars of the Roses
# 24. 玫瑰戰爭

In the year 1453, Columbus was two years old, Leonardo was one, and in that year the Ottoman Turks stormed Constantinople and poured through the Balkan Peninsula in the east of Europe.

1453 年，Columbus 兩歲，Leonardo 一歲，而就在這一年，Ottoman Turks 攻陷了 Constantinople，並席捲了 Europe 東部的 Balkan Peninsula。

In the west of Europe, the terrible Hundred Years' War between England and France came to an end. Joan of Arc had been burnt at the stake twenty years earlier without seeing the end of this war, but it did come to an end. In 1453 England and France made peace.

在 Europe 的西部，England 與 France 之間可怕的百年戰爭終於結束了。Joan of Arc 二十年前已被燒死在火刑柱上，沒有看到這場戰爭的終結，但戰爭確實結束了。1453 年，England 和 France 締結了和平。

In Italy at the time of the Renaissance each great city was a state, and the surrounding small towns and villages came under the rule of the big cities. The power of the big cities did away with the power of knights and lords; the feudal system withered away as the power of the cities grew.

在文藝復興時期的 Italy，每座大城市都是一個國家，周圍的小鎮和村莊都歸大城市管轄。大城市的權力取代了騎士和領主的權力；隨著城市力量的增長，封建制度逐漸消亡。

In England things happened quite differently. England was very much a feudal state. It was the English knights and the English kings who had first tried to conquer Scotland and had been defeated by King Robert the Bruce. It was again the English knights and the English kings who had tried to conquer France and had been defeated by Joan of Arc. Both these wars could not have taken place without the consent of the knights, for the Magna Carta stated that the king of England could not go to war without the consent of his knights and noblemen.

在 England，事情的發展完全不同。England 是一個典型的封建國家。正是 English 騎士和 English 國王最先試圖征服 Scotland，卻被 King Robert the Bruce 擊敗。又是 English 騎士和 English 國王試圖征服 France，卻被 Joan of Arc 擊敗。這兩場戰爭如果沒有騎士們的同意是不可能發生的，因為大憲章規定，England 國王未經騎士和貴族的同意不得發動戰爭。

In England, knights and noblemen were quite powerful; even the king had to ask their consent for taxes for going to war.

在 England，騎士和貴族相當有權勢；就連國王要為戰爭徵稅也得徵求他們的同意。

After a hundred years of war with France, which England lost, one might think that the people of England would settle down to a time of peace. The ordinary people, the peasants and merchants would certainly have wanted peace, but not the knights and the noble lords. But as they dare not attack either Scotland or France again, they started a war among themselves, a terrible war with a beautiful name: the Wars of the Roses.

在與 France 打了一百年的戰爭（England 輸了）之後，人們可能會以為 England 的人民會安定下來，迎接一段和平時期。普通百姓——農民和商人——當然渴望和平，但騎士和貴族老爺們不這麼想。但因為他們不敢再進攻 Scotland 或 France，他們就在自己人之間發動了一場戰爭，一場有著美麗名字的可怕戰爭：玫瑰戰爭。

At that time when great artists in Italy created wonderful works of art, England was ravaged by battles between its own people, its own great lords and their knights.

就在 Italy 的偉大藝術家創造出美妙藝術品的同時，England 正被自己人之間的戰鬥所蹂躪——那些大領主和他們的騎士們互相廝殺。

How did this war come about? The middle part of England is divided by the Pennines, a north-south mountain range. West of the Pennines is Lancashire and east of them is Yorkshire. Now the most powerful noble families in the whole of England were the lords of Lancashire and the lords of Yorkshire. The shield of Lancaster showed a red rose and the shield of York a white rose.

這場戰爭是怎麼爆發的呢？England 中部被 Pennines 山脈——一條南北走向的山脈——所分隔。Pennines 以西是 Lancashire，以東是 Yorkshire。而全 England 最有權勢的貴族家族，就是 Lancashire 的領主和 Yorkshire 的領主。Lancaster 家族的盾徽上有一朵紅玫瑰，York 家族的盾徽上有一朵白玫瑰。

The House of Lancaster had so much power that, during the Hundred Years' War, one of them, Henry IV, simply deposed the ruling king of England, Richard II, and made himself king. From then on, through several generations, the kings of England were of the House of Lancaster.

Lancaster 家族擁有如此大的權力，在百年戰爭期間，他們當中的一位——Henry IV——乾脆廢黜了當時的 England 國王 Richard II，自己當了國王。從那時起，歷經數代，England 的國王都出自 Lancaster 家族。

When the Hundred Years' War came to an end, it was another Henry, Henry VI of the House of Lancaster, who ruled. Henry VI, a king of the red rose of Lancaster, unfortunately suffered from what is thought to be a form of catatonic schizophrenia. For over a year, following the English defeat in the Hundred Years' War, he remained in a kind of stupor and was utterly unresponsive to what was going on around him, including the birth of his son. In those days, at his father's death, the eldest son of a king became king no matter how unfit he was to rule. And so somebody had to be chosen to rule England in the name of the unwell king.

當百年戰爭結束時，統治 England 的是另一位 Henry——Lancaster 家族的 Henry VI。Henry VI，這位紅玫瑰 Lancaster 的國王，不幸患有被認為是一種緊張型精神分裂症的疾病。在 English 於百年戰爭中戰敗之後，他有一年多的時間處於一種恍惚狀態，對周圍發生的一切毫無反應，包括他兒子的出生。在那個時代，國王去世後，他的長子無論多麼不適合統治都會成為國王。因此必須選出一個人，以這位生病國王的名義來治理 England。

The man chosen was the duke of York - the House of the White Rose - the next powerful house in England. The duke of York was called 'Protector', but, practically, he was king and made all of the decisions. Of course, he gave all the high positions to his friends and to members of his own family.

被選中的人是 York 公爵——白玫瑰家族——England 第二有權勢的家族。York 公爵被稱為「攝政王」，但實際上他就是國王，做出所有的決定。當然，他把所有高位都給了他的朋友和自己的家族成員。

Henry, although he was not very well, did not like it at all that the duke of York acted as if he were the real king. Henry's wife, Queen Margaret, hated the duke of York and did not want him to be in power. There were other lords and noblemen who were also jealous and did not want to be ruled by him.

Henry 雖然身體不好，但完全不喜歡 York 公爵表現得好像自己是真正的國王。Henry 的妻子 Margaret 王后痛恨 York 公爵，不希望他掌權。還有其他領主和貴族也心懷嫉妒，不想被他統治。

In the end, all the enemies of the duke of York banded together under the sign of the red rose to depose him. All the lords and noblemen who supported the duke of York gathered to fight for him with the white rose on their shields and banners.

最終，York 公爵的所有敵人都在紅玫瑰的旗號下聯合起來要廢黜他。而所有支持 York 公爵的領主和貴族則聚集起來，盾牌和旗幟上都是白玫瑰，為他而戰。

In 1455, two years after the end of the Hundred Years' War, the Wars of the Roses began, and they lasted for thirty years.

1455 年，百年戰爭結束後兩年，玫瑰戰爭爆發了，持續了三十年。

The duke of York was killed during this war, but his son, Edward, continued the struggle. Henry VI was taken prisoner and locked up in the Tower of London where he died. Queen Margaret asked Scotland and France, England's old enemies, to send armies to fight for the red rose of Lancaster.

York 公爵在這場戰爭中被殺，但他的兒子 Edward 繼續戰鬥。Henry VI 被俘，關進了 Tower of London，死在那裡。Margaret 王后請求 Scotland 和 France——England 的老對手——派軍隊來為紅玫瑰 Lancaster 而戰。

Sometimes Lancaster was winning, during which time any noble who had fought for York and who was captured was executed. Sometimes York had the upper hand and executed the supporters of the red rose. There was one lord, the Earl of Warwick, who first supported York, but when Edward of York had established himself as king, he turned against him and joined the Lancastrians. Warwick died in battle, but the war went on.

有時候 Lancaster 占上風，那時任何為 York 而戰被俘的貴族就會被處死。有時候 York 占上風，處死紅玫瑰的支持者。有一位領主，Warwick 伯爵，起初支持 York，但當 York 的 Edward 確立了自己的國王地位後，他反而倒戈加入了 Lancaster 一方。Warwick 戰死沙場，但戰爭繼續進行。

There was not only bloodshed in battle, but there was also foul murder and treachery. When Edward of York died, his son was murdered by an uncle who wanted the crown for himself. But the uncle did not enjoy the crown for long, he was defeated by Henry Tudor of Lancaster, a relative of Henry VI.

不僅有戰場上的流血，還有卑鄙的謀殺和背叛。當 York 的 Edward 去世後，他的兒子被一個覬覦王位的叔叔謀殺了。但這位叔叔也沒有享受王冠多久，他被 Lancaster 的 Henry Tudor——Henry VI 的一位親戚——擊敗了。

With Henry VII the red rose had won, and that was the end of the Wars of the Roses. To end the enmity between the two houses, Henry Tudor married a princess of the House of York.

隨著 Henry VII 的勝利，紅玫瑰贏了，這就是玫瑰戰爭的結局。為了結束兩大家族之間的仇恨，Henry Tudor 娶了 York 家族的一位公主。

During these thirty years of war, hundreds of knights and noblemen had died in battle or had been executed by one side or another. Their castles and the land they owned had been confiscated by either York kings or Lancastrian kings. When the war ended there were hardly any great and powerful lords left, and that was the end of the feudal system in England.

在這三十年的戰爭中，數百名騎士和貴族在戰鬥中陣亡或被其中一方處決。他們的城堡和土地被 York 國王或 Lancaster 國王沒收了。戰爭結束時，幾乎沒有什麼偉大而有權勢的領主還在了，這就是 England 封建制度的終結。

In Italy, the feudal system had disappeared because the city states had grown rich and powerful. In England, the feudal system was destroyed by the Wars of the Roses, although the king remained the strongest power in the country.

在 Italy，封建制度消失了，因為城邦日益富裕強大。在 England，封建制度被玫瑰戰爭摧毀了，儘管國王仍然是國內最強大的力量。

All over Europe, in one way or another, the feudal system, the power of lords, was breaking up. The end of the feudal system belongs also to this time, the age of discovery and the age of the Renaissance.

在整個 Europe，封建制度、領主的權力，以各種不同的方式在瓦解。封建制度的終結也屬於這個時代——大發現的時代和文藝復興的時代。

# 25. Borgia and Savonarola
# 25. Borgia 與 Savonarola

At the beginning of this new age many new things came into the world: new inventions like the printing press, new exploration like Columbus' and Magellan's voyages, a new love for art was born, the Renaissance with Leonardo, Raphael, Michelangelo, and a new class of people became important, the merchant or middle class.

在這個新時代的開端，許多新事物來到了世界上：像印刷機這樣的新發明、像 Columbus 和 Magellan 航行那樣的新探索、對藝術的新熱愛誕生了——帶著 Leonardo、Raphael、Michelangelo 的文藝復興，以及一個新的階級變得重要起來：商人階級或中產階級。

But as all these new ideas rose and spread, old customs and institutions were swept away. The feudal system with the power and the privileges of the noblemen and lords slowly withered.

但隨著這些新思想興起和傳播，舊的習俗和制度被掃蕩了。帶著貴族和領主的權力與特權的封建制度慢慢枯萎了。

For centuries the Church had enjoyed enormous powers and privileges. In the Early Middle Ages, when Germanic tribes destroyed Rome and its civilisation, only the monks could read and write and they made beautiful illuminated manuscripts. All these monks were sworn to obedience, they would obey the head of the Church, the Pope in Rome, in all things. If the Pope had decreed that the earth was flat, then it was the duty of every monk and priest to believe that the earth was flat, and not only the monks but every peasant, knight, merchant or king had to believe it. Anybody who dared to think differently and to say so was called a heretic, and a heretic was usually burnt at the stake. The astronomer Galileo only saved himself from the stake by pretending he believed the sun goes round the earth.

幾個世紀以來，教會享有巨大的權力和特權。在中世紀早期，當 Germanic 部落摧毀 Rome 和它的文明時，只有修士能讀寫，他們製作了精美的彩繪手抄本。所有這些修士都宣誓服從，在一切事務上聽命於教會的首領——Rome 的教宗。如果教宗頒布法令說地球是平的，那麼每一位修士和教士的義務就是相信地球是平的，不僅是修士，每一個農民、騎士、商人或國王都必須相信。任何人膽敢有不同的想法並說出來，就被稱為異端，而異端通常會被燒死在火刑柱上。天文學家 Galileo 只是靠假裝相信太陽繞著地球轉，才免於被燒死。

But long before Galileo, there had been all kinds of heretics, people who dared to have their own ideas about Christ or about how one should worship God. As these ideas were not what the Pope wanted, these heretics had suffered persecution and death. In the opinion of the Church, only the Pope could know what everybody should think, whether it had to do with religion or science. To disagree with the Pope was a deadly sin, a crime punishable by death.

但早在 Galileo 之前很久，就已經有了各種各樣的異端分子——那些膽敢對 Christ 或如何崇拜上帝有自己想法的人。由於這些想法不是教宗所要的，這些異端分子遭受了迫害和死亡。在教會看來，只有教宗才能知道每個人應該想什麼，無論是關於宗教還是科學。與教宗意見不同是一種致命的罪，一種可以處死的罪行。

But the Church not only had power over minds. Over the centuries, kings and lords and rich men had made great gifts of land, gold and treasure to the Church. They believed that if they gave gifts to the Church, they would be rewarded in heaven. As a result, the monasteries, the bishops and the Pope had become incredibly wealthy.

但教會不僅掌控人們的思想。幾個世紀以來，國王、領主和富人們向教會獻上了大量的土地、黃金和珍寶。他們相信如果向教會獻禮，就會在天堂得到獎賞。結果，修道院、主教和教宗變得極其富有。

Some bishops had more land than the greatest lords, and the Pope had an immense wealth at his disposal. But all this wealth did not help to make good priests, and there were many who thought more about good food, drink and comforts than about serving God. That is why Francis of Assisi had founded a new order of monks, sworn to poverty and sworn to live without comfort. But after his death even his own monks went back to an easier, more comfortable life.

有些主教擁有的土地比最大的領主還多，教宗更是掌握著龐大的財富。但這些財富並無助於培養好的教士，許多人想的是美食、美酒和舒適享受，而不是服事上帝。這就是為什麼 Francis of Assisi 創立了一個新的修會，發誓守貧，發誓過沒有舒適的生活。但他死後，連他自己的修士們也回到了更輕鬆、更舒適的生活方式。

By the Renaissance, the Church as a whole had become as rotten as never before. The higher ranks, the bishops, the cardinals and the Pope, led lives that were a disgrace to the religion of Christ. At the time of Leonardo da Vinci, a man became Pope who can only be called a monster of evil. His name was Rodrigo de Borgia.

到了文藝復興時期，教會整體已經腐敗到前所未有的程度。高層——主教、樞機主教和教宗——過著令基督教蒙羞的生活。在 Leonardo da Vinci 的時代，一個只能被稱為邪惡怪物的人當上了教宗。他的名字是 Rodrigo de Borgia。

When he was still a bishop, Borgia was already known for wild drunken parties with his friends. Then the old pope died and the cardinals had to elect one of themselves as the new pope. Few of them would have considered voting for Borgia, but he bribed them with great sums of money and so he was elected as Pope Alexander VI.

當他還是主教的時候，Borgia 就已經因與朋友們舉辦狂野的酒宴而出名了。然後老教宗去世了，樞機主教們必須從他們當中選出一位新教宗。很少有人會考慮投票給 Borgia，但他用巨額金錢賄賂了他們，於是他當選為教宗 Alexander VI。

But then he wanted to get all that money back again. This was not really difficult, for when a bishop died it was up to the Pope to choose the new bishop, and there were men who were quite willing to pay large sums to the Pope for the privilege of becoming bishops. Every time a bishop died, Alexander sold the vacancy to the highest bidder.

但隨後他想把所有那些錢都賺回來。這其實不太困難，因為當一位主教去世時，由教宗來選擇新主教，而有些人非常樂意向教宗支付大筆金錢以獲得成為主教的特權。每當一位主教去世，Alexander 就把空缺賣給出價最高的人。

Unfortunately, the bishops did not die quickly enough for the needs of Pope Alexander, and so he found a way to speed up things. He used to invite a bishop to a banquet with excellent food, good wine and splendid entertainment. But the next day the guest did not feel very well, a few days later he was dead, and Alexander had another vacancy to sell.

不幸的是，主教們死得不夠快，不能滿足教宗 Alexander 的需要，所以他找到了加速的方法。他常常邀請一位主教赴宴，有精美的食物、上好的美酒和華麗的娛樂。但第二天客人就感覺不太舒服，幾天後他就死了，Alexander 又有了一個空缺可以出售。

In the streets of Rome people whispered of a secret poison that was in the possession of the Holy Father. One had to speak of such things in whispers as it was not safe to speak openly. A young Roman nobleman, Orsini, spoke openly against the Pope. A short time later he was found stabbed to death in a dark street. Everybody in Rome knew that the Pope had a gang of paid murderers ready to do his bidding.

在 Rome 的街頭，人們悄悄議論著一種掌握在教宗手中的祕密毒藥。這些事只能低聲說，因為公開談論是不安全的。一位年輕的 Roman 貴族 Orsini 公開反對教宗。不久之後他就被發現在一條陰暗的街道上被刺死了。Rome 的每個人都知道，教宗養著一幫拿錢辦事的殺手，隨時準備執行他的命令。

Money poured through Alexander's hands like water, and he always needed more. He thought of other ways of increasing his income. In those days people believed that the Pope could forgive sins on behalf of God. Someone who had committed a theft or even murder would fear that God would punish them for their crimes, but if the Pope gave them a pardon, then God would also forgive them.

金錢像水一樣從 Alexander 手中流過，他總是需要更多。他想到了其他增加收入的方法。在那個時代，人們相信教宗可以代替上帝赦免罪惡。一個犯了偷竊甚至謀殺罪的人會害怕上帝懲罰他們的罪行，但如果教宗赦免了他們，那麼上帝也會原諒他們。

Such a pardon by the Pope was called an 'indulgence'. It was a paper on which was written a pardon for a theft, or for a lie, or for murder. Alexander had the bright idea of selling these indulgences: people would pay so much for a lie, so much more for a theft and a still higher price for murder. Not only in Rome or in Italy, but all over Europe monks went about selling these indulgences, and people bought them. It was a great business that brought money flowing into the treasury of the Pope. But not all people agreed with this disgraceful business.

教宗的這種赦免被稱為「贖罪券」。那是一張紙，上面寫著對偷竊、說謊或謀殺的赦免。Alexander 想到了一個妙主意：出售這些贖罪券——說謊要付這麼多錢，偷竊要付更多錢，謀殺則要付更高的價格。不僅在 Rome 或 Italy，在整個 Europe，修士們到處兜售這些贖罪券，人們也買了。這是一門大生意，金錢源源不斷地流入教宗的國庫。但並非所有人都認同這種可恥的勾當。

In the city of Florence, a monk called Savonarola preached against the luxury and wealth that had brought all this evil. He even went so far as to call Alexander Borgia a devil in human shape. Savonarola was a wonderful preacher. He had the power to move the hearts of those who listened to him, and soon the rich citizens of Florence felt ashamed of their own luxury. They made bonfires on which they burnt their fine clothes. They dressed in dark simple garments, they gave up their fine food and lived on bread and olives, and they turned against Pope Alexander VI.

在 Florence 城，一位名叫 Savonarola 的修士大聲疾呼，反對那帶來一切邪惡的奢華與財富。他甚至大膽地稱 Alexander Borgia 為披著人皮的魔鬼。Savonarola 是一位了不起的佈道者。他有感動聽眾心靈的力量，很快，Florence 富裕的市民們就為自己的奢華感到羞恥了。他們生起篝火，把華美的衣服燒掉。他們穿上深色樸素的衣服，放棄精美的食物，靠麵包和橄欖過活，並且反對教宗 Alexander VI。

At first, Alexander tried to silence Savonarola through bribery, offering to make him a bishop. Savonarola scornfully refused. The Pope found other ways to deal with the stubborn monk. There were many priests in Florence who were against Savonarola, and, at the Pope's command, they spread all kinds of lies about him, saying he was in league with evil powers. After a time, when the people of Florence began to miss their good food and their fine clothes, they were also willing to believe these lies. Once Savonarola no longer had the support of the people of Florence, he was doomed. He was taken prisoner by the Pope's men, condemned to death as a heretic and burnt at the stake.

起初，Alexander 試圖用賄賂來讓 Savonarola 閉嘴，提出要他做主教。Savonarola 輕蔑地拒絕了。教宗找到了對付這個頑固修士的其他方法。Florence 有許多反對 Savonarola 的教士，在教宗的指使下，他們散佈了各種關於他的謊言，說他與邪惡力量勾結。過了一段時間，當 Florence 的人們開始想念他們的美食和華服時，他們也願意相信這些謊言了。一旦 Savonarola 失去了 Florence 人民的支持，他就注定了。他被教宗的人逮捕，以異端罪判處死刑，燒死在火刑柱上。

But the justice of God that Alexander had mocked for so long finally caught up with him. He had planned another poisoning of an elderly bishop. There was the usual banquet, and a cup with poisoned wine was ready. But this time the cup-bearer who served the wine to the guests had been bribed by the bishop who knew what was in store for him. At the last moment the cup-bearer switched the cups, so Alexander drank his own poison and died a painful death.

但 Alexander 長久以來嘲弄的上帝的正義終於追上了他。他策劃了又一次毒殺一位年邁主教的陰謀。照例有一場宴會，一杯下了毒的酒已經準備好了。但這一次，為客人斟酒的侍酒人被那位知道自己將遭何種命運的主教買通了。在最後一刻，侍酒人調換了杯子，Alexander 喝下了自己的毒酒，痛苦地死去了。

When the people of Rome heard of his end they celebrated and danced and sang in the streets for five days. At his funeral they spat at the coffin and shouted curses.

當 Rome 的人們聽到他的死訊，他們慶祝、跳舞、歌唱，連續在街上狂歡了五天。在他的葬禮上，他們對著棺材吐口水，大聲咒罵。

# 26. Martin Luther
# 26. Martin Luther

The story of Pope Alexander VI shows that this wonderful time of the Renaissance, the time when Leonardo painted the Last Supper and when Raphael painted his lovely Madonnas, was also the time when the highest ranks of the Church were filled with wicked men.

教宗 Alexander VI 的故事顯示，這個美妙的文藝復興時代——Leonardo 畫出《最後的晚餐》、Raphael 畫出他可愛的聖母像的時代——同時也是教會最高層充斥著邪惡之徒的時代。

Yet the power and authority of the Pope was still so great that a sincere priest, like Savonarola, paid with his life for speaking the truth. There were hundreds of thousands of people across Europe who felt like Savonarola. They looked with horror and shame at the sorry state of the Christian Church, and felt powerless to change things. But then a man came who challenged and, in the end, defied the power of the Pope, cardinals and bishops. He was a German citizen by the name of Martin Luther.

然而教宗的權力和威信仍然如此強大，以至於像 Savonarola 這樣真誠的教士，為說出真相付出了生命的代價。整個 Europe 有成千上萬的人和 Savonarola 有同感。他們驚恐而羞愧地看著基督教會的可悲狀態，卻感到無力改變。但後來有一個人出現了，他挑戰了、並最終公然違抗了教宗、樞機主教和主教的權力。他是一位名叫 Martin Luther 的 German 公民。

Martin Luther was born in 1483, the same year as Raphael, and thirty years after Leonardo. He came from a poor family. His father was a miner who worked in a copper mine, but this poor miner wanted his son to have a good education. The parents made great sacrifices for their son and lived modestly to enable him to study.

Martin Luther 於 1483 年出生，和 Raphael 同年，比 Leonardo 晚了三十年。他出身貧寒。他的父親是一名在銅礦工作的礦工，但這位貧窮的礦工希望兒子能受到良好的教育。父母為兒子做出了巨大的犧牲，過著簡樸的生活，讓他得以求學。

Young Luther was a clever boy and became a university student. Even then life was not easy for him. To earn some money after his lessons, Martin Luther, like many others, went through the streets from house to house singing. Sometimes a door would open and a kind person would either give him a few coppers or a plate of food. Yet young Luther worked hard at his studies and at the age of twenty-one he received his university degree.

年輕的 Luther 是個聰明的男孩，成了大學生。即便如此，他的生活也不輕鬆。為了在課後賺些錢，Martin Luther 和許多人一樣，挨家挨戶在街上唱歌。有時候一扇門會打開，一位好心人會給他幾個銅板或一盤食物。然而年輕的 Luther 刻苦學習，在二十一歲時取得了大學學位。

Then something happened that changed his whole life. He went for a long walk in the countryside with a friend. They started out in brilliant sunshine but later in the day clouds came up and the two friends were caught in a terrific thunderstorm. As they hurried to find a place of shelter there was a blinding flash of light, a loud booming sound, and Luther's friend fell lifeless to the ground. He had been killed by lightning.

接著發生了一件改變他一生的事。他和一位朋友到鄉間遠足。出發時陽光燦爛，但那天晚些時候烏雲密佈，兩個朋友被一場猛烈的雷暴困住了。當他們匆忙尋找避雨處時，一道刺眼的閃光、一聲巨響，Luther 的朋友倒在地上，一動不動。他被閃電擊死了。

From that day on a great change came over Luther. He asked himself again and again, 'Why was I spared? Why was my life not taken?' He became more and more convinced that God had spared his life for a purpose, and he decided to become a monk. In the monastery he would have liked to devote all his time to prayer and to the study of the Bible, but the abbot wanted him to preach sermons. Luther was afraid of giving a sermon, he was very modest and thought people would only laugh at him. But when he stood in the pulpit his fear of making a fool of himself disappeared. He spoke from his heart and all who heard him were deeply moved. In time, Luther even became famous as a preacher.

從那天起，Luther 身上發生了巨大的轉變。他一遍又一遍地問自己：「為什麼我被饒過了？為什麼我的生命沒有被奪走？」他越來越確信上帝饒了他的命是有目的的，於是他決定成為修士。在修道院裡，他本想把所有時間都用來禱告和研讀聖經，但院長要他講道。Luther 害怕講道，他非常謙遜，覺得人們只會嘲笑他。但當他站在講壇上時，出醜的恐懼就消失了。他發自內心地講話，所有聽到他的人都深受感動。漸漸地，Luther 甚至因為佈道而出了名。

When the monastery had to send somebody to Rome, to the Pope, the monks thought they could not send a better man than Martin Luther.

當修道院需要派人去 Rome 見教宗時，修士們覺得沒有比 Martin Luther 更合適的人選了。

When Luther came to Rome he was still a faithful son of the Church. For him, Rome was a holy city, and the Pope was the Holy Father. It was a great honour that he, a simple monk, the son of a miner, was going to meet this holy person, the Pope.

當 Luther 來到 Rome 時，他仍是教會忠實的兒子。對他而言，Rome 是一座神聖的城市，教宗是至聖的天父。他——一個普通的修士、一個礦工的兒子——將要見到教宗這位神聖的人物，這是莫大的榮耀。

But Pope Leo X was not a very holy man. His main ambition was to become famous for building the largest and most beautiful church in the world, St Peter's in Rome (where both Raphael and Michelangelo painted for him). But all this cost money and Leo was as ruthless as his predecessor Alexander VI when it came to getting money.

但教宗 Leo X 並不是一個多麼神聖的人。他的主要野心是因為建造世界上最大最美的教堂——Rome 的 St Peter's 大教堂（Raphael 和 Michelangelo 都曾在那裡為他作畫）——而名留青史。但這一切都需要錢，而 Leo 在斂財方面和他的前任 Alexander VI 一樣無情。

In Rome, Luther saw priests, bishops and cardinals who used their position only to enrich themselves. He saw a pope who sold high positions in the Church to anyone who paid well enough, and all this was a bitter disappointment. But Luther was, after all, a monk. He had sworn an oath of obedience, and so it still did not occur to him to say anything against the Pope. He returned to his monastery in Germany and kept his sorrow and disappointment to himself.

在 Rome，Luther 看到教士、主教和樞機主教們利用他們的職位只為中飽私囊。他看到教宗把教會的高位賣給任何出得起錢的人，這一切都是苦澀的失望。但 Luther 畢竟是一名修士。他宣過服從的誓言，所以還沒有想到要說任何反對教宗的話。他回到了他在 Germany 的修道院，把悲傷和失望埋在心裡。

The new pope needed vast sums of money to fulfil his ambition of building the most splendid church in the world. Alexander VI had found one excellent way of getting money by selling indulgences, selling people forgiveness for their sins. This shameful trade had stopped at his death, but now Pope Leo needed money to pay his architects and painters, and so he sent his 'travelling salesmen' into every country of Europe to sell indulgences. There were priests and monks selling forgiveness for any crime or sin.

新教宗需要巨額資金來實現他建造世上最華麗教堂的野心。Alexander VI 曾找到一個斂財的好辦法——出售贖罪券，向人們兜售罪的赦免。這種可恥的交易在他死後停止了，但現在教宗 Leo 需要錢來付給他的建築師和畫家，於是他把他的「流動推銷員」派往 Europe 各國去賣贖罪券。到處都有教士和修士在兜售對任何罪行或罪惡的赦免。

The priest-salesman sent to Germany was called Tetzel. He was an excellent businessman. Tetzel usually set up a little stall in the market place of a town. He then made a speech and, as he spoke well, more and more people came to listen to him. Tetzel told them what a terrible thing it was to offend God by laziness, by telling lies, by using bad language, and what a terrible punishment God would inflict on all sinners. He had his listeners thoroughly frightened (after all, few people in the world can be certain they have never done anything wrong) and when they were well and truly scared, Tetzel said: 'But, my dear friends, you need not fear God's wrath and punishment. If you come and buy one of these papers here, each one is an indulgence by the Holy Father in Rome. Whatever you have done is forgiven by God as soon as you have paid me for the indulgence.' People queued up to pay.

被派到 Germany 的教士推銷員叫 Tetzel。他是一個出色的生意人。Tetzel 通常在一個城鎮的市場上擺一個小攤位。然後他開始演講，因為他說得很好，越來越多的人來聽他說話。Tetzel 告訴他們，因懶惰、說謊、說粗話而冒犯上帝是多麼可怕的事，上帝會對所有罪人施加多麼可怕的懲罰。他把聽眾嚇得夠嗆（畢竟，世上很少有人能確定自己從未做過任何壞事），等他們被嚇得夠慘了，Tetzel 就說：「但是，親愛的朋友們，你們不必害怕上帝的震怒和懲罰。只要你們來這裡買一張這個，每一張都是 Rome 至聖天父的贖罪券。無論你們做了什麼，只要付了錢買了贖罪券，上帝就會原諒你們。」人們排起隊來付錢。

On one occasion, this clever salesman Tetzel was caught in his own trap. A knight came to him and said he wanted to buy an indulgence for a robbery. That was quite an expensive sin, and Tetzel was pleased to get a lot of money from this knight. The next day Tetzel made still more money and when he left this particular town to start business somewhere else again, he carried with him a well-filled cash box. He was riding on a lonely road when, suddenly, armed men appeared, knocked him down and took his cash box.

有一次，這位聰明的推銷員 Tetzel 掉進了自己的陷阱。一位騎士來找他，說要買一張搶劫罪的贖罪券。那可是一項相當昂貴的罪，Tetzel 很高興從這位騎士那裡拿到了大筆的錢。第二天 Tetzel 又賺了更多錢，當他離開這個城鎮去另一個地方繼續做生意時，他帶著一個裝得滿滿的錢箱。他騎馬走在一條僻靜的路上，突然，武裝的人出現了，把他打倒在地，搶走了他的錢箱。

'You sinners!' cried Tetzel. 'God will punish you for robbing a priest, the messenger of His Holiness, the Pope!'

「你們這些罪人！」Tetzel 叫道。「上帝會懲罰你們搶劫教士——教宗陛下的使者！」

'No, he won't,' said the leader of the gang, and he drew from his pocket the indulgence he had bought the day before from Tetzel.

「不，他不會的，」這幫人的頭目說著，從口袋裡掏出他前一天向 Tetzel 買的那張贖罪券。

Still this misfortune did not stop Tetzel and many other priests sent from Rome. They went from town to town, village to village, selling indulgences and earning money for the Pope and his ambitions.

但這次不幸並沒有阻止 Tetzel 和 Rome 派出的其他許多教士。他們從一個城鎮到另一個城鎮、從一個村莊到另一個村莊，販賣贖罪券，為教宗和他的野心賺錢。

Martin Luther had kept silent about his disappointment, about all the wickedness he had seen in Rome. But when these indulgences were sold like pills for headaches in every market square of Germany, he could not remain silent. He could not stand by and see people cheated in the name of God and the Christian Church.

Martin Luther 一直對他的失望、對他在 Rome 看到的所有邪惡保持沉默。但當這些贖罪券像頭痛藥一樣在 Germany 的每一個市場廣場上出售時，他再也無法沉默了。他不能袖手旁觀，看著人們以上帝和基督教會的名義被欺騙。

He preached openly against this shameful trade. He wrote down ninety-five reasons why these indulgences were against anything in the Bible, and he nailed them to the door of his church in Wittenberg so that people could read them. People came and copied these reasons, and the copies soon spread all over Germany. Once people had read Luther's arguments against the indulgences the whole trade in these papers came to a stop.

他公開講道反對這種可恥的交易。他寫下了九十五條理由，說明為什麼這些贖罪券違反了聖經的一切教導，並把它們釘在他在 Wittenberg 教堂的門上，讓人們閱讀。人們來了，抄下了這些理由，抄本很快傳遍了整個 Germany。一旦人們讀了 Luther 反對贖罪券的論證，整個贖罪券交易就停擺了。

# 27. Luther and the Reformation
# 27. Luther 與宗教改革

If it had not been for the stroke of lightning that killed his friend but left Luther unharmed, Luther might not have become a monk. He might perhaps have been a lawyer, and even as a lawyer he would have been against the shameful trade in indulgences, although people would hardly have paid much attention to his opinions. But Luther spoke against the indulgences as a priest, a famous preacher who had been to Rome and had seen the Pope. If such a man as Luther called the selling of indulgences a cheat and a swindle, then he must be right, and one could not simply 'buy' God's forgiveness by paying for a piece of paper. Luther's words had such a great effect because he was a priest. So the stroke of lightning that made Luther become a monk was of great importance. Without it, none of the things that now happened might have come to pass.

如果不是那道閃電擊死了他的朋友而讓 Luther 安然無恙，Luther 也許不會成為修士。他也許會成為一名律師，即使作為律師，他也會反對那可恥的贖罪券交易，但人們大概不會太在意他的意見。然而 Luther 是以一名教士、一位曾到過 Rome 並見過教宗的著名佈道者的身分，來反對贖罪券的。如果像 Luther 這樣的人都說賣贖罪券是騙局和詐騙，那他一定是對的，人們不能僅僅靠付錢買一張紙就「買到」上帝的赦免。Luther 的話能產生如此大的影響，正是因為他是一名教士。所以那道讓 Luther 成為修士的閃電至關重要。沒有它，後來發生的一切也許都不會發生。

Copies of Luther's arguments against indulgences spread all over Germany. Because they were the words of a greatly respected priest, people in Germany simply stopped buying these bits of paper. As a result, Pope Leo X lost a large part of the money he had expected to receive.

Luther 反對贖罪券的論證抄本傳遍了整個 Germany。因為那是一位深受尊敬的教士所說的話，Germany 的人們乾脆不再購買這些紙片了。結果，教宗 Leo X 失去了他原本預期收到的大筆金錢。

The Pope was angry and he sent a letter to Martin Luther commanding him to come to Rome immediately. But Luther, remembering what had happened to Savonarola, was not going to Italy at all.

教宗怒了，他寫了一封信給 Martin Luther，命令他立即前往 Rome。但 Luther 想起了 Savonarola 的遭遇，根本不打算去 Italy。

By now he was not just a lonely monk who stood against the Pope on his own. Thousands of people in Germany, who had been very unhappy about the greed and the wickedness of the popes, had been waiting for someone to take the lead. Luther was the right man and they all supported him. What all these people wanted was a complete change in the Church. The old form of the Church, with the Pope as head and highest authority, should be re-shaped, re-formed. As a little snowball rolling downhill becomes a great avalanche, so the argument between Luther and the Pope grew into a large movement of hearts and souls that was called the Reformation.

此時他已不再是一個孤身對抗教宗的孤獨修士。成千上萬的 Germany 人，長久以來對教宗們的貪婪和邪惡深感不滿，一直在等待有人站出來領頭。Luther 就是那個對的人，他們都支持他。所有這些人想要的，是教會的徹底改變。舊的教會形式——以教宗為首和最高權威——應該被重新塑造、重新改革。就像一個小雪球從山坡上滾下來變成巨大的雪崩一樣，Luther 與教宗之間的爭論成長為一場聲勢浩大的心靈與靈魂運動，被稱為宗教改革。

Having so many supporters, Luther not only refused to go to Rome, but he also wrote a short book in which he said that there was nothing in the Bible to show that anybody owed obedience to the Pope, and that the Pope was a servant of the devil not of God.

有了這麼多支持者，Luther 不僅拒絕前往 Rome，還寫了一本小書，書中他說聖經裡沒有任何內容表明任何人應該服從教宗，教宗是魔鬼的僕人而不是上帝的僕人。

In response to Luther's book, the Pope sent a message to the town of Wittenberg where Luther lived. The message declared that Martin Luther was a heretic. He was no longer a priest nor was he even a Christian, and so he should not be allowed to enter a church or take part in any service. No good Christian should have anything to do with him.

作為對 Luther 這本書的回應，教宗向 Luther 居住的 Wittenberg 城發了一道諭令。諭令宣布 Martin Luther 是異端。他不再是教士，甚至不再是基督徒，因此不應允許他進入教堂或參加任何儀式。任何好的基督徒都不應與他有任何來往。

In earlier times such a command by the Pope would have meant the end of Luther. But by now there was a different spirit. The whole town of Wittenberg sided with Luther.

在更早的時代，教宗的這樣一道命令就意味著 Luther 的末日。但如今時代精神已經不同了。整個 Wittenberg 城都站在 Luther 這一邊。

Luther called the citizens of Wittenberg together and spoke to them with a power that moved them all deeply. He declared that he did not want to remain a priest in a Church ruled by such a wicked person as the Pope. From now on, he was the minister of a new Church, a Church that owed no obedience to the Pope and which had no master but God. The people cheered and made a big bonfire onto which they threw the Pope's letter and a good many other books that had been written against Martin Luther.

Luther 把 Wittenberg 的市民們召集在一起，以一種深深感動所有人的力量向他們講話。他宣布他不願繼續做一個由教宗這樣邪惡之人統治的教會的教士。從現在起，他是一個新教會的牧師，這個教會不服從教宗，除了上帝之外沒有任何主人。人們歡呼著生起一堆大篝火，把教宗的信和許多反對 Martin Luther 的書都扔進火裡。

This bonfire in the German town of Wittenberg was an important event in history, for it was the beginning of the Reformation, the beginning of the great rebellion against the Pope from which came later all the other Churches and communities that do not recognise the Pope's authority. This bonfire was kindled in the year 1520, one year after Leonardo's death and less than thirty years after the discovery of America.

這堆在 German 小鎮 Wittenberg 燃起的篝火是歷史上的一個重要事件，因為它標誌著宗教改革的開端，標誌著反對教宗的大叛變的開始，後來所有不承認教宗權威的教會和團體都由此而來。這堆篝火點燃於 1520 年，Leonardo 去世後一年，美洲被發現後不到三十年。

Pope Leo X had failed to crush Luther, but he was not going to let this dangerous rebel get away with it. The Pope now turned to the ruler of Germany, Charles V, and asked him to deal with Luther.

教宗 Leo X 未能壓制 Luther，但他不打算讓這個危險的叛逆者逍遙法外。教宗現在轉向 Germany 的統治者 Charles V，請求他來處理 Luther。

Charles V was a very remarkable person. He was the most powerful man of his time, and it was quite true what people said of him: that in his dominions the sun never set.

Charles V 是一個非常了不起的人物。他是當時世界上最有權勢的人，人們對他所說的確實不假：在他的領土上，太陽永不落下。

His father, Maximilian, had been emperor of Germany and Austria; Belgium and Holland were also part of his empire. Charles V's father was already very powerful, then Charles married the daughter of Ferdinand and Isabella of Spain who had no other children. Through this marriage, after Ferdinand's death, Charles V also became king of Spain. It was he, Charles V, who gave Magellan the ships to sail round the world. Apart from all the European countries that Charles ruled - Germany, Austria, Spain, Belgium, Holland - he was also the ruler of the rich Spanish colonies in America, as well as colonies in the East Indies.

他的父親 Maximilian 曾是 Germany 和 Austria 的皇帝；Belgium 和 Holland 也是他帝國的一部分。Charles V 的父親已經非常強大了，然後 Charles 娶了 Spain 的 Ferdinand 和 Isabella 的女兒——他們沒有其他孩子。通過這樁婚姻，在 Ferdinand 死後，Charles V 也成為了 Spain 的國王。正是他——Charles V——給了 Magellan 船隻去環遊世界。除了 Charles 統治的所有 European 國家——Germany、Austria、Spain、Belgium、Holland——他還是 America 富裕的 Spanish 殖民地以及 East Indies 殖民地的統治者。

So it is quite true that the sun never set on the empire of Charles V, for when the sun sets in Austria, it rises in Peru, and when setting in Peru it rises in the East Indies.

所以太陽確實永不在 Charles V 的帝國上落下，因為當太陽在 Austria 落下時，它在 Peru 升起；當它在 Peru 落下時，又在 East Indies 升起。

This mighty ruler, Emperor Charles V, was asked by Pope Leo to deal with that rebellious German monk, Martin Luther. The emperor was a fair-minded person, however. He did not want to do anything against Luther without giving him a chance to defend himself. There was also another reason to be careful. Charles V knew that a great many people in Germany - powerful lords, learned men, simple peasants, generals and common soldiers - were all in sympathy with Luther. Charles V was too clever a man to stir up trouble if he could help it. Luther should have a fair chance to speak for himself.

這位強大的統治者——Charles V 皇帝——被教宗 Leo 請求去對付那個叛逆的 German 修士 Martin Luther。但是皇帝是一個公正的人。他不想在沒有給 Luther 為自己辯護的機會的情況下對他採取行動。還有另一個需要謹慎的原因。Charles V 知道 Germany 有非常多的人——強大的領主、學者、普通農民、將軍和普通士兵——都同情 Luther。Charles V 太聰明了，能避免麻煩就不會去惹事。Luther 應該得到一個公正的機會為自己說話。
