Charles V called a meeting of princes and noblemen, of cardinals and bishops, all the great and powerful men of Germany. Luther was also summoned to appear before this gathering and to defend himself. He was promised 'safe conduct', which means that whatever was decided at this meeting, Luther would be allowed to return to his loyal town of Wittenberg.

Charles V 召集了一次會議，邀請了王公貴族、樞機主教和主教們，Germany 所有偉大而有權勢的人物。Luther 也被傳喚到這次集會面前為自己辯護。他被承諾了「安全通行權」，意思是無論這次會議做出什麼決定，Luther 都被允許返回他忠誠的 Wittenberg 城。

So this monk, the son of a miner, was to come before the most powerful people of his time, including the mighty emperor, Charles V.

就這樣，這位修士——一個礦工的兒子——將要面對他所處時代最有權勢的人物，包括強大的皇帝 Charles V。
# 28. The Diet of Worms
# 28. Worms 帝國議會

Emperor Charles V's assembly of lords and noblemen was called a 'diet',
and the city where this diet was to meet was a German city called Worms.
So this important assembly is called the Diet of Worms, which sounds
funny, but it was not funny for Martin Luther.

Charles V 皇帝召集的貴族和諸侯大會被稱為「diet」（帝國議會），而這次議會召開的城市是一個叫 Worms 的德國城市。所以這次重要的集會被稱為 Diet of Worms（Worms 帝國議會），聽起來很滑稽，但對 Martin Luther 來說一點也不好笑。

There are many kinds of courage: the courage of a soldier going into
battle or courage to own up if one has done something wrong. It needed a special kind of courage to walk alone, like Luther, into a great
assembly and to defend himself before the high and mighty lords of Germany and the emperor himself.

勇氣有許多種：士兵上戰場的勇氣，或者做錯事後坦承的勇氣。但像 Luther 那樣獨自一人走進一個盛大的集會，在 Germany 位高權重的諸侯和皇帝本人面前為自己辯護，則需要一種特殊的勇氣。

When Luther approached the doors of the assembly hall, one of the
soldiers on guard patted him on the shoulder and said: 'I've gone into
many a battle without fear, but I would not like to be in your shoes, little
monk! Then the doors opened and Luther entered the great hall. At the
back of the hall on a high throne sat the emperor, Charles V. To one side
of the throne stood a Roman cardinal in his crimson robe, the Pope's
envoy. Five thousand people thronged the hall: lords and knights in their
colourful clothes, lawyers and learned men dressed in black, bishops,
priests and monks. When Luther walked in, this great crowd fell silent
and all eyes turned to this monk in his dark-brown habit.

當 Luther 走近議會大廳的大門時，一名守衛的士兵拍了拍他的肩膀說：「我上過許多次戰場都毫不畏懼，但我可不想跟你換位子，小修士！」然後大門打開了，Luther 走進了宏偉的大廳。大廳後方高高的寶座上坐著皇帝 Charles V。寶座一側站著一位身穿緋紅長袍的羅馬樞機主教——教宗的特使。五千人擠滿了大廳：穿著華麗衣服的領主和騎士，身著黑衣的律師和學者，主教、神父和修士。當 Luther 走進來時，這一大群人頓時安靜下來，所有的目光都轉向了這位穿著深棕色僧袍的修士。

Luther walked through the crowd until he faced the Roman cardinal.
And now, while all these thousands listened, the questioning began.
The Roman cardinal, the Pope's ambassador, fired questions at Luther,
questions that were meant to trip him up or to show his ignorance.
These questions went on and on. Except for short breaks at mealtimes,
the questioning lasted all day and went on into the next. The purpose of
this long argument was to make Luther admit that he was wrong and
the Pope right.

Luther 穿過人群，直到面對那位羅馬樞機主教。就在這數千人傾聽之際，質詢開始了。羅馬樞機主教——教宗的大使——向 Luther 連珠炮似地發問，那些問題意在讓他自相矛盾或暴露他的無知。質問沒完沒了。除了用餐時的短暫休息，質詢持續了一整天，又延續到了第二天。這場漫長辯論的目的是要 Luther 承認他錯了，而教宗是對的。

But at the end of it all, when the cardinal had no more questions,
Luther said words that have become famous in history: I will not take
back anything I have said for this would be against my conscience. Here I
stand; I can do no other. God help me, amen.'

但在一切結束之時，當樞機主教再沒有問題可問了，Luther 說出了在歷史上流傳至今的名言：「我不會收回我說過的任何一句話，因為這將違背我的良心。我站在這裡，別無選擇。願上帝幫助我，阿門。」

Emperor Charles V had promised Luther safe conduct, and so, when
Luther had said these words with a ringing voice, he was allowed to
leave the assembly and set out on his journey home to Wittenberg.

Charles V 皇帝已承諾給 Luther 安全通行權，因此當 Luther 以響亮的聲音說出這些話後，他被允許離開議會，踏上回 Wittenberg 的歸途。

Luther was still on his way when Charles V made it known that, after
having listened to that long discussion, he had come to a decision. The
decision was that Luther was in the wrong, that Luther was a heretic and
that he was an outlaw. If a man was declared an outlaw, it meant that he
was no longer protected by any law, and that he could be killed by anyone without fear of punishment.

Luther 還在路上時，Charles V 就宣布了他在聽完那場漫長辯論後做出的決定。決定是：Luther 是錯的，Luther 是異端，而且他是法外之徒。如果一個人被宣布為法外之徒，就意味著他不再受到任何法律的保護，任何人都可以殺他而不必擔心受罰。

Now that Luther was an outlaw his life was no longer safe. But he had
friends in Germany, people who were on his side, and they helped him to
go into hiding. Luther found shelter in a castle called the Wartburg
where he was safe from his enemies.

既然 Luther 成了法外之徒，他的生命就不再安全了。但他在 Germany 有朋友，有站在他那一邊的人，他們幫助他躲藏起來。Luther 在一座名叫 Wartburg 的城堡找到了庇護，在那裡他安全無虞。

While Luther was in hiding in this castle, he began a great task: the
translation of the Bible into German. Up to that time, the Bible was only
for educated people who knew Latin - the Church did not want everyone to be able to read the Bible. There was no Bible in German or English or French, there were only some stories from the Bible that people
could hear from priests. Some men who had tried to translate the Bible
into their own language had risked their life doing so.

Luther 藏身在這座城堡時，他開始了一項偉大的工作：將《聖經》翻譯成德文。在那之前，《聖經》只屬於懂拉丁文的受過教育的人——教會不希望每個人都能讀《聖經》。沒有德文、英文或法文的《聖經》，只有一些《聖經》故事是人們可以從神父那裡聽到的。一些試圖將《聖經》翻譯成自己語言的人，為此冒著生命危險。

But Luther, as a German, wanted all his people, not only those who
knew Latin, to be able to read the Bible. So he used the time he was
hiding in the Wartburg to make a translation. This was not an easy task.
Even now, learned people disagree on how many parts of the Bible
should be translated. There is a strange story about what happened to
Luther when he was translating the Bible at the Wartburg.

但 Luther 身為一個 German 人，希望他所有的同胞——不只是那些懂拉丁文的人——都能讀到《聖經》。所以他利用藏身 Wartburg 的時間進行翻譯。這不是一件容易的事。即使到了今天，學者們對於《聖經》的多少部分應該被翻譯仍然意見不一。有一個關於 Luther 在 Wartburg 翻譯《聖經》時發生的奇異故事。

He was always a hard worker, poring over his translation deep into the
night. Perhaps he fell asleep over his work and only dreamed what he
saw, but one night it seemed to him that the light of his candle grew very
dim. A strange cold wind came from nowhere and made him shudder,
and at the same time an unpleasant stench assailed his nose. Luther,
who had not lifted his head from his writing, now looked up and saw before him a dark shape, like a shadow, but a shadow with bat's wings and
horns. This black shape placed a dark, claw-like hand over Luther's writing, as if it wanted to stop him from going on with it. But Luther, as you
have seen on other occasions, was not easily frightened. He was only
angry that there was something that interfered with his work. He took
the inkpot from his desk and threw it at the dark shape. As the glass
shattered on the wall, the dark shape, the stench and the cold air disappeared in an instant. All that remained was a big splash of ink on the wall.

他一向是個勤奮的工作者，深夜仍在埋頭翻譯。也許他在工作中睡著了，只是夢到了他所看見的一切，但有一天夜裡，他覺得蠟燭的光變得非常昏暗。一股不知從何而來的陰冷寒風讓他不禁打了個寒顫，同時一股難聞的惡臭撲鼻而來。Luther 一直沒有從寫作中抬起頭來，但此時他抬頭一看，面前出現了一個黑暗的身影，像一個影子，但是一個長著蝙蝠翅膀和角的影子。這個黑色的形體將一隻黑暗的、爪子般的手放在 Luther 的稿紙上，彷彿想阻止他繼續寫下去。但 Luther，正如你在其他場合看到的那樣，不是一個容易被嚇倒的人。他只是對有東西干擾他的工作感到憤怒。他從書桌上拿起墨水瓶，朝那個黑暗的形體擲去。當玻璃在牆上碎裂的瞬間，那個黑暗的形體、惡臭和冷空氣都在一瞬間消失了。剩下的只有牆上一大片墨漬。

The Wartburg castle where Luther translated the Bible into German
still stands, and visitors who go there can still see the ink blot on the wall
made by Luther when he threw the inkpot at the devil.

Luther 翻譯《聖經》的 Wartburg 城堡至今仍然屹立，前去參觀的遊客仍然可以看到 Luther 向魔鬼擲墨水瓶時留在牆上的墨漬。

After a year, Luther was able to leave the Wartburg, for the emperor
was fighting a war against France and had no time to bother about a
troublesome monk.

一年之後，Luther 得以離開 Wartburg，因為皇帝正在跟法國打仗，無暇顧及一個麻煩的修士。

Luther returned to Wittenberg where his friends received him with
joy. He could now work for the new kind of Church he had in mind: a free
Church, independent of the Pope, independent of Rome. The new kind
of Church was called Protestant, for the people who joined it protested
against the shameful practices of Rome.

Luther 回到了 Wittenberg，朋友們歡欣鼓舞地迎接他。他現在可以為他心中構想的新教會而努力了：一個自由的教會，獨立於教宗，獨立於 Rome。這種新的教會被稱為「新教」（Protestant），因為加入它的人們抗議（protest）羅馬可恥的做法。

Luther took one more step away from the customs of the Roman
Catholic Church. There was nothing in the Bible that said priests should
not marry. It was a rule that had been made by Pope Gregory the Great.
As the rules of popes did not count any longer for Luther, he put away
his monk's habit and married.

Luther 又向遠離羅馬天主教會的習俗邁出了一步。《聖經》裡沒有任何地方說神父不能結婚。這是教宗 Gregory 大帝制定的規則。既然教宗的規則對 Luther 來說已不再有效，他脫下了僧袍，結了婚。

All his life Luther hoped that the great movement that had begun
would not lead to bloodshed. He died at the age of sixty-three and so did
not see the massacres and wars that the Reformation brought about.

Luther 一生都希望他開啟的這場偉大運動不會導致流血。他在六十三歲時去世，因此沒有看到宗教改革所引發的屠殺和戰爭。
# 29. Calvin and Knox
# 29. Calvin 與 Knox

Luther was not alone in challenging the authority of the Pope. Many thousands of people took his side who felt that the Church of Rome was no longer a true Church of Christ. These people supported Luther. But there were others who did not agree with Luther. They knew, just as Luther did, that there were evil popes. They knew that the selling of indulgences was a shame and a disgrace for the Church. Yet these educated people were more worried about Luther than about the evil popes. They said: 'Yes, there is much that needs changing in the Church, much that is wrong that must be put right. But this change should be made by good men who work within the Church, good men who are bishops and cardinals, and who might one day become popes. If rebels like Martin Luther break away from the Church and start a Church of their own, there will be no end of it. There will be all kinds of troublemakers, each one starting their own Church. They will argue among themselves and it will only bring trouble and suffering. It would be far better if we all remained faithful sons and daughters of one Church, but make it a better Church than it is now.'

Luther 並非唯一挑戰教宗權威的人。成千上萬的人站在他那一邊，他們覺得羅馬教會已不再是真正的基督教會。這些人支持 Luther。但也有人不同意 Luther。他們和 Luther 一樣清楚，曾經有過邪惡的教宗；他們知道販售贖罪券是教會的恥辱與醜聞。然而這些有學識的人比起邪惡的教宗，更擔心 Luther 帶來的後果。他們說：「是的，教會裡有許多需要改變的事，有許多錯誤必須糾正。但這種改變應該由教會內部的好人來推動——好的主教、好的樞機主教，他們有朝一日可能成為教宗。如果像 Martin Luther 這樣的叛逆者脫離教會、自立門戶，那就永無止境了。各種搗亂者都會出現，每個人都要建立自己的教會。他們會彼此爭論不休，只會帶來麻煩和苦難。如果我們都留在同一個教會裡，做忠誠的兒女，但把它變成一個更好的教會，那豈不是好得多？」

That is why these people did not support Luther, for they did not want this breaking up of one Church into many. They foresaw that great suffering would follow from it. But they had no power and neither side was ready to listen to them. As a result, the terrible events that they had foreseen came to pass.

正因如此，這些人不支持 Luther，因為他們不希望一個教會分裂成許多個。他們預見到這將帶來巨大的苦難。但他們沒有權力，而且雙方都不願意聽他們的話。結果，他們所預見的可怕事態果然發生了。

Once Luther had shown that it was possible to defy the Pope and the Reformation had started, there came other 'reformers' who were not only against the Pope but against Luther and against each other. Before the Reformation there had, at least, been only one man who claimed to know the will of God; now there were many. Each of these reformers had supporters and followers who formed a Church of their own, and all these different 'reformed' Churches were at loggerheads with the Church of Rome and with each other.

一旦 Luther 證明了反抗教宗是可能的，宗教改革也由此展開，便出現了其他的「改革者」——他們不僅反對教宗，也反對 Luther，還互相對立。在宗教改革之前，至少只有一個人聲稱知道上帝的旨意；如今卻有了許多人。每位改革者都有自己的支持者和追隨者，各自成立自己的教會，而這些不同的「改革」教會不僅與羅馬教會對立，彼此之間也互相敵視。

One of these reformers was a Frenchman, John Calvin. Like Luther he was first a priest of the Roman Catholic Church, and like Luther he was upset by the evil ways of the popes. When Calvin heard of the great changes in Germany, when he heard how Luther had succeeded against Rome, Calvin also left the Church of Rome and preached against it. But his own country, France, was ruled by King Francis who had no patience with heretics, and Calvin had to flee for his life. He went to Switzerland where he found a city that welcomed him: the city of Geneva.

其中一位改革者是法國人 John Calvin。和 Luther 一樣，他起初也是羅馬天主教的神父，同樣對教宗的邪惡行徑感到憤慨。當 Calvin 聽聞德意志發生的巨變，聽聞 Luther 如何成功對抗了羅馬教廷，Calvin 也離開了羅馬教會，開始公開反對它。但他的祖國法國由 Francis 國王統治，這位國王對異端毫無容忍，Calvin 只得逃命。他去了瑞士，在那裡找到了一座歡迎他的城市：Geneva。

After a short time, the citizens of Geneva made Calvin a kind of ruler whose word was law. What he wished and what he said was law in Geneva, and life in Geneva was not easy under Calvin.

不久之後，Geneva 的市民讓 Calvin 成為一種統治者，他的話就是法律。在 Geneva，他所希望的、所說的就是法律，而在 Calvin 治下的 Geneva 生活並不輕鬆。

Like Savonarola, he thought that luxury, vanity and comfort made people evil, and so the people of Geneva had to do without anything that was not absolutely necessary for life. The colourful clothes people used to have in those days were forbidden, only plain black was allowed. Dancing, drinking wine and playing cards were also banned. Not only that, but art was also seen as a kind of luxury, so the churches had to be quite plain without pictures, statues or stained-glass windows. Any amusement or entertainment was an unnecessary luxury and so was outlawed. If the people of Geneva broke these rules a number of times they were executed. John Calvin's Church was a very stern one.

和 Savonarola 一樣，他認為奢華、虛榮和安逸會使人墮落，因此 Geneva 的人民必須捨棄一切非生活所絕對必需的東西。那個年代人們常穿的色彩繽紛的衣服被禁止了，只准穿素黑色的衣服。跳舞、飲酒和打牌也遭到禁止。不僅如此，藝術也被視為一種奢侈，所以教堂必須非常樸素，不得有繪畫、雕像或彩繪玻璃窗。任何娛樂消遣都是不必要的奢侈，因此一律被取締。如果 Geneva 的人民多次違反這些規定，就會被處死。John Calvin 的教會是非常嚴厲的。

In Scotland, too, the time was ripe for change. The bishops owned more than half of the country's wealth and the monks were so corrupt that you could hear anywhere in Scotland songs that mocked the sinful lives of the priests. Yet who would dare speak against the Pope? Scotland was not Germany, and the king of Scotland, James V, would not allow any heretics. If you had been in the town of St Andrews in 1528, you would have seen a bonfire that was quite different from the bonfire in Wittenberg. In this bonfire in St Andrews a young Scotsman, Patrick Hamilton, was burned.

在 Scotland，變革的時機也已成熟。主教們擁有全國一半以上的財富，修道士們腐敗至極，在 Scotland 各地都能聽到嘲諷神父罪惡生活的歌謠。然而誰敢公然反對教宗呢？Scotland 不是德意志，Scotland 國王 James 五世不會容許任何異端。如果你在 1528 年來到 St Andrews 鎮，你會看到一場與 Wittenberg 的那場火焰截然不同的篝火。在這場 St Andrews 的火焰中，一個年輕的蘇格蘭人 Patrick Hamilton 被活活燒死了。

Patrick Hamilton had been to Germany and he had heard of Luther and the new Church that Luther had founded, a Church free of Rome. Patrick Hamilton thought this was wonderful and he came back to Scotland and began to preach - but not for long. He paid for his preaching at the stake in St Andrews.

Patrick Hamilton 曾到過德意志，聽聞了 Luther 和他所創立的新教會——一個脫離了羅馬的教會。Patrick Hamilton 認為這太美好了，於是他回到 Scotland 開始佈道——但沒有持續多久。他在 St Andrews 的火刑柱上為自己的佈道付出了生命的代價。

But Patrick Hamilton's death did not stop the new ideas that were sweeping over Europe. The number of Protestants in Scotland grew, in spite of persecutions and burnings. They even began to fight back. One day a group of Protestants stormed St Andrew's castle and took Cardinal Beaton, who had been their worst oppressor, and hanged him from the window of the castle.

但 Patrick Hamilton 的死並沒有阻止席捲歐洲的新思想。儘管遭受迫害和火刑，Scotland 的新教徒人數仍在增長。他們甚至開始反擊。有一天，一群新教徒攻入了 St Andrews 城堡，抓住了他們最殘暴的壓迫者 Cardinal Beaton，把他從城堡的窗戶吊了出去。

Both sides, the Roman Catholics and the Protestants, fought and killed each other in the name of religion, and forgot that Christ had said: 'Love your enemy!'

雙方——天主教徒和新教徒——都以宗教之名互相爭鬥、互相殺戮，忘記了基督曾說：「要愛你的仇敵！」

The Scots had always been good friends with the French, and so James V called for French ships to help him against the rebellious Protestants of St Andrews. The rebellion was suppressed and there was harsh punishment for the Protestants. One of them was taken to France and condemned to be a galley-slave chained to an oar under the heavy whip of the overseer, rowing with other poor wretches on a French ship. The name of this Protestant sufferer was John Knox. After eighteen months of this terrible life as a galley-slave, he escaped and made his way to Switzerland, to Geneva.

蘇格蘭人向來與法國人交好，因此 James 五世召來法國船隊協助對付 St Andrews 叛亂的新教徒。叛亂被鎮壓了，新教徒受到了嚴厲的懲罰。其中一人被帶到法國，被判為划槳奴隸，鐵鏈鎖在船槳上，在監工的重鞭下與其他可憐人一同在法國船上划槳。這位新教受難者的名字是 John Knox。在經歷了十八個月這種可怕的划槳奴隸生活後，他逃了出來，一路前往瑞士的 Geneva。

That is how John Knox met John Calvin, the stern ruler of Geneva. John Knox agreed with Calvin and thought that Scotland should have the same kind of Church and life as Calvin had established in Geneva. He was so enthusiastic about this idea that he returned to Scotland despite the persecutions of Protestants.

就這樣，John Knox 遇見了 Geneva 那位嚴厲的統治者 John Calvin。John Knox 贊同 Calvin 的理念，認為 Scotland 應該擁有和 Calvin 在 Geneva 建立的那樣的教會和生活方式。他對這個理想如此熱忱，以至於不顧新教徒遭受的迫害，毅然回到了 Scotland。

By now, not only common people, but even noblemen and lords took the sides of the Protestants. They made a 'covenant', a pledge to help each other and do all they could for the new faith. So many people joined the covenant that the king could no longer suppress it. John Knox, who was also a great preacher, brought more and more people to his side. He became the leader of the Covenanters, and in the year 1560 he had the great satisfaction that the kind of Church he wanted, a Church as severe as Calvin's, was declared the Church of Scotland. After much bloodshed, burning and suffering, Scotland had broken away from Rome and had its own Church.

到了這時，不僅是平民百姓，甚至貴族和領主也站到了新教徒這一邊。他們締結了一份「盟約」，誓言彼此扶持，為新信仰竭盡所能。加入盟約的人如此之多，國王再也無法壓制了。John Knox 同時也是一位了不起的佈道家，他吸引了越來越多的人加入他的陣營。他成為盟約者們的領袖，而在 1560 年，他終於如願以償：他所期望的那種教會——一個和 Calvin 的教會一樣嚴厲的教會——被宣布為 Scotland 的國教。在經歷了無數的流血、火刑和苦難之後，Scotland 終於脫離了羅馬，擁有了自己的教會。

Under the influence of John Knox, pictures, statues and stained-glass windows in Scottish churches were destroyed, and entertainments were abolished. But Knox did not execute people for disobeying his rules as Calvin had done. He also had education very much at heart. Due to John Knox, Scotland became the only country at that time where even the children of the poor could go to school and have an education.

在 John Knox 的影響下，蘇格蘭教堂中的繪畫、雕像和彩繪玻璃窗都被摧毀了，娛樂活動也被廢除了。但 Knox 不像 Calvin 那樣，因為人民違反規定就處以死刑。他也非常重視教育。正因為 John Knox，Scotland 成為當時唯一一個連窮人的孩子都能上學接受教育的國家。

As it was with many reformers, there are things one can like in John Knox but also things that one can dislike.

正如許多改革者一樣，John Knox 身上有令人欣賞的地方，也有令人不以為然的地方。

# 30. Henry VIII
# 30. Henry 八世

The Reformation was, first of all, another expression of the change in the human mind that we have already seen in the various inventions and voyages of discovery, in Copernicus with his new idea about the sun and the earth, and in the Renaissance painters and the use of perspective in painting.

宗教改革首先是人類心靈變革的又一個表現，我們已經在各種發明和探險航行中見識過這種變革，在 Copernicus 關於太陽和地球的新觀念中見識過，在文藝復興的畫家和透視法的運用中也見識過。

The Reformation came about because people no longer tolerated the old ways and the authority of the Pope. There had been some quite wicked popes a few hundred years earlier. There was even a time when there were two popes who stood against each other, one in Rome and one in Avignon, in France. Yet in those times, even when there were two popes, people still looked up to one or other of them, but they never questioned whether or not there should be a pope. Now people no longer felt that they needed or wanted the authority of the Pope.

宗教改革之所以發生，是因為人們不再容忍舊的方式和教宗的權威。幾百年前曾有過相當邪惡的教宗。甚至有一段時期同時存在兩位互相對立的教宗，一位在 Rome，一位在法國的 Avignon。然而在那個年代，即使有兩位教宗，人們仍然仰望其中之一，從來不曾質疑到底該不該有教宗。如今人們不再覺得自己需要或想要教宗的權威了。

There were also other people who did not want change. For these people, even a wicked pope was better than having no pope at all.

也有另一些人不希望改變。對這些人來說，即使是一個邪惡的教宗，也比完全沒有教宗要好。

In the south of Europe, in Spain, Portugal and Italy, people remained faithful to the Church of Rome and the authority of the Pope. In these sunny, warm lands of Europe, the new spirit did not touch religion; instead people became explorers like Columbus or Magellan, or artists like Leonardo and Raphael. They used the new spirit for discoveries or in art. But in the colder countries of the north there was as yet little in the way of exploring, and art changed only slowly. North of the Alps the spirit of new things turned to religion and so brought the Reformation.

在歐洲南部——Spain、Portugal 和 Italy——人們依然忠於羅馬教會和教宗的權威。在這些陽光燦爛、溫暖的歐洲土地上，新的精神並未觸及宗教；人們反而成為了像 Columbus 或 Magellan 那樣的探險家，或像 Leonardo 和 Raphael 那樣的藝術家。他們把新的精神用在了探索或藝術上。但在北方較寒冷的國家，探險活動尚不多見，藝術的變化也很緩慢。在 Alps 山脈以北，新事物的精神轉向了宗教，於是帶來了宗教改革。

It was not the case in these countries that all people wanted a new Church, or that all people wanted to break away from Rome, and so there was a lot of suffering and bloodshed. In Scotland the Protestants grew so strong that in the end the king, who was a Roman Catholic and who did not want the Reformation, had to give in. John Knox's ideas led to the Church of Scotland.

在這些國家裡，並非所有人都想要一個新的教會，也並非所有人都想脫離羅馬，因此有許多苦難和流血。在 Scotland，新教徒變得如此強大，以至於最終身為天主教徒、不希望宗教改革的國王也不得不讓步。John Knox 的理念催生了 Scotland 國教。

In England it was just the opposite. There the Reformation came by the will of the king. That is one difference between Scotland and England: in Scotland the Reformation came through the people, in England it came through the king.

在 England 則恰恰相反。那裡的宗教改革是出於國王的意志。這是 Scotland 和 England 的一個差別：在 Scotland，宗教改革來自人民；在 England，宗教改革來自國王。

These two men, John Knox and King Henry VIII of England, were also as persons the very opposite of each other. John Knox was of small stature and thin. He ate and drank very little, just as much as was necessary. Henry VIII was tall and overweight, and whenever he ate a meal he gorged himself. John Knox was a severe, strict man, but he wanted nothing for himself; all his life and all his work was for his Church and for Scotland. Henry VIII, however, thought only of his own good: the Church and the English people existed only for his own benefit and his own convenience. He was a foul-tempered bully who cared only for himself.

這兩個人——John Knox 和 England 的 Henry 八世——在個人特質上也截然相反。John Knox 身材矮小、瘦削。他吃得很少、喝得很少，僅維持基本所需。Henry 八世身材高大、體態臃腫，每次用餐都狼吞虎嚥。John Knox 是個嚴厲、嚴格的人，但他不為自己謀求任何東西；他畢生的精力和工作全都獻給了他的教會和 Scotland。Henry 八世卻只想著自己的利益：教會和英國人民的存在只是為了他自己的好處和方便。他是一個脾氣暴躁的惡霸，只在乎自己。

King Henry VIII was, like everybody else at that time, a Roman Catholic and was not interested in change. When he heard of Luther he called him a madman, and when a few people in England began to preach against Rome, Henry had them burnt at the stake. But Henry VIII was married to a Spanish princess, Catherine of Aragon, who had borne him a daughter, Mary. The time came when Henry no longer loved his wife and wanted to divorce her and marry a lady called Anne Boleyn. But the Catholic Church does not allow divorce. King Henry thought the Pope in Rome would make an exception for him, but he was mistaken. The Pope refused to allow Henry to divorce his wife.

Henry 八世和那個時代的其他所有人一樣，是個天主教徒，對改變並無興趣。當他聽聞 Luther 時，他稱 Luther 為瘋子；當英國有少數人開始公開反對羅馬時，Henry 就把他們送上了火刑柱。但 Henry 八世娶了一位西班牙公主 Catherine of Aragon，她為他生了一個女兒 Mary。後來有一天，Henry 不再愛他的妻子了，想要與她離婚，改娶一位名叫 Anne Boleyn 的女士。但天主教會不允許離婚。Henry 國王以為羅馬教宗會為他破例，但他想錯了。教宗拒絕允許 Henry 離婚。

Henry had sent an old English cardinal to Rome to plead with the Pope. When the old man came back with the news the Pope had refused, the king went into a towering rage. The poor old cardinal was sent to prison, but died on the way. Then Henry declared: 'If the Pope and his Church will not divorce me from my wife, I will have a Church that has nothing to do with Rome!'

Henry 曾派一位年邁的英國樞機主教前往 Rome 向教宗求情。當這位老人帶回教宗拒絕的消息時，國王暴跳如雷。可憐的老樞機主教被送往監獄，卻在途中去世了。接著 Henry 宣布：「如果教宗和他的教會不讓我和妻子離婚，那我就要一個和羅馬毫無關係的教會！」

The English Parliament had no liking for Rome or the Pope, and so at the wish of King Henry VIII a law was passed that, in England, the head of the Church was no longer the Pope, but the king. Priests, monks and bishops who would not take an oath to recognise the king as head of the Church were executed.

英國國會對羅馬和教宗並無好感，因此在 Henry 八世的要求下，一項法律通過了：在 England，教會的元首不再是教宗，而是國王。拒絕宣誓承認國王為教會元首的神父、修士和主教都被處死了。

So the Church that Henry had founded was not a new, reformed Church, like John Knox's or Calvin's or Luther's. It was the old Church, only now Henry and not the Pope was the head of it. In this way the Church of England is different from all the other Churches that came out of the Reformation.

因此 Henry 所建立的教會並不是一個新的、改革後的教會，不像 John Knox 的、Calvin 的或 Luther 的教會。它是那個舊教會，只是現在教會的元首是 Henry 而不是教宗。英國國教就是這樣，與宗教改革所產生的其他所有教會都不同。

The new Church, the Church of England, had of course to obey King Henry VIII. He divorced his wife, the Spanish princess, and married Anne Boleyn. She bore him a daughter, Elizabeth, who was to become one of the great queens of history.

新教會——英國國教——當然得服從 Henry 八世。他與那位西班牙公主離了婚，娶了 Anne Boleyn。她為他生了一個女兒 Elizabeth，這個女孩日後將成為歷史上最偉大的女王之一。

But Anne Boleyn herself was not Henry's wife for long. He got tired of her, and did not even bother to divorce her; Anne was executed. After her Henry VIII had four more wives, one after another - who either died naturally or were executed or divorced.

但 Anne Boleyn 做 Henry 妻子的時間並不長。他厭倦了她，甚至懶得離婚——Anne 被處死了。在她之後，Henry 八世又先後娶了四位妻子——不是自然死亡，就是被處決，或是被離婚。

Henry VIII was a cruel, brutal man, but strangely enough, the people of England liked him. They were glad to be rid of an Italian pope. They would rather have an Englishman as head of the Church, even if he was a selfish man. They liked King Henry VIII because he took all the land and wealth away from the monasteries and closed them down. They had come to think of the monks as useless, lazy men, who were good for nothing.

Henry 八世是個殘忍、粗暴的人，但說來奇怪，英國人民卻喜歡他。他們很高興擺脫了一個義大利教宗。他們寧願讓一個英國人做教會的元首，即便這個人很自私。他們喜歡 Henry 八世，因為他從修道院手中奪走了所有土地和財富，並將修道院關閉。他們已經把修士們看作無用的懶人，一無是處。

The common people liked King 'Hal', and when war broke out between Scotland and England, the English soldiers fought so well for Henry that the Scots suffered terrible defeats at Flodden Field and Solway Moss.

平民百姓喜歡「Hal 國王」，當 Scotland 和 England 之間爆發戰爭時，英國士兵為 Henry 奮勇作戰，蘇格蘭人在 Flodden Field 和 Solway Moss 遭受了慘敗。

After Henry's death, England went through a hard time. His only living son, Edward VI, ruled only a few years before dying. The next ruler was Mary, the daughter of Catherine of Aragon whom Henry had divorced. Mary wanted to bring the Roman Catholic faith back, and the English men or women who spoke out against this were burned at the stake. In five years of Mary's rule three hundred people were burned for this crime. When she died, many people in England rejoiced and looked forward to the new queen, Elizabeth I, the daughter of Anne Boleyn, for she was a Protestant.

Henry 去世後，England 經歷了一段艱難的時期。他唯一在世的兒子 Edward 六世只統治了幾年就去世了。下一位統治者是 Mary——Henry 所離棄的 Catherine of Aragon 的女兒。Mary 想要恢復天主教信仰，任何公開反對的英國男女都被送上了火刑柱。在 Mary 統治的五年裡，有三百人因此被燒死。當她去世時，英國有許多人歡欣鼓舞，期盼著新女王 Elizabeth 一世的到來——Anne Boleyn 的女兒，因為她是新教徒。

# 31. Mary, Queen of Scots
# 31. 蘇格蘭女王 Mary

The new age, the new spirit, showed itself more among the common people than among the noblemen and kings. Columbus, Leonardo, Copernicus, Luther, John Knox, were all common people.

新時代、新精神更多地展現在平民百姓之中，而非貴族和國王之間。Columbus、Leonardo、Copernicus、Luther、John Knox 都是平民出身。

It was also the common people who welcomed the Reformation - at least most of them. The noblemen were more or less evenly divided for or against the Reformation. The kings were, to begin with, all against the Reformation.

歡迎宗教改革的也是平民百姓——至少大多數是。貴族們在支持和反對宗教改革之間大致各占一半。而國王們一開始全都反對宗教改革。

The German emperor declared Luther an outlaw. The king of France solved the problem of the French Protestants by a terrible massacre. In one night, St Bartholomew's Night, thirty thousand Protestants were slaughtered in France. In Scotland, King James V tried to destroy the Protestant movement by executions and burnings, but the movement only grew stronger and in the end, the Church of Scotland was established against the will of King James.

德意志皇帝宣布 Luther 為不受法律保護的人。法國國王以一場可怕的屠殺來解決法國新教徒的問題。在一個夜晚——聖 Bartholomew 之夜——三萬名新教徒在法國遭到屠殺。在 Scotland，James 五世試圖以處刑和火刑來摧毀新教運動，但運動只是越來越壯大，最終 Scotland 國教在違反 James 國王意願的情況下建立了起來。

In England, Henry VIII was also against the Reformation and heretics were burnt at the stake. It was only later, and for his own selfish reasons, that he established a Church separate from Rome.

在 England，Henry 八世起初也反對宗教改革，異端被燒上火刑柱。後來純粹是出於他自私的理由，他才建立了一個脫離羅馬的教會。

But throughout all of this, England was more fortunate than other countries. In England, the ruler and the great majority of the people belonged to the same Church, the Church of England. When Elizabeth became queen, she too was in the fortunate position to belong to the Church that most of the people wanted: the Protestant Church of England. There were only a few Catholic sympathisers left in England.

但在這一切當中，England 比其他國家幸運。在 England，統治者和絕大多數人民屬於同一個教會——英國國教。當 Elizabeth 登基為女王時，她也幸運地屬於大多數人民所期望的教會：英國國教（新教）。England 只剩下少數天主教同情者。

Scotland was not so fortunate. For the most part the people belonged to the Church of Scotland, but the royal family, the Stuarts, remained Roman Catholics, and so did quite a number of noblemen. In Scotland, royalty and the people were divided by belonging to different Churches.

Scotland 就沒有這麼幸運了。大部分人民屬於 Scotland 國教，但皇室家族 Stuart 一家仍然是天主教徒，不少貴族也是。在 Scotland，皇室和人民因為屬於不同的教會而分裂了。

That was the tragedy in the life of Mary, the daughter of James V. When James V died, Mary was still a young child and she was crowned queen of Scotland as a baby. Her mother, a French princess, acted as Mary's regent (ruling until Mary was old enough). She sent Mary to France to be brought up at the Roman Catholic French court, and so Mary grew up in a religion and in a country quite different from Scotland and the Church of Scotland.

這就是 Mary 一生的悲劇所在。Mary 是 James 五世的女兒。James 五世去世時，Mary 還是個幼兒，她在襒褒中就被加冕為蘇格蘭女王。她的母親是一位法國公主，擔任 Mary 的攝政（在 Mary 長大成人之前代為治理）。母親把 Mary 送到法國，在法國天主教宮廷中長大，因此 Mary 在一個與 Scotland 及 Scotland 國教截然不同的宗教和國家中成長。

When Mary was only sixteen years old she was married to the young king of France, and became queen of both Scotland and France. It was the happiest time of her life. Mary was merry and charming, and the French courtiers were witty and amusing, they flattered and praised her. Her life was full of dancing, parties and games.

Mary 年僅十六歲就嫁給了年輕的法國國王，同時成為 Scotland 和 France 的女王。那是她一生中最快樂的時光。Mary 活潑而迷人，法國的朝臣們機智風趣，他們恭維她、讚美她。她的生活充滿了舞蹈、宴會和遊戲。

But this joyful time of Mary's life lasted only two years. First, her young husband died, and then her mother in Scotland died and Mary was called back to become Queen of Scots.

但 Mary 這段歡樂的日子只持續了兩年。先是她年輕的丈夫去世了，接著她在 Scotland 的母親也過世了，Mary 被召回去做蘇格蘭女王。

For Mary it was a heart-breaking change, being taken from her merry life at the court of France to Scotland, where John Knox and his followers looked upon merriment as a sin. Mary was a Roman Catholic and remained one, attending Roman Catholic services in her chapel in Holyrood Palace. The people of Scotland never quite trusted her, fearing she would try to bring back the Catholic faith. John Knox, who was by then an old man, said very unkind things about Mary in his sermons.

對 Mary 來說，這是一個令人心碎的轉變——從法國宮廷的歡樂生活被帶到 Scotland，在那裡 John Knox 和他的追隨者把歡樂視為罪惡。Mary 是天主教徒，也始終保持天主教信仰，在 Holyrood Palace 的禮拜堂參加天主教儀式。Scotland 的人民從未完全信任她，擔心她會試圖恢復天主教信仰。John Knox 那時已是個老人，在佈道中對 Mary 說了許多很不友善的話。

Mary, with her Roman Catholic religion and her love for fine, colourful dresses, for parties, dancing and games, was like a stranger in Scotland, even though she was the queen. Then she did something that made her less popular: she married a Catholic Scottish nobleman, Lord Darnley. The Scottish people did not like that at all. Darnley was an ill-tempered and coarse man, without education or manners. Mary was soon very unhappy with her husband, who probably did not really love her and had only married her in the hope of being crowned king of Scotland one day.

Mary 帶著她的天主教信仰，和她對華美彩衣、宴會、舞蹈和遊戲的熱愛，在 Scotland 就像一個異鄉人，儘管她是女王。後來她做了一件讓自己更不受歡迎的事：她嫁給了一位天主教的蘇格蘭貴族 Lord Darnley。蘇格蘭人民對此非常不滿。Darnley 是個脾氣暴躁、粗魯無文的人，既無教養也無禮儀。Mary 很快就對丈夫感到非常不幸福——他大概並不真正愛她，娶她只是盼望有朝一日能加冕為蘇格蘭國王。

Although Lord Darnley did not really care for Mary, he was madly jealous of any man with whom Mary was friendly. She did not have many friends, but there was one, an Italian musician. He used to play for Mary and so gave the young, lonely queen some pleasure. But this enraged Lord Darnley and one day when Riccio, the Italian musician, was playing for the queen, Lord Darnley and some of his friends dragged Riccio away and stabbed him to death.

雖然 Lord Darnley 並不真正在乎 Mary，他卻瘋狂地嫉妒任何與 Mary 友好的男人。她的朋友不多，但有一位是義大利音樂家。他常為 Mary 演奏，給這位年輕、孤獨的女王帶來一些歡樂。但這激怒了 Lord Darnley，有一天當那位義大利音樂家 Riccio 正在為女王演奏時，Lord Darnley 和他的幾個朋友把 Riccio 拖了出去，亂刀將他刺死。

Mary never forgave Darnley for this murder, but she did not show how she felt. Soon another man was often seen in her company, a Scottish nobleman, James Hepburn, the fourth earl of Bothwell. Mary's husband, Darnley, was not very pleased with this friendship either, but now he kept away from Mary and hardly ever came to see her in Holyrood Palace. Then Lord Darnley fell ill. To everybody's surprise Mary showed great concern for her husband. She went to Glasgow and persuaded Darnley to be brought to Edinburgh where she could visit him daily.

Mary 從未原諒 Darnley 犯下的這樁謀殺，但她沒有表露自己的感受。不久，另一個男人經常出現在她身邊——一位蘇格蘭貴族 James Hepburn，Bothwell 的第四代伯爵。Mary 的丈夫 Darnley 對這段友誼也很不高興，但他開始疏遠 Mary，幾乎不再到 Holyrood Palace 來看她了。後來 Lord Darnley 病倒了。令所有人驚訝的是，Mary 對丈夫表現出極大的關切。她去了 Glasgow，說服 Darnley 被送到 Edinburgh，好讓她每天都能去探望他。

Mary came regularly to visit the sick man, but one evening she came and apologised that she could not stay very long as there was a great dance at Holyrood Palace. That night, while the windows of Holyrood Palace were bright with the light of hundreds of candles, while colourfully dressed courtiers and ladies thronged the large rooms of the palace, while the sound of music and laughter could be heard, there suddenly came the roar of an explosion. The house where Darnley was lying on his sickbed had been blown up, and he and a page were found strangled in a garden nearby.

Mary 定期去探望這位病人，但有一天傍晚她來了，卻表示歉意說她不能久留，因為 Holyrood Palace 有一場盛大的舞會。那天夜裡，當 Holyrood Palace 的窗戶在數百支蠟燭的光芒中閃耀，當衣著華麗的朝臣和貴婦們擠滿了宮殿寬大的廳堂，當音樂聲和笑聲不絕於耳時，突然傳來一聲巨大的爆炸。Darnley 躺在病床上的那棟房子被炸毀了，他和一名侍從被發現在附近的花園裡被勒死。

We shall never know who was behind the death of Darnley, but the Scottish people blamed Mary and her friend, the earl of Bothwell. When Mary married Bothwell three months after Darnley's death, it was too much. A great number of Protestant noblemen rose in rebellion against Mary. She was taken prisoner and kept imprisoned in a castle on an island in the middle of Loch Leven. She never saw her new husband again. He escaped to Denmark and later died there.

我們永遠不會知道 Darnley 之死的幕後黑手是誰，但蘇格蘭人民指責 Mary 和她的朋友 Bothwell 伯爵。當 Mary 在 Darnley 死後三個月就嫁給了 Bothwell，這實在太過分了。大批新教貴族起兵反叛 Mary。她被俘虜，囚禁在 Loch Leven 湖中央一座小島上的城堡裡。她再也沒有見過她的新丈夫。他逃到了 Denmark，後來死在那裡。

For a year Mary was imprisoned in that castle, but then a page stole the keys of the castle and with his help she escaped in a small rowing boat. Catholic noblemen now came to her aid, gathering an army to fight against the Protestants who had imprisoned Mary. Scotland was torn by a war between its own people, but in the end the Protestants were stronger. The Roman Catholics were defeated and Mary had to flee. No place in Scotland was safe for her. She fled to England, hoping that Elizabeth, who was a cousin of hers, would give her shelter and protection.

Mary 在那座城堡裡被囚禁了一年，後來一名侍從偷了城堡的鑰匙，在他的幫助下，Mary 乘坐一條小划船逃了出來。天主教貴族們前來援助她，集結了一支軍隊與囚禁 Mary 的新教徒作戰。Scotland 被自己人民之間的戰爭撕裂了，但最終新教徒更為強大。天主教徒被擊敗了，Mary 不得不逃亡。Scotland 沒有任何地方對她是安全的。她逃到了 England，希望她的表親 Elizabeth 能給她庇護和保護。

But Elizabeth gave Mary only a very cold welcome. There were still a number of Catholics in England who might well have tried a rebellion to make Mary the queen of England. Elizabeth was not going to take any risks. Mary was imprisoned in a series of English castles for nineteen years.

但 Elizabeth 只給了 Mary 非常冷淡的歡迎。England 仍有不少天主教徒，他們很可能會嘗試發動叛亂讓 Mary 成為英國女王。Elizabeth 不會冒任何風險。Mary 在一連串的英國城堡中被囚禁了十九年。

But even as a prisoner, Mary was a danger to Elizabeth. The English Catholics made plans to free Mary. All these plots failed, but they showed that as long as Mary was alive, the English Catholics were thinking of rebellion against Elizabeth. When, after nineteen years, another such plot was discovered, the English Parliament persuaded Elizabeth that Mary had to die, and so the English queen signed Mary's death warrant.

但即便身為囚徒，Mary 對 Elizabeth 依然是個威脅。英國的天主教徒制定了解救 Mary 的計劃。這些密謀全都失敗了，但它們表明只要 Mary 活著，英國的天主教徒就一直在策劃對 Elizabeth 的叛亂。十九年後，又一個這樣的密謀被發現，英國國會說服 Elizabeth，Mary 必須死，於是英國女王簽署了 Mary 的死刑執行令。

# 32. Elizabeth I and the Great Armada
# 32. Elizabeth 一世與無敵艦隊

Mary, Queen of Scots, was a warm-hearted woman of strong feelings. She followed her heart more than her head. Elizabeth, queen of England and Ireland, on the other hand did not have the warmth and charm of her cousin Mary. She did not follow her feelings, but thought over and weighed up everything she did. For a queen, this was the better way by far. Elizabeth, cool and level-headed as she was, had a great sense of responsibility: what she did was for the benefit of England. Mary, brought up in France, had little sense of responsibility for Scotland.

蘇格蘭女王 Mary 是一個熱心腸、感情強烈的女人。她更多地遵從自己的心，而非頭腦。另一方面，England 和 Ireland 的女王 Elizabeth 並沒有她表親 Mary 的溫暖和魅力。她不追隨自己的感情，而是對自己所做的每一件事都深思熟慮、權衡利弊。對一位女王來說，這無疑是好得多的方式。Elizabeth 冷靜而理智，她有著強烈的責任感：她所做的一切都是為了 England 的利益。Mary 在法國長大，對 Scotland 幾乎沒有什麼責任感。

That is why Mary is one of the tragic queens of history, while Elizabeth became one of the great queens of history: she never forgot that she had a duty towards her people.

這就是為什麼 Mary 是歷史上悲劇性的女王之一，而 Elizabeth 成為了歷史上偉大的女王之一：她從未忘記自己對人民負有責任。

England was experiencing terrible dangers and hardships at that time, and these dangers and hardships mainly came from Spain. Spain at that time was immensely powerful. Enormous riches had come to it from the colonies in America and vast numbers of Spanish ships sailed the seas. The Spanish ships were larger and the number of ships greater than that of any other navy. The ruler of this mighty Spanish Empire was Philip II, the son of Emperor Charles V, who had declared Luther an outlaw.

England 在那個時期正經歷著可怕的危險和艱難，而這些危險和艱難主要來自 Spain。那時的 Spain 無比強大。來自美洲殖民地的巨大財富使它富甲天下，大量的西班牙船隻航行在海上。西班牙的船隻比任何其他海軍的都大，船隻數量也比任何其他海軍的都多。這個強大的西班牙帝國的統治者是 Philip 二世，他是曾宣布 Luther 為法外之人的 Charles 五世皇帝的兒子。

Philip II was a devout Roman Catholic whose sole aim in life was to destroy the Reformation and to force the authority of the Pope back on the people who had broken away from Rome. He could do nothing about Germany, which was ruled by a brother of Charles V, but Belgium and Holland were under Philip's rule and in these unhappy countries the Protestants were burned by the hundreds. Philip's great ambition was to bring these 'blessings' to the people of England and, by force and terror, make England a Roman Catholic country again. Philip nearly had the opportunity to do this, for as a young prince he married England's Catholic Queen Mary, the daughter of King Henry VIII, who had ruled England before Elizabeth. But when Mary died, Elizabeth became queen.

Philip 二世是一位虔誠的天主教徒，他人生的唯一目標就是摧毀宗教改革，迫使那些脫離羅馬的人民重新接受教宗的權威。他對德意志無能為力，因為那裡由 Charles 五世的兄弟統治；但 Belgium 和 Holland 都在 Philip 的統治之下，在這些不幸的國家裡，新教徒成百上千地被燒死。Philip 的宏大野心是要把這些「恩典」帶給英國人民，以武力和恐怖手段把 England 重新變成天主教國家。Philip 幾乎獲得了這樣做的機會，因為他年輕時曾娶了英國的天主教女王 Mary——Henry 八世的女兒，她在 Elizabeth 之前統治英國。但 Mary 去世後，Elizabeth 成了女王。

Now Philip made another attempt to get England under his power the easy way. Through the Spanish ambassador in London he sent a proposal of marriage to Elizabeth.

於是 Philip 又企圖以輕鬆的方式將 England 納入他的勢力範圍。他通過駐倫敦的西班牙大使向 Elizabeth 求婚。

Of course, in his plan Elizabeth would have to become Roman Catholic, and of course, the English Protestants would be forced by terror and by persecution to return to the Church of Rome. But imagine what a mighty empire this union of Spain and England would have been. For an ambitious person - and Elizabeth was ambitious - it must have been a very tempting offer to become queen of England, Spain and the vast colonies in America. Elizabeth knew, however, that by marrying Philip she would bring terrible misery and suffering to all the Protestants in England, to the majority of her people. She refused the offer.

當然，按照他的計劃，Elizabeth 必須改信天主教，而英國的新教徒也當然會被恐怖和迫害逼迫回到羅馬教會。但想像一下，Spain 和 England 的聯合將是多麼強大的帝國。對一個有野心的人——而 Elizabeth 確實有野心——來說，成為 England、Spain 和美洲廣大殖民地的女王，一定是一個非常誘人的提議。然而 Elizabeth 知道，嫁給 Philip 會給 England 所有的新教徒、給她的大多數人民帶來可怕的苦難。她拒絕了這個提議。

Philip was furious that his proposal of marriage had been rejected, but he soon had more reason to be annoyed by England. At this time the people of England began to realise that the future of their country was to become a seagoing power.

Philip 對自己的求婚遭到拒絕勃然大怒，但他很快有了更多被 England 激怒的理由。就在這個時候，英國人民開始意識到他們國家的未來在於成為一個海洋強國。

The ships of Prince Henry the Navigator had made Portugal rich, and the caravels of Columbus had given Spain untold wealth and power. Britain, an island surrounded by the sea, could only become great and prosperous with English ships and English sailors. It was at the time of Elizabeth that the English navy began to grow and the English sailors set out on the high seas.

航海家 Henry 王子的船隊使 Portugal 富裕起來，Columbus 的卡拉維爾帆船給 Spain 帶來了無盡的財富和權力。Britain 是一個被大海環繞的島嶼，只有憑藉英國的船隻和英國的水手才能變得偉大和繁榮。正是在 Elizabeth 的時代，英國海軍開始壯大，英國水手們駛向了遠洋大海。

These English captains and sailors were rather like the Spanish Conquistadors: their main interest was gold and treasure. They did not care how they gained their fortunes, as long as they could get rich.

這些英國船長和水手頗似西班牙的征服者們：他們的主要興趣是黃金和財寶。他們不在乎如何獲得財富，只要能致富就行。

The simplest way to gain wealth was by pouncing on the Spanish ships carrying gold and silver from America to Spain. The English sailors were simply pirates, but they were the most daring pirates in the world. One or two English ships would not only capture much bigger Spanish ships, but they would also sometimes attack one of the big Spanish ports in America, plundering it and sailing away loaded with booty.

獲取財富最簡單的方式就是撲向那些從美洲運載金銀到 Spain 的西班牙船隻。英國水手們簡直就是海盜，但他們是世界上最大膽的海盜。一兩艘英國船不僅能俘獲比自己大得多的西班牙船，有時還會攻擊美洲的某個大型西班牙港口，洗劫一空後滿載戰利品揚帆而去。

King Philip of Spain was thoroughly annoyed with this English impudence. As long as Mary, Queen of Scots lived, Philip had hoped that the Roman Catholics in England would set her free, making her queen of England and Ireland. But when Mary was executed, there was an end to these hopes.

Spain 的 Philip 國王對英國人的放肆行徑非常惱火。只要蘇格蘭女王 Mary 還活著，Philip 就抱有希望：英國的天主教徒會救出她，讓她成為 England 和 Ireland 的女王。但當 Mary 被處死後，這些希望就破滅了。

So Philip decided on one bold stroke that would finish off Queen Elizabeth, who had insulted him by refusing marriage, the English navy, which continued to rob his treasure ships, and the Protestant Church of England, which he had always wanted to destroy.

於是 Philip 決定以一記大膽的打擊來一舉解決三件事：拒絕他求婚而羞辱了他的 Elizabeth 女王、不斷搶劫他寶船的英國海軍、以及他一直想要摧毀的英國新教教會。

All three things should be accomplished with one mighty blow by the ships of Spain. Preparations began in Spain to send the largest fleet the world had ever seen against England. The fleet would not only attack English ports, but also carry a vast army to invade England and to occupy it. The dockyards of Spain worked in frantic haste to build more and more ships, and the Spanish warships from all over the world were called back to join the great fleet.

這三件事都要由西班牙的船隊以一記強力打擊來完成。Spain 開始準備派出世界上前所未見的最龐大艦隊進攻 England。這支艦隊不僅要攻擊英國港口，還要運載一支龐大的軍隊入侵並占領 England。Spain 的造船廠瘋狂趕工，建造越來越多的船隻，世界各地的西班牙戰艦也被召回來加入這支龐大的艦隊。

While all this preparation was going on, an English captain, Francis Drake, suddenly appeared with a handful of English ships in the Spanish port of Cadiz, and before the Spaniards recovered from their surprise, ten great Spanish galleons and twenty smaller vessels were sunk. As Drake sailed away, he caught a Spanish treasure ship and took from it a cargo of gold worth many millions in today's money. When Francis Drake arrived back in England, he said: 'I have singed the beard of the king of Spain!'

就在這一切準備如火如荼進行的時候，一位英國船長 Francis Drake 突然率領幾艘英國船出現在西班牙港口 Cadiz，趁西班牙人還沒從驚愕中回過神來，十艘巨大的西班牙大帆船和二十艘較小的船隻就被擊沉了。Drake 在離去途中還截獲了一艘西班牙寶船，從上面取走了以今日幣值計算價值數百萬的黃金。Francis Drake 回到 England 後說：「我燒焦了西班牙國王的鬍子！」

This important stroke made Philip II only more eager to punish England and, in May 1588, his fleet was ready. It was called the Great Armada. The Great Armada was a fleet of seventy large and sixty smaller ships. The large galleons of about five hundred tons were floating fortresses, carrying about three hundred men each. The whole Armada of a hundred and thirty ships carried twenty thousand soldiers and eight thousand sailors. Against this mighty fleet the English only had thirty-four much smaller vessels and fifteen thousand sailors. The English fleet was commanded by Lord Howard of Effingham, an experienced sailor, while the Armada was under the duke of Medina Sidonia, who belonged to a very noble family and who knew very little about ships or sailing.

這次重要的突襲只讓 Philip 二世更加迫切地想要懲罰 England，到了 1588 年五月，他的艦隊準備就緒了。它被稱為「無敵艦隊」（Great Armada）。無敵艦隊由七十艘大型船和六十艘小型船組成。大型帆船約五百噸，是漂浮的堡壘，每艘搭載約三百人。整個一百三十艘船的無敵艦隊共載有兩萬名士兵和八千名水手。面對這支強大的艦隊，英國只有三十四艘小得多的船隻和一萬五千名水手。英國艦隊由經驗豐富的水手 Lord Howard of Effingham 指揮，而無敵艦隊則由 Medina Sidonia 公爵統率，他出身非常高貴的家族，卻對船隻和航海所知甚少。

The English were certainly not afraid of the enemy's might. Francis Drake, who was one of the captains under Lord Howard, was at Plymouth playing a game of bowls when the news came that the Armada was approaching England. 'Time enough to finish this game and to beat the Spaniards,' said Drake. And he calmly finished the game before sailing against the enemy.

英國人當然不怕敵人的強大。Francis Drake 是 Lord Howard 麾下的船長之一，當無敵艦隊正在逼近 England 的消息傳來時，他正在 Plymouth 打保齡球。Drake 說：「打完這場球再去打敗西班牙人，時間綽綽有餘。」然後他從容地打完了球，才出海迎戰。

When the Armada appeared, beacon fires blazed from one end of England to the other to warn the people. Queen Elizabeth went to her fleet to speak to the sailors and her words stirred the hearts of the men.

當無敵艦隊出現時，烽火從 England 的一端燃到另一端，向人民發出警告。Elizabeth 女王親臨艦隊向水手們講話，她的言詞激盪了官兵們的心。

As the Spanish ships came into the English Channel a strong gale blew up which made most of the twenty thousand soldiers so seasick that they were no use at all. Moreover, the high galleons could hardly be steered in heavy weather and the little English ships darted in and out between them, doing great damage and getting away before the Spaniards could hit back. This game lasted a whole week, during which time the gale grew fiercer and fiercer. More and more Spanish ships ran aground, and then the Spanish admiral made the mistake of ordering his ships to seek shelter on the French coast at Calais. The Spanish ships were all crowded together so the English sent fire-ships among them. These were ships filled with gunpowder and other combustibles that were deliberately set on fire and steered towards the enemy's fleet. The Spanish galleons, trying to get out of the way of the fire-ships, ran into each other.

當西班牙船隻駛入英吉利海峽時，一場強烈的暴風刮了起來，使兩萬名士兵中的大多數嚴重暈船，完全派不上用場。而且，高大的西班牙帆船在惡劣天氣中幾乎無法操控，而小巧的英國船在它們之間穿梭自如，造成巨大的破壞，又在西班牙人反擊之前溜之大吉。這場遊擊戰持續了整整一週，期間風暴越來越猛烈。越來越多的西班牙船擱淺了，接著西班牙將軍犯了一個錯誤，命令船隻到法國海岸的 Calais 尋求避風。西班牙船隻全擠在一起，英國人就放出了火船。這些火船裝滿了火藥和其他易燃物，被故意點燃後駛向敵人的艦隊。西班牙大帆船試圖避開火船，結果互相撞在了一起。

By the end of the week the gale became so wild that even the English ships took to their ports. The Armada tried to get away by sailing around Scotland, but the roaring storm shattered so many ships on the rocks and islands that, in the end, only fifty vessels, broken and battered, reached Spain. The English had lost only two hundred men and not a single ship.

到了那一週結束時，暴風變得如此狂猛，連英國船隻也只好回港。無敵艦隊試圖繞過 Scotland 逃走，但咆哮的風暴把許多船撞碎在岩石和島嶼上，最終只有五十艘殘破不堪的船隻回到了 Spain。英國人只損失了兩百人，沒有失去一艘船。

All over England bells rang and bonfires were lit. Elizabeth ordered that a special medal be struck in memory of this great occasion. On that medal was the inscription: 'God blew and they were scattered by His breath!'

全 England 的鐘聲齊鳴，篝火熊熊。Elizabeth 下令鑄造一枚特別的紀念章來紀念這個偉大的時刻。紀念章上刻著：「上帝吹了一口氣，他們就被祂的氣息吹散了！」

# 33. Elizabethan Times, Shakespeare and Raleigh
# 33. Elizabeth 時代、Shakespeare 與 Raleigh

When the Great Armada came, the people of England rallied around their queen. If the Spaniards had landed they would have found every Englishman and woman, from the peasant in their hut to the lord in his manor, ready to fight to their last breath. They loved their queen. When it became known she would pass through a street, people gathered together hours before and gave her rousing cheers when she came. They called her Good Queen Bess, but the courtiers invented better-sounding names for her. They called her the 'Virgin Queen' because she never married, and 'Gloriana', meaning the glorious one.

當無敵艦隊來襲時，英國人民團結在女王的周圍。如果西班牙人登了陸，他們會發現每一個英國男女——從茅屋中的農民到莊園裡的領主——都準備好戰鬥到最後一口氣。他們熱愛自己的女王。每當人們得知她將經過某條街道，就會提前幾個小時聚集起來，在她到來時熱烈歡呼。他們稱她為「好女王 Bess」，但朝臣們為她發明了更華麗的稱號。他們稱她為「處女女王」（Virgin Queen），因為她終身未嫁；又稱她「Gloriana」，意思是光榮者。

These were flattering names, and Queen Elizabeth liked to be flattered. With her auburn hair and delicate complexion she had a striking appearance, and she helped this striking appearance by wearing the most glorious clothes. She set fashions that made the clothes of wealthy women and men in England more colourful, more showy than they have ever been, either before or after.

這些都是恭維的稱號，而 Elizabeth 女王喜歡被恭維。她有著赤褐色的秀髮和細緻的膚色，外表引人注目，而她身上穿的最華麗的服飾更增添了這種引人注目的風采。她引領了時尚風潮，使英國富有男女的服飾比以往任何時候都更加色彩繽紛、更加華麗奪目——無論是之前還是之後都未曾見過。

Wealthy women's dresses were made of silk, or from cloth of silver or gold. They wore immense skirts that were made to stand out by means of petticoats with wooden hoops. Men's clothes were just as colourful: graceful jackets slashed to show brightly coloured linings; short, stuffed trousers; long stockings. Both men and women wore wide ruffs round their necks that stood out above the shoulders and high behind the head. Jewellery was worn by men and women, and many men wore an earring, a large single pearl or jewel.

富裕女性的禮服用絲綢製成，或以銀線布、金線布縫製。她們穿著巨大的裙子，靠著內裡有木箍的襯裙撐出蓬鬆的裙形。男士的服裝同樣色彩繽紛：剪開口子露出明亮彩色裡襯的優雅外套、短而蓬鬆的褲子、長筒襪。男女都在脖子上戴著寬大的環狀皺領，高聳在肩膀之上、頭部之後。珠寶首飾男女皆佩戴，許多男士還佩戴耳環——一顆碩大的珍珠或寶石。

The crude eating habits of earlier times disappeared, and for the first time people began to use forks, knives and spoons instead of their fingers. Houses, too, changed. With the invention of gunpowder there was no point in building castles that were like fortresses with moats and keeps. Now noblemen built graceful houses with large windows, wide doorways and spacious gardens. Some of these stately homes can still be seen today.

早期粗鄙的飲食習慣消失了，人們第一次開始使用刀叉和湯匙，而不是用手指。住宅也發生了變化。火藥發明之後，建造那種帶護城河和主塔的堡壘式城堡已毫無意義。如今貴族們建造優雅的宅邸，有大窗戶、寬門廊和寬敞的花園。這些雄偉的宅邸中，有些至今仍可看到。

English ships sailing the seas brought trade, money and prosperity. Rich people could find more time for leisure and art.

英國船隻航行於海上，帶來了貿易、財富和繁榮。富人們可以騰出更多時間從事休閒和藝術。

One can say that at the time of Elizabeth, the Renaissance came to England. It did not show itself so much in paintings or sculptures, but in a different art: in poetry and in plays.

可以說，在 Elizabeth 的時代，文藝復興來到了 England。它並不是以繪畫或雕塑的形式呈現，而是以一種不同的藝術形式：詩歌和戲劇。

As the Italian people had become interested in paintings, so the English became fascinated by the writing and the production of plays. Queen Elizabeth had special plays performed for her at her royal court. Thousands of plays were written and performed in her time. The greatest of all the writers of that time, and arguably the greatest of all English writers of all times, was William Shakespeare.

正如義大利人對繪畫產生了興趣，英國人則著迷於劇本的寫作和演出。Elizabeth 女王在她的王室宮廷中讓人為她上演特別的戲劇。在她的時代，成千上萬的劇本被寫成並上演。那個時代最偉大的作家，也可以說是有史以來最偉大的英語作家，就是 William Shakespeare。

At that time actors formed little groups, and at about the time of the Armada, William Shakespeare joined such a troupe of players in London. At first he was only a kind of stagehand. There is even a story that he used to look after the horses of people who came to see the plays. Then he became an actor himself and, after a time, he began to write plays for his group of players, who performed at the Globe Theatre in London.

那個時代演員們組成小型劇團，大約在無敵艦隊來襲的時候，William Shakespeare 加入了 London 的這樣一個劇團。起初他只是一種舞台雜工。甚至有一個故事說，他曾經為來看戲的觀眾照看馬匹。後來他自己成為了演員，過了一段時間，他開始為他的劇團寫劇本，這個劇團在 London 的 Globe Theatre 演出。

Shakespeare had learned the art of acting from scratch. He knew from his own experience what works effectively on the stage, and this no doubt contributed to his plays having the power they have to this day.

Shakespeare 從零開始學習表演藝術。他從自身經驗中知道什麼在舞台上有效果，這無疑使他的戲劇至今仍具有那種震撼力。

As the Renaissance produced Leonardo and Michelangelo in Italy, in England it produced the great genius of Shakespeare. But the Renaissance, the time of Queen Elizabeth, produced all kinds of colourful personalities with many amazing gifts. Such a person of many gifts who lived at that time was Sir Walter Raleigh.

正如文藝復興在 Italy 孕育了 Leonardo 和 Michelangelo，在 England 它孕育了 Shakespeare 這位偉大的天才。但文藝復興——Elizabeth 女王的時代——產生了各種多才多藝、色彩繽紛的人物。那個時代一位這樣多才多藝的人就是 Sir Walter Raleigh。

The best way to be in Queen Elizabeth's favour was to flatter her. One day she was travelling in a coach through the streets of London with some of her courtiers. As usual, crowds gathered to cheer her and, in order to show herself to her people, Elizabeth ordered the coach to stop, and stepped out of it. And there, right in front of her, was a big puddle of mud. If she made another step her dainty shoes would sink into the mud and her satin skirt would be splattered. As she hesitated, not knowing what to do, a young man stepped forward, he wore a fine scarlet cloak on his shoulders. In a moment he tore the cloak from his shoulders and threw it over the puddle. The queen could now step safely on the cloak and reach dry ground. She turned to the young man and ordered him to come with her to the court. He had spoiled his fine coat, but he had made his fortune.

討得 Elizabeth 女王歡心的最佳方式就是奉承她。有一天，她和幾位朝臣乘坐馬車穿過 London 的街道。照例，人群聚集起來為她歡呼。為了向她的人民展示自己，Elizabeth 命令馬車停下，走了下來。就在她面前，是一大灘泥水。如果她再走一步，精緻的鞋子就會陷入泥裡，緞面裙子也會被濺髒。正當她猶豫不知所措時，一個年輕人走上前來，他肩上披著一件華美的猩紅色披風。轉眼間他從肩上扯下披風，覆蓋在泥灘上。女王現在可以安全地踩在披風上走到乾燥的地面。她轉向那個年輕人，命令他隨她進宮。他毀了自己的好外套，卻為自己贏得了前程。

The young man was Walter Raleigh, and he became the queen's favourite courtier. He had been poor, but the queen gave him large gifts of money and land, and later knighted him. But Sir Walter Raleigh was not only an elegant courtier, he was also a clever man and the queen followed his advice in matters of government. And so it came to pass that Sir Walter Raleigh changed the course of history. He once spoke to Queen Elizabeth and said: 'Spain has become rich and powerful through its colonies in the New World, in America. If England is to become a great nation, then we too must have colonies in America. We are not strong enough to take the Spanish colonies in South America, but Spain has not touched North America. Let us establish English colonies in North America, and we shall in time be greater than the Spaniards!'

這個年輕人就是 Walter Raleigh，他成為女王最寵愛的朝臣。他原本很窮，但女王賜予他大量的金錢和土地，後來還封他為騎士。但 Sir Walter Raleigh 不僅是一位優雅的朝臣，他也是一個聰明人，女王在政務上聽從他的建議。就這樣，Sir Walter Raleigh 改變了歷史的進程。他有一次對 Elizabeth 女王說：「Spain 因為在新世界、在美洲的殖民地而變得富有強大。如果 England 要成為偉大的國家，我們也必須在美洲擁有殖民地。我們還不夠強大，無法奪取西班牙在南美洲的殖民地，但 Spain 還沒有觸及北美洲。讓我們在北美洲建立英國殖民地，假以時日我們就會超越西班牙人！」

Queen Elizabeth agreed with Raleigh's advice, but, even though he longed for adventure, she would not let him leave the court. Sir Walter Raleigh was not allowed to sail across the Atlantic to found an English colony in America, but he was rich enough to buy ships and to send men there. The first English colony in North America was established through Sir Walter Raleigh, and in order to flatter the Virgin Queen Elizabeth, this first English colony was called Virginia. It is now part of the United States and still bears the name Virginia.

Elizabeth 女王同意了 Raleigh 的建議，但儘管他渴望冒險，她卻不讓他離開宮廷。Sir Walter Raleigh 不被允許橫渡大西洋去美洲建立英國殖民地，但他足夠富有，可以買船並派人前往。第一個在北美洲建立的英國殖民地就是通過 Sir Walter Raleigh 促成的，為了奉承「處女女王」Elizabeth，這第一個英國殖民地被命名為 Virginia。它現在是 United States 的一部分，至今仍保留著 Virginia 這個名字。

As with the Spanish Conquistadors, the English colonists arrived in North America to find indigenous people already living there. The colonists fought with the local tribes, who were of course simply defending their homeland. But the colonists also learned from these Indigenous Americans. They learned from them the use of a peculiar American plant: tobacco. Soon the habit of smoking spread to Europe and made the colonists rich. Virginia tobacco is still grown today. Sir Walter Raleigh was one of the first to try the new habit of smoking. A servant who saw smoke coming from Raleigh's nose and mouth thought his master was on fire and threw a bucket of water over him.

和西班牙征服者一樣，英國殖民者抵達北美洲時，發現那裡已有原住民居住。殖民者與當地部落發生了衝突，而那些部落當然只是在保衛自己的家園。但殖民者也向這些美洲原住民學到了東西。他們從原住民那裡學會了一種奇特的美洲植物的用法：菸草。不久，吸菸的習慣傳播到歐洲，使殖民者致富。Virginia 菸草至今仍在種植。Sir Walter Raleigh 是最早嘗試吸菸這種新習慣的人之一。一個僕人看到煙從 Raleigh 的鼻子和嘴裡冒出來，以為主人著火了，潑了一桶水在他身上。

Much more important was another American plant: the potato. In earlier times, when the wheat harvest happened to be bad in England, there was famine and starvation. Now people could fall back on potatoes when there was not enough bread. Raleigh was the first to have potatoes planted on his farms in England and so brought back something worth more than gold.

更重要的是另一種美洲植物：馬鈴薯。在早期，當 England 的小麥收成碰巧不好時，就會出現飢荒和餓殍。如今人們在麵包不足時可以依靠馬鈴薯。Raleigh 是第一個在英國自己的農場上種植馬鈴薯的人，他帶回了比黃金更有價值的東西。

When Queen Elizabeth died, she appointed James VI of Scotland, the son of Mary, Queen of Scots, as her successor to the throne of England and Ireland. James VI had made no move to rescue his mother when she was condemned to death: he did not want to rouse the anger of Elizabeth and so lose his chance to become king of England and Ireland. At Elizabeth's death he then became king of Scotland, England and Ireland. For the first time in history the three countries were united and remained so.

Elizabeth 女王去世時，她指定 Scotland 的 James 六世——蘇格蘭女王 Mary 的兒子——為 England 和 Ireland 王位的繼承人。James 六世在母親被判處死刑時並未採取任何行動去營救她：他不想激怒 Elizabeth，以免失去成為英格蘭和愛爾蘭國王的機會。Elizabeth 去世後，他便成為 Scotland、England 和 Ireland 三國的國王。歷史上三國第一次聯合在一起，此後一直如此。

Under King James, Sir Walter Raleigh could at last follow his thirst for adventure. As there was no gold in North America, Sir Walter Raleigh went to South America in search of a fabulous land called Eldorado where, so people said, even houses were made of solid gold. Raleigh and his men went through terrible hardships and dangers in the jungle, but never found Eldorado. When Raleigh returned to England, the Spaniards complained that he had attacked Spanish colonists and broken the peace between Spain and England. King James, who wanted peace with Spain, had Raleigh arrested and imprisoned. While Raleigh was in prison he wrote a book, a history of the world from the beginning to his own time. He was a very learned man as well as a wise statesman and fearless explorer. But King James had no liking for the man who had been the favourite of Elizabeth and, in the end, Raleigh was condemned to death and beheaded for having attacked Spaniards.

在 James 國王治下，Sir Walter Raleigh 終於可以追隨他對冒險的渴望了。由於北美洲沒有黃金，Sir Walter Raleigh 前往南美洲尋找一個傳說中的國度，名叫 Eldorado——據說那裡連房子都是用純金蓋的。Raleigh 和他的手下在叢林中經歷了可怕的艱辛和危險，但始終沒有找到 Eldorado。當 Raleigh 回到 England 時，西班牙人投訴他攻擊了西班牙殖民者，破壞了 Spain 和 England 之間的和平。想要與 Spain 和平共處的 James 國王將 Raleigh 逮捕入獄。Raleigh 在獄中寫了一本書，一部從開天闢地到他自己時代的世界史。他既是一位非常博學的人，也是一位睿智的政治家和無畏的探險家。但 James 國王不喜歡這個曾是 Elizabeth 寵臣的人，最終 Raleigh 以攻擊西班牙人的罪名被判處死刑，斬首而亡。

# 34. Francis Drake
# 34. Francis Drake

The Age of Discovery, the Renaissance, the Reformation, are all names for the same period of time. When Columbus travelled to America in 1492, Leonardo da Vinci was in his forties and Martin Luther was a boy of nine: they were all children of the same new age, and in different ways they showed the same adventurous spirit. Copernicus, who surprised the world by saying that the earth moves around the sun, was twenty years old when Columbus discovered America.

大發現時代、文藝復興、宗教改革，這些都是同一個時期的不同名稱。當 Columbus 在 1492 年航向美洲時，Leonardo da Vinci 四十多歲，Martin Luther 還是個九歲的男孩：他們都是同一個新時代的孩子，以不同的方式展現著同樣的冒險精神。Copernicus 提出地球繞著太陽轉這個驚世之說時，Columbus 發現美洲那年他才二十歲。

An imaginary person who lived from 1500 to 1600 could have met all the famous people of that one century: Magellan and Pizarro, Calvin in Geneva, John Knox in Scotland and Savonarola in Florence, Michelangelo in Rome and William Shakespeare in London. They could have seen the Great Armada as well as Sir Walter Raleigh's first English colonists sailing to Virginia in America. This imaginary person would have met bold and adventurous spirits in all these people - for that was what they all had in common.

一個假想的人如果生活在 1500 年到 1600 年之間，他可能遇見那一個世紀裡所有的名人：Magellan 和 Pizarro，Geneva 的 Calvin，Scotland 的 John Knox，Florence 的 Savonarola，Rome 的 Michelangelo，London 的 William Shakespeare。他可能親眼見證無敵艦隊的到來，也見證 Sir Walter Raleigh 的第一批英國殖民者啟航前往美洲的 Virginia。這個假想的人會在所有這些人身上看到大膽無畏的冒險精神——因為那正是他們所有人的共同之處。

One of the English sea captains, in his own rough and tough way, had the same spirit of boldness and adventure that belongs to that time. Francis Drake was, at first, simply a merchant sailor, a sea captain who used his ships for trade. Nowadays we know that his trade was despicable, but in those days it was regarded by Europeans as ordinary business. He sailed his ships to Africa, where he and his men kidnapped African people and then shipped them to the Spanish colonies in America. The Spanish colonists paid well for these people, who they forced to work for them as slaves, and Drake was quite content in selling slaves to the Spaniards. This was many years before the Armada.

一位英國海船船長，以他自己粗獷強悍的方式，擁有那個時代同樣的大膽和冒險精神。Francis Drake 起初只是一個商船水手，一個用船隻從事貿易的船長。今天我們知道他的買賣是卑劣的，但在當時歐洲人視之為普通的生意。他把船開到非洲，和他的手下一起綁架非洲人，然後把他們運到美洲的西班牙殖民地。西班牙殖民者為這些人付了高價，強迫他們做奴隸，而 Drake 對向西班牙人販賣奴隸相當滿意。這是無敵艦隊事件之前許多年的事。

One day, with five ships under his command, Drake had sold a cargo of Africans to Spanish colonists, and had bought all kinds of goods in America that he expected to sell profitably in England. He was a skilled businessman. But on the way back, Drake's ships ran into a storm and took shelter in an island off the South American coast. This island was also a Spanish colony. The Spaniards seemed quite friendly and Drake had no reason to fear any harm from them. But when the gale was over and Drake's ships were about to sail away, the Spanish opened fire and three of Drake's ships were sunk with all men aboard. Drake escaped with two of his ships, but he swore he would make the Spaniards pay for their treachery.

有一天，Drake 率領五艘船，把一批非洲人賣給了西班牙殖民者，又在美洲購買了各種貨物，指望回 England 能賣個好價錢。他是個精明的生意人。但在回程途中，Drake 的船遇上風暴，在南美洲海岸外的一個島上避風。這個島也是西班牙殖民地。西班牙人看起來相當友善，Drake 沒有理由擔心他們會加害。但當暴風結束、Drake 的船正要離開時，西班牙人開了火，Drake 的三艘船連同船上所有人全部沉沒。Drake 帶著兩艘船逃了出來，但他發誓要讓西班牙人為他們的背叛付出代價。

At the time, England was at peace with Spain, and Queen Elizabeth was not at all anxious to start a war with Spain for the sake of three ships, so Drake began a one-man war of his own.

當時 England 和 Spain 處於和平狀態，Elizabeth 女王完全不想為了三艘船就和 Spain 開戰，所以 Drake 開始了他一個人的戰爭。

Drake prepared himself well for this war. For a whole year he sailed up and down the coast of America on which the Spanish colonies were until he knew every little bay and island. This American coastline, with its rich, great ports, was called the Spanish Main. He also made friends with runaway slaves. There were a few thousand people who had run away from their cruel Spanish masters and who lived in the jungle along the South American coast where the Spaniards could never catch them. These desperate gangs became staunch allies of Francis Drake.

Drake 為這場戰爭做了充分的準備。整整一年，他沿著西班牙殖民地所在的美洲海岸來回航行，直到摸清了每一個小海灣和島嶼。這條擁有富裕大港的美洲海岸線被稱為 Spanish Main（西班牙大陸）。他也和逃跑的奴隸們交了朋友。有幾千人從殘暴的西班牙主人那裡逃了出來，住在南美洲海岸的叢林中，西班牙人永遠抓不到他們。這些走投無路的人成為了 Francis Drake 最堅定的盟友。

Then he was ready to begin his own private war. His new allies had told him that there was a regular train of five hundred mules carrying silver from the mines of Peru to a sea port near Panama. From there ships carried the silver to Spain. Drake decided to take the silver before it got to the port.

於是他準備好開始自己的私人戰爭了。他的新盟友告訴他，有一支固定的五百頭騾子隊伍，把白銀從 Peru 的礦山運往 Panama 附近的一個海港，再由船隻把白銀運回 Spain。Drake 決定在白銀到達港口之前截獲它。

He had two ships, which he left on a wild stretch of coast. Then he set out with fifty men into the jungle to ambush the silver-laden mules. Now Drake had been told that every twenty mules had one leading mule, and if this leading mule would lie down the other twenty would do the same. They had been trained to do so. When the mule-train came, the Spanish escorts were met with a hail of bullets and they ran for their lives without first counting the attackers. As soon as the Spanish soldiers were gone, Drake and his men made the leading mule lie down and all the others did the same. Drake and his men now took the silver off the mules. They buried one part in the forest and returned a few months later to get it. But they took as much as they could carry to the ships and sailed away.

他有兩艘船，停在一段荒涼的海岸邊。然後他帶著五十個人深入叢林，埋伏攔截滿載白銀的騾隊。Drake 事先被告知，每二十頭騾子有一頭領頭騾，如果這頭領頭騾趴下，其他二十頭也會照做。牠們被訓練成這樣。當騾隊來到時，西班牙護衛遭到了一陣彈雨，他們來不及清點攻擊者的人數就拔腿逃命了。西班牙士兵一離開，Drake 和他的手下就讓領頭騾趴下，其他騾子也全都跟著趴下了。Drake 和手下隨即把白銀從騾子身上卸下來。他們把一部分埋在森林裡，幾個月後再回來取。但他們帶著盡可能多的白銀回到船上，揚帆而去。

After this first blow, Drake gave the Spaniards no peace. Up and down the Spanish Main he sailed. He stopped any Spanish ship, and his men went aboard and took away any valuable cargo before the Spanish ship could sail on. Drake's ships were soon loaded with plunder. When he had looted two hundred Spanish ships he returned to England where he was welcomed as a hero.

在這第一次打擊之後，Drake 再也不讓西班牙人安寧了。他在 Spanish Main 上來回巡航。他攔截任何西班牙船隻，手下登船取走所有值錢的貨物，然後才放西班牙船繼續航行。Drake 的船很快就裝滿了掠奪物。當他洗劫了兩百艘西班牙船之後，他回到了 England，在那裡被當作英雄來歡迎。

The next time Drake set out, it was with the help and approval of Queen Elizabeth. That voyage became famous as the voyage of the Golden Hind. It was the first English voyage around the world.

Drake 下一次出航，得到了 Elizabeth 女王的幫助和批准。那次航行以「Golden Hind 號之旅」而聞名。那是英國人第一次環球航行。

At first, Drake had no intention of sailing around the world. He had already plundered the Spanish colonies on the east coast of America and now he wanted to attack the fabulously rich colonies on the west coast. To do this, Drake had to sail through the Strait of Magellan.

起初，Drake 並沒有打算環遊世界。他已經搶劫了美洲東海岸的西班牙殖民地，現在他想進攻西海岸那些極其富裕的殖民地。為此，Drake 必須穿過 Magellan 海峽。

Drake set out with three ships, but two were lost in a storm and only one ship, his Golden Hind, made the voyage. The Golden Hind sailed through the Strait of Magellan and appeared on the west coast where nobody expected to see an English ship.

Drake 帶著三艘船出發，但有兩艘在風暴中失去了，只有一艘船——他的 Golden Hind 號——完成了航程。Golden Hind 號穿過 Magellan 海峽，出現在西海岸——在那裡沒有人預料會看到一艘英國船。

So Drake and his men simply sailed into the harbour in the city of Valparaiso, shot up the Spanish ships lying at anchor, and then seized the whole city and took what they wanted. They sailed away and, on the way out, captured a Spanish galleon carrying a fortune in gold and jewels.

於是 Drake 和他的手下直接駛入了 Valparaiso 城的港口，擊沉了停泊在那裡的西班牙船隻，然後占領了整座城市，拿走了他們想要的一切。他們離去時，又在途中俘獲了一艘載滿黃金和珠寶的西班牙大帆船。

By now the enraged Spaniards had got a whole fleet together and were waiting at the Strait of Magellan to catch Drake on his way back. But Drake got to know about it and decided he need not go back through the Strait of Magellan: the world was round and he could go back round the world as Magellan's ship had done.

此時被激怒的西班牙人已經集結了整支艦隊，守在 Magellan 海峽等著在 Drake 回程時抓住他。但 Drake 得知了這件事，決定不必再經 Magellan 海峽回去：地球是圓的，他可以像 Magellan 的船那樣環繞世界回去。

So, like Magellan, he sailed across the Pacific Ocean, past India, around Africa and reached England after three years absence, and with the greatest treasure ever gained by a single ship. Most of that went to Queen Elizabeth, but he was knighted by her and became Sir Francis Drake. The Golden Hind is one of the famous ships of history, like the Santa Maria.

於是，如同 Magellan 一樣，他橫渡太平洋，經過 India，繞過 Africa，在離開三年之後回到了 England，帶回了一艘船有史以來獲得的最大財寶。大部分財寶歸了 Elizabeth 女王，但她冊封他為騎士，他成為了 Sir Francis Drake。Golden Hind 號是歷史上最著名的船隻之一，如同 Santa Maria 號一樣。

The next time Drake sailed out, he performed the boldest stroke of his life. The capital of the Spanish colonies was Cartagena, an immensely rich city with strong fortifications and great guns pointing towards the sea. Drake let his ships feign an attack from the sea, but in the night he led a thousand men through swamps to the rear of Cartagena. The defenders were completely taken by surprise, and in a few hours, Drake was master of the city. The citizens of Cartagena had to pay him an enormous ransom before he left and sailed back to England.

Drake 下一次出海時，完成了他一生中最大膽的一擊。西班牙殖民地的首府是 Cartagena，一座極其富裕的城市，防禦工事堅固，巨炮對準大海。Drake 讓他的船隻佯裝從海上進攻，但在夜裡他率領一千人穿過沼澤來到 Cartagena 的後方。守軍完全措手不及，幾個小時之內，Drake 就成了這座城市的主人。Cartagena 的市民不得不付給他一筆巨額贖金，他才離去、駛回 England。

Although no enemy ever got the better of Sir Francis Drake, he died of malaria while sailing on another venture against the Spanish Main. He was one of the most renowned seafarers in history.

儘管沒有任何敵人能打敗 Sir Francis Drake，他最終在又一次遠征 Spanish Main 的航行中死於瘧疾。他是歷史上最負盛名的航海家之一。
